# Chapter 2: Domains of Ravenloft
*Source: Ravenloft: The Horrors Within* 

![By the light of the full moon, villagers in Kartakass undergo a terrifying transformation](file://book/RHW/028-02-001.kartakass-transformation.webp#center)

At the unfathomable edge of the Shadowfell lie the Domains of Dread, realms bound by Mists where magic and reality twist into nightmare. This chapter for DMs explores the most terrifying of the Domains of Dread. Among other tools, each featured domain includes the following details:

- **Domain.** This initial section introduces the domain, its unique horrors, and notable locations.  
- **Darklord.** The domain's Darklord, their stat block, effects they create within their domain, how they close their domain's borders (see the introduction), and details of their lair appear here.  
- **Adventures.** This section provides guidance on creating adventures in the domain, a campaign outline, and short adventures.  

This chapter concludes with an overview of "additional domains".

## Tarokka and the Mists

Tarokka fortune-telling cards (detailed in the "appendix") have special relationships with domains and their Darklords.

### Tarokka Mist Talismans

Each Domain of Dread is aligned with a tarokka card. A character with a tarokka deck can use it to travel between domains. While in the Mists, the deck's bearer can draw a random card from the deck; that card serves as a Mist talisman (see the introduction), allowing travel to the domain it is aligned with. A tarokka deck can be used in this way once every 24 hours. A list of domains and their aligned tarokka cards appears later in "this book".

### Darklords and the Tarokka

Every Domain of Dread has a tarokka card that opposes it—one hinting at the truth of the domain's Darklord. If a domain's opposed tarokka card is drawn during a tarokka reading in that domain, that domain's Darklord becomes aware of the reading and its participants. When this occurs, the Darklord can choose to see through the eyes of the tarokka user and speak through them for 1 minute. The Darklord might make their presence known, level a threat, or misinterpret the cards. A tarokka reader has no memory of what a Darklord uses them to say.

## Domains of Ravenloft Guide

The table below lists the Dread Domains and the respective Darklord that resides there.

**Domains & Darklords**

| Domain (Alphabetical) | Darklord |
|-----------------------|----------|
| "Barovia" | "Strahd von Zarovich" |
| "Borca" | Ivana Boritsi and Ivan Dilisnya |
| "Darkon" | None (formerly Azalin Rex) |
| "Dementlieu" | Saidra d'Honaire |
| "Falkovnia" | Vladeska Drakov |
| "Har'Akir" | Ankhtepot |
| "Hazlan" | Hazlik |
| "Innsmouth" | Cthulhu |
| "Kalakeri" | Ramya Vasavadan |
| "Kartakass" | Harkon Lukas |
| "Lamordia" | Viktra Mordenheim |
| "Mordent" | Wilfred Godefroy |
| "Shadowlands" | Ebonbane |
| "Sithicus" | "Lord Soth" |
| "Tepest" | Mother Lorinda |
| "Valachan" | Chakuna |
^domains-darklords

## Barovia

*Domain of the First Vampire*

> [!note] 
> 
> - **Darklord.** Strahd von Zarovich  
> - **Genre.** Gothic horror  
> - **Hallmarks.** Undead despot, notorious haunted stronghold, tragic resurrection  
> - **Mist Talismans.** Barovian wine bottle, von Zarovich crest, Mark of the Raven talisman  
> - **Aligned Tarokka Card.** Darklord  
> - **Opposed Tarokka Card.** Mists  
^0d1

> [!gallery]
> ![](file://book/RHW/029-03-001.darklord-tarokka.webp#gallery)
> ![](file://book/RHW/030-03-002.mists-tarokka.webp#gallery)

In Barovia, the night is a curse. As darkness falls, wicked souls slip from the spires of Castle Ravenloft to work the will of an immortal overlord. This is the realm of the vampire [Count Strahd von Zarovich](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/strahd-von-zarovich-rhw.md), whose depravities have doomed him and his land to endless cycles of obsession and despair.

The howls of wolves and shrieks of ravens echo through the dismal valleys and oppressive forests of Barovia. In isolated communities, superstitious villagers find the brightness in their lives smothered by dread of their aloof overlord and other festering evils. These Barovians fear the night, as agents of the devil Strahd watch in the dark and claim whatever he desires. Yet few in Barovia realize their torments have played out again and again. In every generation, echoes of Strahd's past reemerge, compelling and confounding the Darklord as he endlessly obsesses over the one victim who's eluded him for centuries.

### Domain Features

Barovia is known for the following features:

- **The Devil Strahd.** Few have seen Count von Zarovich, but all know he dwells in Castle Ravenloft, a citadel from which few visitors return. Strahd is infamous for viciously executing any who flagrantly break his laws, but otherwise he rarely interferes in the lives of his people. Some whisper that he is a vampire.  
- **Haunted Tales.** The stories of Barovia's people are full of hidden evils: accursed ruins, portentous ravens, secretive cults, treacherous witches, vicious werewolves, and worse.  
- **Isolation and Suspicion.** Barovia is a realm of wolf-prowled forests and treacherous mountains where the sun is obscured. The land's superstitious people live in scattered villages. They distrust strangers, fearing they're agents of the count.  

### Locations in Barovia

Barovia is a land of long shadows where ancient wildernesses strangle the ruins of a near-forgotten empire. Mysteries pervade the domain, and those who leave the relative safety of Barovia's dismal settlements enter perilous lands where mortals aren't welcome.

The village of Barovia is described below, and other notable locations are summarized on the "Barovia Locations table".

#### Village of Barovia

Lying in the shadow of Castle Ravenloft, the village of Barovia teeters on the brink of ruin. Its few residents rarely venture from their homes, suspecting their neighbors of wickedness and fearing evils in the night. Their dread is largely justified, as wolves, ghosts, and vampire spawn haunt the town, and many locals have been consumed by callousness or wicked temptations.

A rare exception to the village's cold desperation can be found at the local tavern, the Blood of the Vine. Those few who oppose Strahd's evil congregate here—under the covert oversight of the count's agents.

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.1: Barovia](file://book/RHW/031-map-03-01.barovia.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/032-map-03-01.barovia-player.webp#gallery)

![Barovia Locations](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/barovia-locations-rhw.md)

### Strahd von Zarovich

*First of the Darklords*

![](file://book/RHW/033-03-003.strahd-von-zarovich.webp#center)

> [!quote] A quote from Strahd von Zarovich  
> 
> I am the Ancient. I am the Land. My beginnings are lost in the darkness of the past. I am not dead. Nor am I alive. I am undead, forever.

Count Strahd von Zarovich has lost all he ever desired—over and over again. Tormented by the Dark Powers, Strahd is haunted by visions of his lost family and tarnished nobility. The count spends long years brooding in the depths of Castle Ravenloft, but a reincarnation of his obsession appears every generation: Tatyana. Each time Tatyana's reincarnation emerges, Strahd seeks to undo the failures of his past and find a way to win her love. Time and time again, Strahd's heartless, domineering nature causes his bloody history to repeat itself and drives Tatyana beyond his clutches.

A severe, aristocratic figure, the count has the bearing of a former soldier and the impatience of one used to being obeyed. He feels little but occasionally embraces the novelty of toying with amusing strangers or breaking the spirits of his enemies. During his unnaturally long existence, he has learned many occult secrets and mysteries of the Domains of Dread. Strahd's dignified bearing crumbles when someone breaks his laws or denies him what he desires. In such cases, Strahd makes bloody examples of his opponents, drawing out his vengeance into campaigns of terror.

> [!embed-monster]- Strahd von Zarovich
> ![Strahd von Zarovich](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/strahd-von-zarovich-rhw.md#^statblock)

#### Strahd's Tale

Count Strahd von Zarovich was a ruthless conqueror. Retiring after years of war, Strahd settled in the beautiful valley where he'd won his greatest victory. There, in the way of his ancestors, he spilled his blood into the earth, sealing a pact between himself and the land. In honor of his parents, King Barov and Queen Ravenovia, he named the valley Barovia and constructed his home, Castle Ravenloft.

Strahd invited his few remaining family members to live with him at Castle Ravenloft and eventually was joined by his younger brother, Sergei. Sergei was everything Strahd wasn't—youthful, empathic, and warm. Soon after he arrived, the younger von Zarovich and a local villager named Tatyana fell in love. Strahd resented his brother, even more so after meeting Tatyana and being charmed by her pure kindness. Obsessed, Strahd sought to woo her but was rebuffed. Unwilling to accept her wishes or the idea of Sergei as his better, Strahd made a pact with ancient evil forces to regain his vitality and ensnare Tatyana's heart.

The day of Sergei and Tatyana's wedding, Strahd murdered Sergei and, to seal his pact, drank his brother's blood. He revealed his new might to Tatyana, expecting to enthrall her. Instead, horrified by Sergei's murder, Tatyana fled Strahd, ultimately leaping from the height of Castle Ravenloft and vanishing into the Mists. At the same time, traitors from among the castle's guards and wedding's guests rose up to assassinate Strahd. Despite countless wounds, Strahd didn't die. His bargain with the Dark Powers had made Strahd the multiverse's first vampire. A night of slaughter followed; when dawn touched the parapets of Castle Ravenloft, no living soul survived within. But Strahd remained.

Strahd's villainy and his connection to his land drew all of Barovia into the grip of the Dark Powers, which transplanted the vampire and his realm into the Shadowfell. This began a succession of torments that plague the count still. The Dark Powers' attentions have spilled forth to drag others into the Mists as well, giving rise to the Domains of Dread.

#### Strahd's Domain

Barovia is altered by Strahd's presence, creating the following effects:

- **Closing the Borders.** While in his domain, Strahd can close or open the borders to Barovia at will. While the borders are closed, noxious fog suffuses the Mists surrounding Barovia. A creature that enters the Mists for the first time on a turn or starts its turn there must succeed on a DC 20 Constitution saving throw or gain 1 [Exhaustion](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/conditions.md#Exhaustion) level. A creature makes this save only once per turn.  
- **Dreadful Darkness.** While in an area of [Darkness](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/darkness-xphb.md), creatures other than Strahd and creatures of his choice have [Disadvantage](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/disadvantage-xphb.md) on saving throws to end or avoid the [Frightened](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/conditions.md#Frightened) condition.  
- **Jealous Heart.** When a character receives [Heroic Inspiration](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/heroic-inspiration-xphb.md) but already has it, that character can't give it to another character in the group.  

If Strahd dies, these effects end immediately.

#### Strahd's Lairs

While the notorious Castle Ravenloft is Strahd's home, it isn't his only redoubt in Barovia. Multiple bastions of evil serve as sanctuaries for the count and his servants, should fate demand.

![Nightly the village of Vallaki bars its gates against attacks from wolves and deadlier predators](file://book/RHW/034-03-004.village-of-vallaki.webp#center)

##### Castle Ravenloft

Castle Ravenloft is Strahd von Zarovich's accursed sanctuary. Tormented spirits and Strahd's minions haunt the vast castle, each serving the count's schemes, reflecting some aspect of his depraved past, or protecting his coffin in the castle catacombs. Mementos of lost times and fallen heroes lie throughout the count's home, some of which might hold the key to his undoing. The adventure Curse of Strahd details Castle Ravenloft.

##### Von Zarovich Sanctuaries

Hidden across Barovia lie secret sanctuaries known only to Strahd and his servants. These crypt-like boltholes are hidden from the sun and exist primarily to shelter the count should he require. Over the centuries, Strahd has granted trusted servants access to some of these sanctuaries and used others in plots or experiments that he keeps distant from Castle Ravenloft. Still others Strahd has forgotten, allowing other evils to fester there. An example of one of these sites is depicted on "map 2.2" and has the following features:

- **Count's Coffin.** Hidden in each sanctuary lies a coffin bearing the von Zarovich crest. This might be obvious or in a space only accessible to vampires.  
- **The Lord's Presence.** Behind a vault-like iron door, an entry chamber holds a high-backed throne. Strahd forbids servants from using these symbols of his authority.  
- **Servants' Space.** Alcoves carved in the walls provide space for the coffins or bunks of Strahd's living or dead servants. Sometimes, the Darklord uses these spaces for arcane experiments or as makeshift prisons.  

### Adventures in Barovia

Adventures set in Barovia involve oppressive, gothic menace; suspicion; and the legendary threat of Strahd von Zarovich. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

![Castle Ravenloft, the accursed home of Count Strahd von Zarovich, casts its shadows across the village of Barovia and far beyond](file://book/RHW/035-03-005.castel-ravenloft.png.webp#center)

#### Horror in Barovia

Adventures in Barovia often include the following elements.

##### The Ancient, The Land

Strahd remains bound to Barovia and it to him in a way few rulers or Darklords understand. He knows when any creature enters or dies violently within Barovia, and he takes offense when someone slays his servants or the domain's wolves. Strahd can manifest a variety of dramatic effects, such as casting his voice on the wind, making his visage appear in the clouds, or changing the weather. These effects don't aid him in combat, but they contribute to making him feel like an oppressive and ever-present threat.

##### Incarnations of the Past

The subject of Strahd's obsession, Tatyana, perpetually reincarnates among the people of Barovia. No matter what form she takes, the Darklord unceasingly seeks her, determined to possess her and make her part of an idealized fantasy of his past. Tatyana's incarnation might be anyone, including a player character. If her incarnation is an NPC, roll on the Tatyana's Reincarnation and Connection to Strahd tables to inspire a new chapter in the count's tale of obsession.

**Tatyana's Reincarnation**

`dice: [](3-chapter-2-domains-of-ravenloft.md#^tatyanas-reincarnation)`

| dice: 1d10 | Tatyana's Reincarnation Is... |
|------------|-------------------------------|
| 1 | Anna, the keeper of what another Darklord desires—such as Ankhtepot's ka or Mordenheim's Unbreakable Heart (both detailed later in this book). |
| 2 | [Ez d'Avenir](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ez-davenir-rhw.md) (see chapter 5), a monster hunter. |
| 3 | Ireena Kolyana, adopted daughter of Burgomaster Indirovich of the village of Barovia. |
| 4 | Lyssa von Zarovich, a distant relative of Strahd's, who has become a vampire. |
| 5 | Nasseri and Yasmine, identical twins who serve the god Ezra. |
| 6 | Petra Rilenovich, an artist who paints images of what she calls "dream lives." |
| 7 | Quentin L'Argent, the dragonborn son of herders living near Argynvostholt. |
| 8 | Renoir Laurent, the son of Chantal Laurent, a woman Strahd abducted years ago. |
| 9 | Vanasia, a member of a far-ranging Vistani band or other group of mist wanderers. |
| 10 | Vasilka, a [Flesh Golem](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/construct/flesh-golem-xmm.md) or [reborn](3-Mechanics/CLI/races/reborn-rhw.md) who lives in the abbey of Krezk. |
^tatyanas-reincarnation

**Connection to Strahd**

`dice: [](3-chapter-2-domains-of-ravenloft.md#^connection-to-strahd)`

| dice: 1d10 | Tatyana's Reincarnation... |
|------------|----------------------------|
| 1 | Has weaponized their blood with poison that will put Strahd to sleep for a generation. |
| 2 | Is hidden from Strahd by another Darklord or some more mysterious evil. |
| 3 | Becomes trapped by a deceitful servant of Strahd, either bodily or by an effect such as a [Magic Jar](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/magic-jar-xphb.md) spell. |
| 4 | Knows of their reincarnations and seeks to end them by freeing Barovia from the Mists. |
| 5 | Lives a charmed life, unknowingly protected and cultivated by the count. |
| 6 | Misguidedly plans to redeem Strahd through their exceptional kindness or faith. |
| 7 | Uses magic to hide from Strahd by appearing elderly, childlike, or as a mysterious animal. |
| 8 | Searches for a relic that can weaken Strahd. |
| 9 | Seeks to join a group of adventurers and organize a siege of Castle Ravenloft. |
| 10 | Wants to resurrect past incarnations of Tatyana to battle Strahd. |
^connection-to-strahd

##### Roots of Evil

As the first Domain of Dread, Barovia might serve an important role in the metaphysical underpinnings of the setting. Some Darklords might have emerged from the Mists first in Barovia, encountered Strahd, and found their ways to their own domains later. Others might have a particular interest in Barovia and in undoing Strahd's connection to his land. Consider these possibilities when developing plots involving conflicts between Darklords or escaping the Mists, as outlined in "chapter 3".

##### Signs of the Count

Servants of Strahd are everywhere in Barovia. While in the domain, characters experience regular reminders that the Darklord watches them—and that they are unwelcome. Roll on the Strahd's Presence table to inspire such encounters.

**Strahd's Presence**

`dice: [](3-chapter-2-domains-of-ravenloft.md#^strahds-presence)`

| dice: 1d8 | Strahd's Presence Is Suggested... |
|-----------|-----------------------------------|
| 1 | As clouds momentarily resemble clawed hands, gaping skulls, or Castle Ravenloft. |
| 2 | As wolves or ravens soundlessly follow the characters and mirror their actions. |
| 3 | By faded carvings or tapestries bearing the von Zarovich crest. |
| 4 | During a tarokka reading, when the Darklord card changes to resemble Strahd. |
| 5 | In a dream where a character becomes charmed or threatened by Strahd. |
| 6 | In a rustic shrine littered with vials of dried blood, snapped splinters, and wolf fangs. |
| 7 | When characters awake to find swarms of roosting bats or bloodless animal corpses. |
| 8 | When spying villagers try to eavesdrop on or steal small things from the characters. |
^strahds-presence

#### Barovia Campaign Arc

Campaigns set in Barovia involve communities oppressed by fear of Strahd and his cycles of obsession. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–5.** The characters emerge from the Mists and seek shelter from danger in the village of Barovia, Krezk, or Vallaki. There they learn the people fear Count von Zarovich, and the characters might meet a "reincarnation of Tatyana". They help strike back against agents of the count, such as deadly [Wolves](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/beast/wolf-xmm.md) or [Zombies](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/zombie-xmm.md).  
- **Levels 6–8.** The characters learn more of the count's history and about magical relics that might help oppose him. They seek these in haunted corners of the domain, facing servants of Strahd and remnants of his past, including [Ghosts](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/ghost-xmm.md), [Werewolves](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/werewolf-xmm.md), and deadly [Druids](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/druid-xmm.md).  
- **Levels 9–10.** Armed with knowledge and magical weapons, the characters lay siege to Castle Ravenloft, facing [Strahd's](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/strahd-von-zarovich-rhw.md) most terrifying servants and the count himself.  

#### Blood o' the Vine

*Adventure for Level 6 Characters*

- **Situation.** A discovery beneath the Blood of the Vine tavern in the village of Barovia has unleashed sinister magic, transforming the owners.  
- **Hook.** Disguised as a human, Urwin Martikov (Medium [Wereraven](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/wereraven-rhw.md); see chapter 5) of the Blue Water Inn in Vallaki hires the characters to investigate why the Blood of the Vine tavern in the village of Barovia has closed, claiming he was in negotiations with the owners to buy it. Urwin offers to pay each character 500 GP.  

![The Blood of the Vine tavern is one of the few places in the village of Barovia that welcomes strangers](file://book/RHW/036-03-006.blood-of-the-vine-tavern.webp#center)

##### Encounters

This adventure uses "map 2.2: Blood of the Vine Tavern" and consists of these encounters.

###### Corrupted Owners

The three human sisters who owned the Blood of the Vine tavern—Alenka, Mirabel, and Sorvina—have been transformed into the following ravenous embodiments of primal hunger:

**Alenka** ([Relentless Slasher](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fiend/relentless-slasher-rhw.md)) wields kitchenware and prowls the first floor.

**Mirabel** (Medium [Ghast Gravecaller](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/ghast-gravecaller-xmm.md)) stalks the second floor with her two [Ghoul](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/ghoul-xmm.md) servants.

**Sorvina** ([Unspeakable Horror](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/unspeakable-horror-rhw.md); see chapter 5) conducts strange rituals in the basement.

###### Taproom

Dust covers the taproom. Here, the animate corpse of Arik the barkeep mindlessly cleans pieces of shattered glassware at the bar. If attacked or otherwise interrupted, Arik falls to pieces.

###### Office

The office in the northeast corner of the first floor is cluttered with junk and unfinished notes to the count describing the activities of the tavern's patrons. This suggests the owners spied on the locals. If the characters have visited the tavern before, their activities are detailed. A trapdoor descends to an area beneath the tavern.

###### Private Dining Room

The dining room in the southeast corner of the second floor is strewn with broken dishes, rotten food, and pages from a destroyed book. The pages are from the journal of Mirabel, one of the inn's owners. Surviving entries note the following information:

- **First Entry.** Mirabel's sister Sorvina discovered a hollow hidden under the tavern. Strange ruins lie amid the dirt walls. Sorvina wants to excavate them, hoping to find a tomb filed with treasures.  
- **Second Entry.** Sorvina's digging revealed strange standing stones. Mirabel worries about her sister, who's started whispering to herself as she obsesses over learning more about the stones.  
- **Third Entry.** Sorvina discovered the bones of some monster at the center of the standing stones. All three sisters are having nightmares from which they wake up ravenous. Sorvina claims the hunger is a blessing. Food has lost its taste, but the inn's patrons suddenly smell delicious.  

###### Temple of Ravenkind

A circle of ancient menhirs carved with stylized ravens and sunbursts is partially unearthed beneath the tavern. The creature that was once Sorvina is here, chanting over a monstrous skeleton of black bones with stag horns and tusks. When she notices intruders, Sorvina howls, causing the bones to rise as a [Minotaur Skeleton](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/minotaur-skeleton-xmm.md). Both it and Sorvina fight the characters to the death. When the skeleton is defeated, its bones remain intact.

###### Cursed Remains

The skeleton exudes evil magic. Casting [Remove Curse](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/remove-curse-xphb.md) on the monster destroys the skeleton. However, if a character touches the skeleton (while it's animate or otherwise), its spirit whispers to the character, bidding them to end its ancient curse. Doing so destroys the skeleton and grants the character the [Second Skin](3-Mechanics/CLI/feats/second-skin-rhw.md) Dark Gift. A character who already has a Dark Gift can't accept the curse.

###### Returning to Urwin

If the characters defeat the monsters in the tavern and return to Urwin, he pays them and shares that a benevolent relic, the [Holy Symbol of Ravenkind](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/holy-symbol-of-ravenkind-cos.md), was created at a site like the one hidden under the tavern. The circle was used later to imprison a vicious spirit of the Svalich Woods. If the characters destroyed the skeleton, Urwin rewards them with two random [Quaal's Feather Tokens](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/quaals-feather-token-xdmg.md). Each character also receives a bonus 1,400 XP.

> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/042-map-03-05.outside-the-village-player.webp#gallery)

#### Treacherous Blood

*Adventure for Level 9 Characters*

- **Situation.** Lyssa von Zarovich (Medium, Chaotic Evil [Vampire Nightbringer](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/vampire-nightbringer-xmm.md)), a distant relative of Strahd, plots to undermine the count by unleashing her monstrous servants on Barovia.  
- **Hook.** A human resident of Vallaki named Ernst Larnak (Medium, Lawful Evil [Spy](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/spy-xmm.md)) tells the characters that locals have seen figures excavating the churchyard in the ruins of Berez. He offers to pay 2,500 GP if they investigate. He doesn't share that his information comes from the count's servants.  

##### Encounters

This adventure uses "map 2.2: Von Zarovich Sanctuary" and consists of these encounters.

###### Berez Churchyard

A stone slab covering a grave in the churchyard has been shattered, revealing stairs leading down to a von Zarovich sanctuary. There, two [Vampire Spawn](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/vampire-spawn-xmm.md) guardians fight trespassers.

###### Lyssa's Plot

Lyssa greets the characters in the sanctuary's central room. Observing that they don't look like servants of the count, she shares the following information:

- She is a distant relative of Count Strahd von Zarovich. She, too, is a vampire.  
- She seeks to depose Strahd and raise Barovia to its deserved glory.  
- With the aid of allies beyond the Mists, she has created servants immune to many of Strahd's powers. Now she needs to test them.  

Regardless of whether the characters agree to aid Lyssa, she opens a door to the adjacent chamber and unleashes a pair of [Vampire Mind Flayers](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/vampire-mind-flayer-rhw.md). The monsters obey Lyssa's commands and fight the characters. Lyssa fights as well but flees if she takes damage, swearing her revenge.

###### Crypt

The chamber to the north holds the bloodless corpse of a mind flayer and a journal filled with accounts of strange dreams. The journal is a Mist talisman linked to the domain of Bluetspur (see ""Other Domains of Dread"" later in this book).

###### Hidden Chamber

A character who investigates the large room as a [Study](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/actions.md#Study) action and succeeds on a DC 16 Intelligence ([Investigation](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Investigation)) check finds evidence of a bricked-over hidden chamber in the east wall. Characters can physically remove the wall in 1 hour (half that time if they have Mason's Tools).

###### Elder Evil

Strahd buried a foe in a coffin behind the main chamber's east wall. Opening the coffin releases a [Vampire Nosferatu](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/vampire-nosferatu-rhw.md) and a [Swarm of Infesting Insects](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/beast/swarm-of-infesting-insects-rhw.md) (both detailed in "chapter 5") that fight to the death. Also in the coffin is a [Gem of Brightness](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/gem-of-brightness-xdmg.md).

###### Conclusion

If the characters defeat or drive off Lyssa, each character gains a bonus 2,600 XP.

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.2: Von Zarovich Sanctuary](file://book/RHW/043-map-03-04.von-zarovich-sanctuary.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/044-map-03-04.von-zarovich-sanctuary-player.webp#gallery)

## Borca

*Domain of Desire and Deceit*

> [!note] 
> 
> - **Darklords.** Ivana Boritsi and Ivan Dilisnya  
> - **Genres.** Gothic horror and psychological horror  
> - **Hallmarks.** Political intrigue, poison, revenge  
> - **Mist Talismans.** Dram of sweet-smelling poison, flame-singed love letter, tarnished signet ring  
> - **Aligned Tarokka Card.** Beggar  
> - **Opposed Tarokka Card.** Tempter  
^0f4

> [!gallery]
> ![](file://book/RHW/045-04-001.beggar-tarokka.webp#gallery)
> ![](file://book/RHW/046-04-002.tempter-tarokka.webp#gallery)

The noble families of Borca engage in an endless war of conspiracies and lethal betrayals as they pursue influence, thrills, and age-old rivalries. People here value guile and callousness, and none embody those traits better than the domain's two Darklords: the genius poisoner [Ivana Boritsi](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ivana-boritsi-rhw.md) and the childishly cruel stalker [Ivan Dilisnya](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ivan-dilisnya-rhw.md).

Beyond the fashionable holdings of Borca's elite, commoners struggle against crime, poverty, and starvation. In scattered villages and tenement-filled cities, locals view nobles as celebrities, and the commoners' idealized vision of noble life leads them to mimic the aristocrats' callousness and appetite for empty fads. Desperate commoners are tempted into debt and depravity in pursuit of nobles' favor and passing fancies. Those who don't bend to the whims of Borca's elite face humiliation before they're crushed.

### Domain Features

Borca is known for the following features:

- **Two Darklords.** Ivana Boritsi and Ivan Dilisnya are both Darklords of Borca. They control the domain equally—one of countless facts that contributes to their mutual loathing.  
- **Cruel Intentions.** Borca's most influential families are vicious rivals bound by blood, politics, and business. Their rivalries unfold in an endless shadow war of lies, shifting alliances, and assassinations. The nobles value appearances above all else; they favor stylish poisons, clever clockwork devices, and public embarrassment in their plots.  
- **Desperate Sycophants.** Commoners own little, renting homes in crowded cities or rural villages that serve noble interests. Many commoners desperately court the favor of the elite.  
- **Noble Intrigue.** Nobles control all aspects of Borcan society. They squabble over artistic, political, and religious influence to feed their gluttonous egos and fill their idle lives. The Boritsi family holds the greatest influence.  

### Locations in Borca

The impoverished lands of Borca languish in the shadow of opulent noble estates and garish monuments to greed. The exploited land bears the scars of age-old rivalries and the hiding places of noble secrets.

The capital of Levkarest is described below, and other notable locations are summarized on the "Borca Locations table".

#### Levkarest

Borca's capital of Levkarest stands at the pinnacle of culture and ostentatious power. Here, lesser nobles pursue fickle dramas and vogue trends while the populace labors amid workhouses and cultlike fashion houses. Commoners glimpse this world of toxic glamor only from afar or when nobles exploit street-level fads.

At the city's heart rises the People's Parliament, the land's ineffective seat of government. Here, unpopular members of noble families squabble over meaningless legislation. The nation's true rulers conduct business on noble estates, in avant-garde clubs, and in the offices of faceless mercantile ventures.

Near the People's Parliament stands the Great Cathedral. Within, pious commoners and ostentatious aristocrats attend ceremonies sacred to the deity Ezra. Locals say the cathedral was created by nobles who believed they'd earned the ire of some great evil. Centuries later, these families still support the church, transactionally investing in dubious supernatural insurance.

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.3: Borca](file://book/RHW/047-map-04-01.borca.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/048-map-04-01.borca-player.webp#gallery)

![Borca Locations](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/borca-locations-rhw.md)

### Ivana Boritsi

*Darklord of Poisonous Ambition*

![](file://book/RHW/049-04-003.ivana-boritsi.webp#center)

> [!quote] A quote from Ivana Boritsi  
> 
> Your kind can't possibly fathom how much this sort of interruption costs the House of Boritsi. Don't make it worse by being tedious.

Ivana Boritsi tires of playing games no one realizes she's already won. The head of Borca's most influential family, Ivana effortlessly manipulates all aspects of society. Her servants, employees, and fractious cousins prove endlessly unreliable, forcing her to attend personally to tedious duties and social functions to maintain her power.

Ivana looks eternally youthful, causing some to doubt her competence and attribute her success to her elder cousin, [Ivan Dilisnya](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ivan-dilisnya-rhw.md). Perpetually bored with and disappointed by predictable people, she takes refuge in her alchemical studies and her gardens of poisonous plants. Her vast knowledge of toxins makes her a peerless poisoner. She uses her creations to make people more pliable and to assassinate those she deems too boorish to live. Secretly, Ivana seeks someone who can match her intellect and relieve her boredom, but she quickly grows weary of even the most charming and clever souls.

#### Ivana's Tale

The firstborn of a fantastically wealthy family, Ivana Boritsi was clever, poised, and—in the eyes of her father, Klaus—utterly unfit to lead the family. Driven to prove her father wrong and encouraged by her mother, Camille, Ivana learned every aspect of her family's vast perfume and medicine business.

Her focus on her goals faltered when she met Pieter, a skilled chemist in her family's service. Camille recognized her daughter's budding romance and saw the lowborn Pieter as a threat to the girl's prospects. Camille seduced Pieter and arranged for her daughter to discover them, intent on convincing her to forsake this and all future romances.

Ivana took a different lesson from the experience. Realizing the depths of her family's depravity, she poisoned her mother and her callous younger siblings with toxins of her own design. None suspected Ivana, but soon after, Klaus summoned her. Having lost his sons, Klaus named her cousin, Ivan Dilisnya, his heir. Ivana was the last to be informed, her father having already announced his decision to the estate and sent a messenger to inform the Dilisnyas.

Having expected this, Ivana had poisoned the perfumery on the estate's grounds, turning its far-ranging smells deadly. Ivana laughed as toxic mist poured across the estate. As she sipped the antidote, she watched Klaus and the manor's staff die choking amid a violet fog. When the poison cleared, the Mists had surrounded the land of Borca (for details on Ivana's domain and lair, see "Ivan Dilisnya").

> [!embed-monster]- Ivana Boritsi
> ![Ivana Boritsi](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ivana-boritsi-rhw.md#^statblock)

### Ivan Dilisnya

*Darklord of Childish Cruelty*

![](file://book/RHW/050-04-004.ivan-dilisnya.webp#center)

> [!quote] A quote from Ivan Dilisnya  
> 
> Oh ho oh! What succulent insipidity I see in those lumpish eyes! What divine folly! I swoon, I croon, I know! You'll be a new favorite!

Ivan Dilisnya—a spoiled, selfish attention seeker—has the tastes of a child but a withered wreck of a body. Borcan society widely regards this recluse as an innovator and a genius. In truth, he is neither. Ivan is a wicked and off-putting manipulator who, despite his appearance and intellect, affects childlike behaviors and speech patterns for attention. He is alone—despite having been born with everything—and the solitude terrifies him.

By staying out of sight or using deceptive correspondence, Ivan makes his targets doubt reality and overestimate his control. He manipulates people into performing pointless errands for him or spying on his cousin, [Ivana Boritsi](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ivana-boritsi-rhw.md), whom he believes mocks him and has caused his aged, squalid state.

Ivan surrounds himself with dangerous clockwork toys and fawning, mechanical servants. While he goes through the motions of crafting such devices, the Dark Powers provide him with any creation he desires, no matter how bizarre.

#### Ivan's Tale

Treachery is tradition for the Dilisnya family. The land of Borca originates from the same world as Barovia's conquerors, the von Zaroviches. Dilisnyas were at Castle Ravenloft the night of Strahd von Zarovich's transformation.

Ages later, the siblings Boris and Camille Dilisnya plotted to steal the prestige of their cousins, the Boritsis. Camille manipulated her way into the Boritsi family, while Boris prepared his son, Ivan, to act as head of a united Boritsi–Dilisnya house.

Despite abundant opportunities, Ivan resented his family's plans for him and grew to embody puerile vice and impulses. His family's wealth and doting servants exacerbated this problem, even as Ivan fixated on childish toys and behaviors. Frequent "accidents" transpired around him, forcing his family to cover up the maimings and deaths of numerous pets and servants. Only his beloved sister, Kristina, remained immune to his wicked tricks. Although Ivan's family grew unsettled by Ivan, they sheltered the future head of their house, reshaping their estate and investing in whimsical diversions for him.

On the same night Ivana Boritsi poisoned her family, Ivan learned his parents intended to send Kristina to a prestigious boarding school. Screams, cruel cackling, and clockwork screeching filled the estate that night. When it ended, Ivan Dilisnya was the last living member of his family, and the Mists had closed around Borca.

> [!embed-monster]- Ivan Dilisnya
> ![Ivan Dilisnya](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ivan-dilisnya-rhw.md#^statblock)

#### Ivana and Ivan's Domain

Borca is altered by Ivana's and Ivan's presences, creating the following effects:

- **Closing the Borders.** While in their domain, Ivana or Ivan can close or open the borders to Borca at will. While the borders are closed, the Mists surrounding Borca are filled with briar vines (Ivana) or barbed wire (Ivan). The Mists become [Difficult Terrain](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/difficult-terrain-xphb.md), and whenever a creature moves into or within the Mists, it takes `dice:2d4|noform|noparens|avg` (`2d4`) Piercing damage for every 5 feet it travels. Once Ivana or Ivan closes or opens the borders, neither Darklord can do so again until the next dawn.  
- **Ivana's Whispers (Ivana Only).** Ivana can encode a message of 25 words or fewer into flowers in Borca at dawn. Until the next dawn, the first time a creature smells a flower, it hears the message in its mind, understanding the meaning of the message.  
- **Mystery Letters (Ivan Only).** Whenever Ivan writes a letter and addresses it to a creature in Borca whose name he knows and that he's seen before, the letter appears near that creature at the next dawn. The letter appears in an unobserved but obvious space, such as a bedside table or among gear.  
- **Spies.** While in Borca, Ivana and Ivan can cast [Clairvoyance](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/clairvoyance-xphb.md), requiring no Material components and using Intelligence as the spellcasting ability. To cast the spell, there must be a Large or bigger plant (Ivana) or a Tiny doll or similar toy (Ivan) within range from which the sensor appears.  

If a Darklord of Borca dies, that Darklord's effects end immediately. Those effects resume if that Darklord gains a new body (see [Ivana's](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ivana-boritsi-rhw.md) and [Ivan's](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ivan-dilisnya-rhw.md) Darklord Restoration traits).

#### Ivana's Lair

The vast Boritsi estate, Misericordia, hosts fields, greenhouses, and alchemy labs used to create Boritsi-branded perfumes and tinctures. Within the manor, the Darklord cultivates rare and unique plants in greenhouse-like conservatory wings only she can enter.

##### Misericordia Conservatories

The conservatories of Misericordia, the Boritsi estate, hold strange plants, many of which Ivana cultivated. One such site is depicted on map 2.4 and has the following features:

- **Gardens.** Plants of exceptional beauty and toxicity flourish under Ivana's care in Misericordia's gardens and greenhouses. Many require unusual fertilizers to flourish—particularly the carnivorous plants.  
- **Laboratory.** In her lab, the Darklord brews deadly alchemical concoctions and wondrous perfumes. A sizable perfume organ here is filled with rare scents and lethal poisons.  
- **Nursery.** Hidden behind a rotating wall is Ivana's private nursery and study. Here she cultivates new plant species, many of which have supernatural properties or monstrous life.  

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.4: Misericordia Greenhouse](file://book/RHW/051-map-04-02.misericordia-greenhouse.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/052-map-04-02.misericordia-greenhouse-player.webp#gallery)

#### Ivan's Lair

The Dilisnya estate, Degravo, is a confusing tangle of topiary gardens, hedge mazes, and neglected petting zoos that abut sheer cliffs. At the heart of the grounds sits a largely abandoned compound that includes the Laughing House, Ivan's home.

##### The Laughing House

The only occupied structure in Degravo, the Laughing House has been renovated and redecorated to suit a child's whimsical tastes. The site is depicted on map 2.4 and has the following features:

- **Ivan's Playroom.** On the second floor of the manor, a gallery of childish art leads to doors minded by a clockwork attendant that Ivan can taunt intruders through. At the hall's end is a fake bedroom decorated for a neglected youngster. A hidden door there leads to Ivan's true personal chambers. This playroom is a wonderland of ingenious toys, all of which are secretly deadly. Beyond the Darklord's personal chamber lie secret rooms where he creates new playthings and discards toys he's grown tired of.  
- **Playhouse.** Beyond a lobby attended by clockwork staff, a theater hosts brutal stage productions for Ivan's amusement. Performers might be life-size toys or desperate prisoners.  

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.4: Degravo Laughing House](file://book/RHW/053-map-04-03.degravo-laughing-house.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/054-map-04-03.degravo-laughing-house-player.webp#gallery)

### Adventures in Borca

Adventures set in Borca involve intrigue between petty nobles, family secrets, manipulation, and deception. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

![At Misericordia, the Boritsi family estate, Ivana Boritsi indulges her research into rare and deadly plants](file://book/RHW/055-04-005.boritsi-family-estate.webp#center)

#### Horror in Borca

Adventures in Borca often include the following elements.

##### Nobles of Borca

Twelve depraved families rule over every aspect of life in Borca. Each is a core family of fifteen or fewer irredeemable individuals united around the head of the house, who tyrannically controls the clan's myriad ventures. Servants and business representatives across the domain support these core families, as do members of branch families—lackeys with different surnames who are distantly related to the core family or indentured to them.

The Noble Families of Borca table details the domain's most powerful families.

![Noble Families of Borca](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/noble-families-of-borca-rhw.md)

##### Supernatural Intrigue

Magic and the supernatural heighten the gilded depravities of Borca. When planning adventures in Borca, consider including the following elements.

###### Curses and Poison

"Chapter 3" of the "Dungeon Master's Guide" describes curses, magical contagions, and poison. Villains in Borca might use these or adjusted versions of your own design—perhaps with signature cosmetic effects.

###### Monsters

Monsters can serve as threats but also agents of noble houses. [Shape-shifting](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/shape-shifting-xphb.md) creatures such as [Imps](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fiend/imp-xmm.md) and [Wererats](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/wererat-xmm.md) excel at infiltration, while [Doppelgangers](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/doppelganger-xmm.md) and [Succubi](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fiend/succubus-xmm.md) might pose as nobles, innocents, or trusted allies. Creatures like [Ghosts](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/ghost-xmm.md) and [Intellect Devourers](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/aberration/intellect-devourer-xmm.md) might control individuals, making them behave in unusual ways. Choose a single monster, and consider how you might make it central to a devious noble's plot.

###### Spells and Magic Items

Don't try to account for or incorporate all magic into adventures involving supernatural intrigue. Choose a single spell—such as [Clairvoyance](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/clairvoyance-xphb.md), [Geas](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/geas-xphb.md), or [Speak with Dead](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/speak-with-dead-xphb.md)—and consider how to make it central to a plot involving secrets and mysterious revelations. Consider doing the same with a magic item such as a [Cloak of the Bat](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/cloak-of-the-bat-xdmg.md), a [Hag Eye](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/hag-eye-xdmg.md), or [Sending Stones](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/sending-stones-xdmg.md). Characters should earn rewards for using their own magic in clever ways.

#### Borca Campaign Arc

Campaigns set in Borca typically involve the domain's noble families. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–3.** A scheming noble targets the characters, presenting them with an opportunity or exorbitant compensation for a simple task. In the aftermath, the characters discover they have given up something of great value or realize they look like criminals.  
- **Levels 4–6.** The scheming noble or a rival offers the characters a way out of their predicament, but this involves a dangerous confrontation or daring infiltration. Supernatural forces—such as jilted doppelgangers, cursed family members, or dead nobility—might aid the characters. Against expectations, the characters complete their mission and turn the tables on their foe.  
- **Levels 7–8.** The characters' activities attract the attention of [Ivana Boritsi](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ivana-boritsi-rhw.md) or [Ivan Dilisnya](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ivan-dilisnya-rhw.md). The Darklord invites the characters to their estate or corresponds with them from afar, using them as agents in their rivalry. For example, either Darklord might task the characters with seeking out the missing will of Ivana's father, Klaus.  

#### Lethal Lavender

*Adventure for Level 5 Characters*

- **Situation.** The human siblings Eroso and Siobhan Manduchi (Medium, Neutral Evil [Nobles](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/noble-xmm.md)) are scions of a minor noble family who stole a rare plant, not realizing it belonged to the Boritsis. After discovering the owner, they feign their deaths to avoid reprisal.  
- **Hook.** Eroso and Siobhan seek out the characters to use as patsies in their staged murder.  

##### Encounters

The adventure consists of these encounters.

###### Dig Your Vibe

Eroso and Siobhan Manduchi approach the characters and invite them to go carousing if the adventurers agree to share tales of their exploits. The two are [Friendly](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/friendly-attitude-xphb.md) and flattering.

###### Exquisite Corpse

Soon after the characters leave the siblings, they hear a scream. If they investigate, they find Eroso's stabbed corpse surrounded by guards. Siobhan accuses the characters of killing her brother. A group of four [Guards](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/guard-xmm.md) and one [Guard Captain](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/guard-captain-xmm.md) (in the Manduchis' employ) moves to kill the characters, while Siobhan vanishes into the night.

###### Wanted

More guards hunt for the characters but are easy to avoid. Before the characters flee the community, Nostalia Romaine (Medium, Lawful Evil [Assassin](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/assassin-xmm.md)), who appears to be human, discovers them. She explains that she works for the Boritsi family, shares the details in "Situation" above, and insists the characters help her find the Manduchis.

###### Dead Walking

Any character who spends a day searching for the Manduchis and succeeds on a DC 14 Wisdom ([Insight](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Insight)) or Charisma ([Persuasion](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Persuasion)) check learns Eroso's or Siobhan's whereabouts. If they investigate, they find a public site—like a theater or bar—where the noble is behaving recklessly. These aren't the actual Manduchis, but [Waxworks](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/construct/waxwork-rhw.md) (see chapter 5) striving to destroy themselves in public. The characters encounter at least two of these creatures, perhaps more at your discretion.

###### Flawed Perfection

After the characters encounter at least two self-destructive Manduchi waxworks, they find a **Waxwork** convinced that it is the new, improved Eroso Manduchi, and it doesn't want to die. If the characters promise to let it go, the Construct leads them to Lethal Lavender, the secret club where the Manduchis are hiding.

###### Lethal Lavender

The interior of the Lethal Lavender club is overgrown with bruise-colored fungus. A pair of fungus-covered [Zombie Plague Spreaders](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/zombie-plague-spreader-rhw.md) haunts the bar. In the VIP lounge, the plant the Manduchis stole has bloomed into a [Violet Fungus Necrohulk](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/plant/violet-fungus-necrohulk-xmm.md) composed of the real Manduchis and their remaining wax duplicates.

###### Ivana's Favor

After the monster's defeat, Nostalia finds the characters. She rewards them with a vial of Boritsi perfume worth 2,000 GP and a letter from Ivana Boritsi inviting them to a private social event at Misericordia in a week's time. Each character also earns a bonus 1,100 XP.

## Darkon

*Domain on the Brink of Destruction*

> [!note] 
> 
> - **Darklord.** None  
> - **Genres.** Dark fantasy and disaster horror  
> - **Hallmarks.** Fractured realm, magical ruins, ongoing supernatural catastrophe  
> - **Mist Talismans.** Ashes of a corpse, coin stamped with Azalin Rex's face, tainted spring water  
> - **Aligned Tarokka Card.** Necromancer  
> - **Opposed Tarokka Card.** Donjon  
^113

> [!gallery]
> ![](file://book/RHW/056-05-001.necromancer-tarokka.webp#gallery)
> ![](file://book/RHW/057-05-002.donjon-tarokka.webp#gallery)

Darkon is a sprawling realm of somber gothic cities, vast wildernesses, hidden secrets, and the dead. The ruins of forgotten magical empires scar the land. Undead creatures haunt the domain's lonely reaches, and the living acknowledge that the land's morbid magic might one day reanimate their corpses.

Yet, for all its mysteries, the domain of Darkon has failed. Across the realm, the Mists close in, inexorably overwhelming the land. These Mists turned ravenous are known as the Shroud, and what they consume doesn't reemerge.

Darkon's dissolution ties to the disappearance of its Darklord, [Azalin Rex](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/azalin-rex-rhw.md). During a disastrous event known as the Hour of Ascension, Azalin's citadel, Castle Avernus, was destroyed, and a mysterious golden star called the King's Tear appeared in the heavens. Since then, no one has seen Azalin, and the Shroud has eroded the domain.

Despite the encroaching annihilation, life in Darkon hasn't changed. The residents of towns and cities far from the domain's borders dismiss reports of vanishing frontiers as fearmongering. As Darkon splits into crumbling islands, ambitious individuals vie for Azalin's power, each touting that they alone can save the land by becoming its tyrant.

### Domain Features

Darkon is known for the following features:

- **Divided Domain.** The Mists consuming Darkon have divided the land into four separate regions.  
- **Hour of Ascension.** Azalin Rex vanished during an event his servants call the Hour of Ascension.  
- **Inevitable Undeath.** The night after any Humanoid dies, its corpse reanimates and shambles into the night. Locals swiftly burn bodies to prevent this.  
- **King's Tear.** Since the Hour of Ascension, a golden star called the King's Tear hangs in the sky. The sun and moon pass behind this star in their orbits.  
- **Secret Police.** The Kargat, the domain's secret police, remains active in Darkon's largest cities: Il Aluk and Martira Bay.  

### Locations in Darkon

Darkon is a place of dark wonders and apathy. The ruins of impossible structures litter the landscape, but the domain's jaded people ignore these marvels to focus on daily concerns.

The regions of Darkon are described below, and other notable locations are summarized on the "Darkon Locations table".

#### Regions of Darkon

The Shroud has divided Darkon into four parts (see "Fractures of Darkon" for details):

- **Jagged Coast.** Dense forests and shattered cliffs compose the Jagged Coast, skirting the Sea of Souls. Undead within the forests prey on isolated communities here.  
- **Lychgate.** Lychgate is ruled by the dead. Aimless undead creatures wander the forest, milling around amid the time-locked ruins of Castle Avernus and many of Azalin's powerful servants.  
- **Mistlands.** Scattered communities dot the Mistlands, which were once Darkon's wild eastern reaches. Strange monsters emerge from the forests and mountains to prey on the isolated lands.  
- **Rexcrown.** The heart of Darkon, Rexcrown has become a sagging bog. From it rise the spires and grim wonders of Il Aluk, Darkon's capital, and the homes of the domain's indifferent elite.  

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.5: Darkon](file://book/RHW/058-map-05-01.darkon.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/059-map-05-01.darkon-player.webp#gallery)

![Darkon Locations](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/darkon-locations-rhw.md)

### Azalin Rex

*Darklord Who Won't Be Caged*

![](file://book/RHW/060-05-003.azalin-rex.webp#center)

> [!quote] A quote from Azalin Rex  
> 
> It is customary to kneel before your dread lord.

In Darkon, Azalin was a tyrannical wizard-king obeyed by the living and the dead. When he first appeared before his people, he adopted an illusion of the form he possessed in life: that of a middle-aged human man with dark hair and a superior demeanor. However, his true form was that of a moldering lich, eyes ablaze with blasphemous energy.

Since arriving in the Domains of Dread, Azalin has been unable to learn new magic. For a wizard who forsook his mortality to pursue arcane studies, this was the ultimate frustration. Despite the limits on his studies, Azalin numbered among the few Darklords who understood the mysterious nature of the Domains of Dread. For generations, Azalin struggled to escape Darkon. His magical atrocities reshaped Darkon and the Domains of Dread time and again. However, these struggles gave Azalin only a glimpse of freedom, and his metaphysical violations inevitably reverted to the Dark Powers' original designs. Nevertheless, Azalin refused to stay a prisoner. His most recent plot culminated in the Hour of Ascension and the destruction of Castle Avernus. Since then, no one in Darkon has seen the Darklord, and his realm has begun deteriorating.

The stat block in this section presents the Darklord as he was prior to his disappearance and how he would be should he return. Azalin's current spirit jar is a golden amulet he carries. If this amulet is destroyed, Azalin's original spirit jar—an immovable dragon skull in the ruins of Castle Avernus—reactivates, and the lich's spirit returns to Darkon if his body is destroyed.

> [!embed-monster]- Azalin Rex
> ![Azalin Rex](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/azalin-rex-rhw.md#^statblock)

#### Azalin's Tale

Firan Zal'honan was a noble and heir to the city-state of Knurl on the world of Oerth. A student of magic, Firan adopted the title "Azal'Lan," meaning "wizard-king," when he came to power. Firan's rule was marked by harsh laws and violent expansion, but his people flourished, as their lives were filled with magical wonders.

As Firan aged, he looked toward his succession. His son, Irik, was generous and charming but, in Firan's eyes, soft and unfit to rule. No matter how Firan tried to teach his son of the world's harsh realities, Irik's kind spirit wouldn't bend to his father's cynical outlook. This difference came to a head when Firan caught Irik freeing political prisoners. Firan could have ignored the crime or pardoned his son. Instead, Firan personally wielded the axe during Irik's execution.

In the years that followed, Firan was tormented by his son's death, but he also became convinced that only he was fit to rule. Researching the mysteries of death, he discovered the secret to becoming a lich. After embracing the transition into undeath, Firan ruled for decades more, increasing Knurl's power and earning himself many foes. Eventually, tales of magic that might restore Irik lured Firan from his home. During his search, a band of mercenaries ambushed the ruler. Firan fled into the mist to avoid the assassins. When the mist cleared, Firan found himself in "Barovia".

In Barovia, peasants Firan encountered mistook his title and called him Azalin. Soon, Azalin encountered Barovia's ruler, [Strahd von Zarovich](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/strahd-von-zarovich-rhw.md). The two came to respect each other, and Azalin taught Strahd much of the way of magic. Together, the pair learned a great deal about the nature of the Domains of Dread and made attempts to escape. Their plots failed, though, and resulted in other realms—such as the domain of "Mordent"—being drawn into Barovia's orbit. Eventually, the two tyrants' respect soured into loathing. Before Azalin and Strahd could destroy each other, Azalin entered the Mists, and the domain of Darkon spread before him.

#### Azalin's Domain

Darkon is altered by Azalin's presence, creating the following effects:

- **Closing the Borders.** While in his domain, Azalin can close or open the borders to Darkon at will. While the borders are closed, undead terrors fill the Mists surrounding Darkon. Whenever a creature enters the Mists, one [Hostile](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/hostile-attitude-xphb.md) [Zombie Clot](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/zombie-clot-rhw.md) appears in a random unoccupied space within 30 feet of that creature.  
- **Lord of the Dead.** While in his domain, Azalin can cast [Clairvoyance](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/clairvoyance-xphb.md), requiring no spell components and using the same spellcasting ability as his Spellcasting action. When Azalin casts this spell in this way, he can place the sensor in any Undead in Darkon with an Intelligence of 6 or less, even if it is beyond 1 mile of Azalin. In addition, Azalin can speak through the Undead he placed the sensor in.  
- **No Secrets.** Whenever a creature in Darkon casts a spell using a level 5+ spell slot, Azalin becomes aware of that creature's name and location. A [Nondetection](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/nondetection-xphb.md) spell blocks this effect.  

If Azalin dies, these effects end immediately.

#### Azalin's Lair

During the Hour of Ascension, Castle Avernus—Azalin's seat of rule and magical laboratory—erupted in a magical conflagration. Now, Castle Avernus stands frozen in time at the instant of its destruction, blasted to magically floating chunks of rubble. Its towers pitch wildly and crumble to pieces amid arcane flames, yet they don't fall. Although time has halted in the ruins, Azalin's servants who avoided the disaster have returned, unaffected by the castle's frozen time. Meanwhile, the fortress's magic attempts to heal the wreckage, slowly creating new halls and winding stairs between the fractured floors.

##### Castle Avernus

Amid its magical destruction, Castle Avernus is a vast structure filled with Azalin's arcane creations and summoned servants. Prominent locations from this ruin are depicted on "map 2.7" and detailed here:

- **Outer Bailey and Gallery.** The castle's entry, called the Maw by Azalin's servants, remains partially intact. Undead from the surrounding wilds lurk here, waiting for their lord's commands.  
- **Hall of Records.** A column of stationary but still deadly magical fire blasts through Avernus's library. Scattered on ruined islands of rubble are the remains of a collection said to hold the biographies of all who have died in Darkon.  
- **Tomb of Irik Zal'honan.** Here stands the tomb of Azalin's son, Irik. The [Ghost](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/ghost-xmm.md) of Irik appears to those with benevolent intentions. Despite his tragic fate, he forgives his father—but he doesn't want Azalin to harm anyone else. He can't leave the crypt and knows little of Azalin's plots.  
- **Lair of Ebbasheyth.** The [Shadow Dragon](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/dragon/shadow-dragon-xmm.md) Ebbasheyth served as Azalin's adviser and steed. While she has moved much of her hoard to Mount Nyid, she still watches over the treasures here.  
- **Hall of Life.** The Hall of Life has largely crumbled and is accessible only via gaps in the ceiling of the floor below. Within survives a circle of glass and emerald cylinders. These hold the remains of Azalin's magical cloning experiments. A gigantic dragon skull made of gold has fallen into the midst of these failed experiments. This is Azalin's original spirit jar, but the skull's eyes, which once glowed with unholy flames, now look empty.  
- **Heart of Avernus.** Amid the tower's wreckage glows the magical anomaly called the Heart of Avernus. This is the epicenter of the disaster that destroyed the castle during the Hour of Ascension. This mysterious force draws droves of the undead to feed on the ongoing magical reaction.  

### Fractures of Darkon

The domain of Darkon has fractured into four regions: the Jagged Coast, Lychgate, the Mistlands, and Rexcrown. In Azalin's absence, ambitious villains unleash terrors as they strive to dominate their piece of the domain. This section explores the horrors unfolding in each region of Darkon.

#### Jagged Coast

Stark vistas of sheer cliffs, mysterious islands, and knotted forests bleed from one to the next along the Jagged Coast. The shadow of Castle Avernus once loomed over the southern part of the region, enforcing grim peace on the small communities there. In the north, the thriving city of Martira Bay prides itself on its inhabitants' wealth and reason.

Since Azalin's disappearance, the Darklord's secret police have maintained order here—obeying not the commands of the missing king, but rather the will of their regional leader, Alcio Metus.

![The Treacherous Harbor of Martira Bay](file://book/RHW/061-05-004.martira-bay.webp#center)

##### Kargat

Azalin's secret police, the Kargat, has long enforced the Darklord's edicts and smothered any ember of rebellion in Darkon. Those "disappeared" by the Kargat are never seen again.

While all Darkon fears these dark-cloaked spies, few realize the Kargat is largely composed of vampires and other shape-shifting creatures. Members operate in cells assigned to particular tasks or locations, with each reporting to a regional leader. The highest-ranking members reported to Azalin. Serving the Kargat are the Kargatane, a cultlike rank of living informants and initiates who spy on their neighbors in hopes of earning supernatural power and induction into the larger organization.

The Hour of Ascension threw the Kargat into disorder. Taking advantage of this opportunity, Alcio Metus (Medium, Neutral Evil [Vampire](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/vampire-xmm.md)), a Kargat leader and criminal kingpin in Martira Bay, slew her peers and took over the western branch of the group. From the Black Tower in Martira Bay, Alcio spreads her Kargat spies across region and beyond.

##### Martira Bay

A foggy port on the Sea of Souls, Martira Bay is a cosmopolitan hub of trade and ideas. The populace prides itself on its worldliness and believes that the best of Darkon and lands beyond passes through the city. Martira Bay's people appreciate reason and tangibility, and many have never left the city. This makes many residents incredulous of magic and the supernatural, even as séances and spiritualist practices flourish in posh salons.

Martira Bay is infamous for sensationalist murders. Newspapers such as *The Bullseye* update their devoted readership on the grisly details of sprees committed by killers such as the Midnight Slasher, the Spider, and the Weeping Woman. The overwhelmed Martira Bay constabulary works to counter these killers, as do professional detective agencies including the Ray Detectives (founded by Alanik Ray; see chapter 3) and the Dusklight Detectives.

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.6: Martira Bay](file://book/RHW/062-map-05-02.martira-bay.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/063-map-05-02.martira-bay-player.webp#gallery)

#### Lychgate

Lychgate hides the magically shattered remains of Castle Avernus. Whatever ongoing magical disaster befell the castle during the Hour of Ascension has locked its ruins in time, freezing it in a semi-exploded state. While Castle Avernus remains the lair of some of Azalin's most dangerous servants, the surrounding wilderness has become overrun by shuffling corpses and mournful spirits drawn to the castle's strange magic. The region is ruled by Ebbasheyth, Azalin's [Shadow Dragon](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/dragon/shadow-dragon-xmm.md) ally who maintains a lair in Castle Avernus.

Adventures in Lychgate likely relate to the mystery of Azalin's disappearance. Roll on or choose a result from the Doom in Lychgate table to inspire adventures in this ruined realm.

![Doom in Lychgate](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/doom-in-lychgate-rhw.md)

#### Mistlands

Even before the Hour of Ascension, western Darkon was a land of magical mysteries and strange creatures. No longer fearing the Darklord's magic, ancient evils have crept from the shadows to terrorize and control the scattered communities.

In the town of Nevuchar Springs, an elf mystic and leader of the Eternal Order, Cardinna Artazas, works to turn back the Shroud. To do this, she sought to resurrect a being bonded to the land and capable of bending the Mists to its will. This resulted in the corruption of her order's sacred pools and unleashed Darcalus Rex, a [Necrichor](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/necrichor-rhw.md) (see chapter 5) that claims to be the first king of Darkon. Uncertain of what it has unleashed but desperate for salvation, the Eternal Order serves the whims of Darcalus Rex as the strange being grows in power.

##### Rexcrown

Residents of Rexcrown consider themselves the only true Darkonians due to their proximity to the capital, Il Aluk. Despite that prestige, Rexcrown is covered in deadly swamps, depleted mountains, and fields that produce disturbingly malformed crops.

The city of Il Aluk is built in a bend in the Vuchar River and rises in countless gothic spires. These mark the homes of the city's elite, severe governmental buildings, and temples dedicated to dozens of grim deities. Serving the city are the vassal villages of Decimus, Desolatus, and Despondia, where peasants struggle to feed the city's people and the decadent lifestyles of local nobles.

As the Shroud spreads fear among traders, Il Aluk suffers from shortages in food and other supplies. The city's residents have grown desperate and resentful of the exploitative upper class. This has resulted in violence and the ransacking of wealthy homes. The city's elite have rallied behind one of their eldest members, Lady Talisveri Eris.

Eris is a vain human who uses elaborate fashions and makeup to disguise the fact that her body is permanently imperceptible. Once each moon, she incites her fearful peers to go out at night and commit violence while using her high-priced [Potions of Greater Invisibility](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/potion-of-greater-invisibility-xdmg.md). These magical attacks and Eris's pompous, detached rhetoric exacerbate tensions in the city while enriching her nearly bankrupt family.

### Adventures in Darkon

Adventures set in Darkon's disconnected regions often involve the mystery of Azalin's disappearance, the domain's dissolution, or the metaphysical nature of the Domains of Dread. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

#### Horror in Darkon

Beyond the adventures you might develop in Darkon's disconnected regions, the following elements persist across the domain.

##### Azalin's Fate

The events of the Hour of Ascension and the fate of Azalin loom over adventures in Darkon. The details of these mysteries are yours to decide. You can take inspiration from the following possibilities when determining Azalin's fate.

###### Severed Darklord

During the Hour of Ascension, Azalin's body was destroyed as he tore open portals to the Negative and Positive Energy Planes. The former portal lies at the heart of Castle Avernus, while the latter is known as the King's Tear. The opposed planar energies are disrupting Darkon. Once the domain is destroyed, Azalin theorizes, his spirit jar will be released into the Shadowfell.

###### Shattered Darklord

The Hour of Ascension was Azalin's failed attempt to become one of the Dark Powers. His essence is now trapped within his spirit jar, scattered pieces of his iron crown, and the floating amber sarcophagus known as the King's Tear. Whoever frees Azalin's essence will become the new Darklord.

###### Unmoored Darklord

During the Hour of Ascension, Azalin split his soul, leaving a piece in Darkon while the greater part escaped through a metaphysical rent between domains—the King's Tear. Now, disguised as the scholar Firan Zal'honan, Azalin searches for secrets of the Dark Powers in other domains. He avoids entering the Mists without Mist-wandering guides, fearing the Dark Powers will find him otherwise.

##### The Dead Serve

In Darkon, Humanoid corpses reanimate as [Zombies](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/zombie-xmm.md) 24 hours after death. These corpses obey Azalin. While he remains missing, they roam in a winding path toward Castle Avernus. These zombies avoid other creatures, but they fight anything that blocks their path.

##### The Shroud

During the day, one can traverse the Mists surrounding Darkon as normal, allowing travel between domains or regions of Darkon. At night, the Mists surrounding the domain turn deadly and encroach on the land—sometimes by infinitesimal degrees, other times in unstoppable floods. A creature that touches the Shroud takes `dice:2d6|noform|noparens|avg|text(7)` (`2d6`) Necrotic damage and is [Frightened](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/conditions.md#Frightened) until the end of its next turn. If a creature is slain by the Shroud or enters it entirely, the creature vanishes. What becomes of it is a mystery.

#### Darkon Campaign Arc

Campaigns set in Darkon likely involve the mystery of the Hour of Ascension. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–3.** The characters arrive in Darkon near Il Aluk, Martira Bay, or Nevuchar Springs. They soon make an ally among those who oppose the villains rising to replace Azalin: Alcio Metus, Darcalus Rex, or Talisveri Eris. The characters help defend their allies and learn of these villains' methods.  
- **Levels 4–15.** The characters confront the region's villain. Rather than fighting the characters, the villain entreats the group to help them establish control over the domain, which they believe will reunite Darkon's regions and end the threat of the Shroud. To do so, they must defeat the domain's other villains or recover the scattered remnants of Azalin's power. The characters work to save Darkon while undermining their wicked patron.  
- **Levels 16–18.** The characters' adventures take them to Castle Avernus, where they must either claim a remnant of Azalin's might or learn his fate. In doing so, they can restore Azalin and bring his wrath down on those who would claim his throne.  

#### Secrets of Avernus

*Adventure for Level 16 Characters*

- **Situation.** The characters must learn the secret of Azalin's disappearance.  
- **Hook.** The threat of the Shroud and those who would claim Azalin's throne has grown too great to ignore. An ally directs the characters to the only place they can find answers regarding Azalin's disappearance: Castle Avernus.  

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.7: Castle Avernus](file://book/RHW/064-map-05-03.castle-avernus-prominent-ruins.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/065-map-05-03.castle-avernus-prominent-ruins-player.webp#gallery)

##### Encounters

This adventure uses map 2.7: Castle Avernus. Before starting, consult the "Azalin's Fate" section and develop the details behind the Darklord's disappearance. The floors of Castle Avernus are disconnected, allowing characters to access them in any order.

###### Lychgate Encounters

While traveling through Lychgate or between floors of Castle Avernus, roll on the following table to determine what the characters encounter.

`dice: [](3-chapter-2-domains-of-ravenloft.md#^1-encounter)`

| dice: 1d4 | Encounter |
|-----------|-----------|
| 1 | Two scavenging [Arcanaloths](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fiend/arcanaloth-xmm.md) |
| 2 | Two [Dullahans](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/dullahan-rhw.md) (see chapter 5) and two [Nightmares](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fiend/nightmare-xmm.md) |
| 3 | Two [Haunting Revenants](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/haunting-revenant-xmm.md) disguised as rubble |
| 4 | Two [Relentless Juggernauts](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fiend/relentless-juggernaut-rhw.md) |
^1-encounter

###### Into the Maw

Droves of animate corpses fill the outer bailey. A [Spirit Naga](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fiend/spirit-naga-xmm.md) named Lossa lurks amid the rubble. If she spots the characters, she impersonates Azalin and commands the corpses to fight. They rise as three [Zombie Clots](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/zombie-clot-rhw.md).

###### The Archive

Elzarath, an [Indifferent](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/indifferent-attitude-xphb.md) [Ghost](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/ghost-xmm.md) with a floating severed head, laments the state of the archives. Elzarath shares that they once held the biographies of all who died in Darkon, but now the books are scattered. If asked about Azalin's biography, the ghost searches and finds nothing. Elzarath doesn't know Azalin's actual name, but if specifically asked about the biography of Firan Zal'honan, the ghost finds the book. This biography relates the information in the "Azalin's Tale" section and key details of the Hour of Ascension.

###### Crypt of Irik Zal'honan

The [Ghost](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/ghost-xmm.md) Irik Zal'honan appears to any Good-aligned creature or those who call out to him. Irik can't leave this area, but he aids those who seek to restore his father. He knows Azalin's true name is Firan Zal'honan and shares that with anyone who destroys the corrupted experiment in the Hall of Life in the ruins above. Irik reveals that he is Azalin's son only if asked directly.

###### Hall of Life

This room holds a dragon skull made of gold and a circle of glass and emerald cylinders. The dragon skull remains magically anchored so only Azalin can move it. The cylinders are cracked and filled with bubbling decay. If someone smashes all the cylinders, the cylinders fuse into a Hostile abomination with the same stat block as a [Lesser Star Spawn Emissary](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/aberration/lesser-star-spawn-emissary-rhw.md).

###### Ebbasheyth's Lair

Ebbasheyth the [Shadow Dragon](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/dragon/shadow-dragon-xmm.md) is in her lair, attended by a Kargat messenger (Medium [Vampire Nightbringer](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/vampire-nightbringer-xmm.md)). The monsters are [Hostile](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/hostile-attitude-xphb.md), but any character who takes an [Influence](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/actions.md#Influence) action and succeeds on a DC 16 Charisma ([Persuasion](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Persuasion)) check can make them [Indifferent](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/indifferent-attitude-xphb.md). Characters who mention their desire to restore Azalin have [Advantage](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/advantage-xphb.md) on this check. If made Indifferent, Ebbasheyth tells the characters the archives might hold details of Azalin's schemes. If asked what name to search for, she doesn't know but relates that the spirit in the room below might.

###### Conclusion

The biography of Firan Zal'honan in the archive reveals the secret of Azalin's disappearance. From this, the characters should know how to find or restore Azalin or how to recover his power. Each character also earns a bonus 9,800 XP.

## Dementlieu

*Domain of Decadent Delusion*

> [!note] 
> 
> - **Darklord.** Saidra d'Honaire  
> - **Genres.** Dark fantasy and psychological horror  
> - **Hallmarks.** Masquerades, decadent aristocracy, social decay, illusions, impostor syndrome  
> - **Mist Talismans.** Jeweled or feathered mask, article of well-worn fine clothing, shoe made of glass or gold  
> - **Aligned Tarokka Card.** Charlatan  
> - **Opposed Tarokka Card.** Seer  
^136

> [!gallery]
> ![](file://book/RHW/066-06-001.charlatan-tarokka.webp#gallery)
> ![](file://book/RHW/067-06-002.seer-tarokka.webp#gallery)

Composed of the city of Port-a-Lucine and its shining, fog-shrouded outskirts, Dementlieu is a realm where the truth is smothered by collective delusion. Everything in Port-a-Lucine appears to be more than it is, and people behave as if the few examples of grandeur and prosperity were the norm. Beneath its facade, the city is rotten.

Despite pervasive claims of happiness and success, the people of Dementlieu fight to survive and maintain social appearances. Every individual struggles to hide their struggles. Lying is central to life in the domain, creating a breeding ground for con artists and smiling villains.

Behind the domain's denial of reality is its Darklord, the phantomlike [Duchess Saidra d'Honaire](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/saidra-dhonaire-rhw.md). The cynosure of high society, this masked duchess ensnares the city's upper class in her exaggerated ideas of luxury and civility. During her weekly masquerade balls, Saidra's guests must perform to her expectations. Those who fail to charm her are decried as impostors and reduced to ash by her magic. Saidra's terror also grips the city's desperate. Her murderous, unmasked form—the Red Death—stalks the benighted streets, preying on any who tarnish her preposterous vision of a perfect society.

### Domain Features

Dementlieu is known for the following features:

- **City of Lies.** Nothing in Port-a-Lucine is as it appears. Everyone pretends to be more successful than they are. Lies great and small fill everyday communication. All residents know these truths, but none dares speak of them.  
- **Grand Masquerade.** Every week Duchess d'Honaire holds a Grand Masquerade. Invitations are coveted, and invitees who don't attend rarely survive for long.
