- **Lord Governor.** Administration of Port-a-Lucine rests in the hands of Lord Governor Marcel Guignol. He is counseled by aristocratic advisers, including the duchess.  
- **Masks.** Decorative masks are common accessories, worn at social events and in daily life.  

### Locations in Dementlieu

Port-a-Lucine's grand structures and garish promenades dazzle viewers, distracting most from the grimy streets and cramped homes beyond. The countryside of Chateaufaux is described below, and other notable locations are summarized on the "Dementlieu Locations table".

#### Chateaufaux

The people of Port-a-Lucine speak of the countryside, Chateaufaux, where nobles summer at their estates and where idyllic villages send goods for sale into the city. But no one travels far beyond the city walls, no goods arrive from beyond, and Chateaufaux doesn't actually exist. The Mists creep close to Port-a-Lucine, occasionally exposing patches of forests and meadows but nothing more. Nevertheless, Chateaufaux remains a convenient explanation for whatever mysteriously appears or disappears.

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.8: Dementlieu](file://book/RHW/068-map-06-01.dementlieu.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/069-map-06-01.dementlieu-player.webp#gallery)

![Dementlieu Locations](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/dementlieu-locations-rhw.md)

### Saidra d'Honaire

*Darklord Who Rules Illusions*

![](file://book/RHW/070-06-003.saidra-dhonaire.webp#center)

> [!quote] A quote from Saidra d'Honaire  
> 
> Welcome, treasured guests—you bright jewels in my city's sterling crown. Bask in all you've earned and deserve. Oh... that's not a loose button, is it?

Duchess Saidra d'Honaire knows her life isn't her own—she knows she isn't alive at all—yet she ignores that for the sparkle of empty celebrations and a parody of her ideal life. The duchess terrorizes Dementlieu, forcing the realm to conform to her desires. Those who expose the flaws in her fantasy and remind her of the desperation she once endured, she slays using her life-sapping power.

All can plainly see Duchess d'Honaire isn't one of the living. Nevertheless, servants and sycophants flatter her poise, beauty, and array of lavish masquerade costumes. When not hosting decadent social events, Saidra removes her mask and slips into the night. Through the streets and alleys of Port-a-Lucine, the Darklord prowls as the Red Death: a murderous spirit that preys on liars, the struggling, and all who remind her of her humble origins.

Saidra is overbearing and elitist, despite being unworldly. She fears being exposed as a fraud and projects this fear onto others, violently accusing them of being liars on the barest evidence or sign of vulgarity. Yet, in mysterious letters and rumors, Saidra receives evidence that her own simple, spiteful family dwells somewhere beyond her city. Their confessions could bring all her deceptions to light.

> [!embed-monster]- Saidra d'Honaire
> ![Saidra d'Honaire](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/saidra-dhonaire-rhw.md#^statblock)

#### Saidra's Tale

Despite being raised in poverty, Saidra d'Honaire was an arrogant bully whose father led her to believe she was secretly royalty. When her father remarried, Saidra suffered slights and mockery at the hands of her callous stepmother and stepsisters.

The night her father revealed that Saidra was only distantly related to nobility, she fled into the night. At her mother's grave, Saidra's curses were overheard by a mysterious stranger. This grandmotherly figure offered to grant Saidra any wish. When the stranger heard Saidra's desire, she cackled and dressed the girl in rubies and a crimson gown. Resplendent, Saidra set off to the masquerade ball celebrating the coronation of the land's new duke.

At the masquerade, Saidra charmed the duke and his court. Yet, as bells tolled midnight, the gems on her dress evaporated, releasing a magical poison. The evil magic killed everyone at the masquerade, a massacre that would have fulfilled Saidra's murderous wish and left her within reach of the throne. As Saidra toured a palace full of the dying, clouds of spreading poison rose in a mysterious mist.

When the mist cleared, Saidra found herself in a grand estate in Port-a-Lucine. The estate's servants acknowledged her as their duchess, but the lethal poison had dissolved Saidra's body into a deathly vapor. As none seemed to notice, Saidra embraced the fantasy that she had achieved her vain desires.

#### Saidra's Domain

Dementlieu is altered by Saidra's presence, creating the following effects:

- **Closing the Borders.** While in her domain, Saidra can close or open the borders to Dementlieu at will. While the borders are closed, the countryside called Chateaufaux appears in the Mists surrounding Dementlieu. Creatures in the Mists get lost amid mazelike hedgerows and fogbanks, only to reappear on the outskirts of Port-a-Lucine `dice:2d6|noform|noparens|avg` (`2d6`) hours later.  
- **Empowered Actors.** Humanoids add `dice:1d8|noform|noparens|avg` (`1d8`) to Charisma ([Deception](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Deception) or [Performance](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Performance)) checks made while wearing a mask.  
- **Invitation.** At dawn, Saidra can choose a creature whose name she knows or that she's seen before. A simple mask and an invitation to the next Grand Masquerade appear to that creature. The letter and mask appear in an unobserved but obvious space, such as a bedside table or among gear.  

If [Saidra](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/saidra-dhonaire-rhw.md) dies, these effects end immediately. The effects resume if Saidra gains a new body (see her Darklord Restoration trait).

#### Saidra's Lair

The duchess dwells at the d'Honaire Estate. This lavish manor and its manicured grounds cover the largest island in Lucine Bay.

##### D'Honaire Estate

The d'Honaire Estate is well lit and filled with expensive decor and artwork—some of it quite good, but most is of middling quality. The estate is depicted on "map 2.9" and has the following features:

- **Grand Entry.** A grand staircase sweeps from the estate's entry to airy balconies above. This broad space also serves as a ballroom and is the focus of the duchess's social events.  
- **Salons.** Elegant rooms with distinct themes fill the estate. Popular spaces include the Skobeloff Salon (themed like a sunken ship), the Sulfur Salon (with dizzying wallpaper), and the Taupe Salon (filled with underwhelming taxidermies).  
- **Sea Caves and Docks.** Those who travel to the island estate by gondola dock in this sculpted sea cave. Stairs rise from the docks to the main estate.  
- **Second Floor.** The halls remain locked and guarded. Within are the duchess's quarters, a joyless, hollow space that the Darklord haunts between stalkings and social events.  

### Adventures in Dementlieu

Adventures set in Dementlieu feature mystery and deception, often involving illusions and fairy-tale grandeur masking depravity and murder. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

![The desperate elite of Port-a-Lucine gather at Duchess d'Honaire's island estate for the Grand Masquerade](file://book/RHW/071-06-004.port-a-lucine.webp#center)

#### Horror in Dementlieu

Adventures in Dementlieu often include the following elements.

##### Lies and Liars

In Dementlieu, one can take little at face value. Terrible food might be called gourmet, while horrendous art might be dubbed avant garde. Those who resist such claims might find themselves mocked for not understanding a thing's appeal. This can lead to challenges that range from the comical to the surreal. Roll on or choose a result from the Dementlieu Deceptions table to inspire overlooked events that might lead to broader consequences.

![Dementlieu Deceptions](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/dementlieu-deceptions-rhw.md)

##### Scourge of the Red Death

Between masquerades, Saidra d'Honaire fixates on her past and her fear that people suspect her ignoble origins. At these times, her glamorous facade fades, reducing her to a crimson spirit. In this guise, she slips into the night and scours Port-a-Lucine, targeting the sick, poor, or uncouth; those who disparage nobles; and those she suspects of investigating her past. The resulting life-drained bodies are attributed to a notorious figure locals call the Red Death.

###### Using the Red Death

While Port-a-Lucine's residents ignore the Red Death's victims—potentially chiding corpses for their laziness or public drunkenness—the characters are unlikely to overlook bodies so clearly drained of life. Use such corpses to remind the group that the lies of Dementlieu's people are dangerous denials of reality.

#### Dementlieu Campaign Arc

Campaigns set in Dementlieu often involve the discovery and unraveling of a conspiracy. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–3.** Someone asks the characters in Port-a-Lucine for help finding a missing friend, opera performer, or noble. Following the clues, the characters learn this is but one of a rash of disappearances involving dangerous creatures hiding in plain sight—such as [Gargoyles](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/elemental/gargoyle-xmm.md), [Wererats](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/wererat-xmm.md), or [Waxworks](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/construct/waxwork-rhw.md) (see chapter 5).  
- **Level 4–5.** The mystery points toward an elite member of society. The characters can't gain access to this individual, but they know the noble attends the Grand Masquerade of Duchess d'Honaire. The characters must prepare for and infiltrate the event (detailed below) to learn more.  
- **Levels 6–8.** Learning that the suspicious noble supports or benefits from the disappearances, the characters investigate the noble's home or business (such as the opera house or House of Wax). There, they discover and disrupt the creatures behind the disappearances, likely finding that the vanished people have been turned into monsters. If the noble escapes, an unrefusable invitation to the Grand Masquerade might draw them out, resulting in a showdown during that event—and potentially attracting the ire of [Duchess d'Honaire](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/saidra-dhonaire-rhw.md).  

#### The Grand Masquerade

*Adventure for Level 4 Characters*

- **Situation.** The Grand Masquerade is an opportunity for characters to meet Dementlieuse nobles and gain information they can't otherwise access.  
- **Hook.** The date of the next masquerade is public knowledge. To attend, the characters need to create their own costumes and invitations.  

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.9: D'Honaire Estate](file://book/RHW/072-map-06-02.dhonaire-estate.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/073-map-06-02.dhonaire-estate-player.webp#gallery)

##### Encounters

The adventure uses map 2.9 and consists of these encounters.

###### Dressed to Kill

Attendees at the Grand Masquerade are expected to sport lavish costumes featuring fanciful masks. Any character not wearing an appropriate [Costume](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/costume-xphb.md), a mask, and at least 100 GP worth of jewelry (or appropriate magical alternatives) has [Disadvantage](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/disadvantage-xphb.md) on Charisma checks made during this adventure. Armor can't be worn with a nonmagical costume. If a character becomes [Bloodied](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/conditions.md#Bloodied) while wearing a nonmagical costume, their costume is destroyed.

###### Arrival

At the entrance to the estate, servants check the characters' invitations. A character with a forged invitation must succeed on a DC 10 Charisma ([Deception](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Deception)) check to be admitted. Those who fail are asked to leave. If they refuse, four [Ghouls](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/ghoul-xmm.md) wearing formal wear and masks fight them.

###### Masquerade

The Grand Masquerade unfolds in three tableaux. During each, the characters can decide to dance, gossip, flirt, or do something else. Each character can earn renown for their group with the ball's attendees and host by making positive impressions on other guests (see "chapter 3" of the "Dungeon Master's Guide" for details on renown). Each positive interaction can increase the group's Renown Score by 1 per character per tableau.

Duchess d'Honaire has yet to appear, but hundreds of other costumed nobles mingle during the masquerade. These masked guests might share their names, but a character must succeed on a DC 10 Wisdom ([Perception](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Perception)) check to identify even someone they're familiar with. The following guests pay particular attention to the characters:

**Alexandre du Cire** (Medium [Waxwork](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/construct/waxwork-rhw.md); see chapter 5) poses as a human and runs the House of Wax. He urges the characters to visit his establishment. His costume is a suit on one side and a ball gown on the other. He is [Friendly](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/friendly-attitude-xphb.md).

**Angel Pajaro** (Medium [Werewolf](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/werewolf-xmm.md)) is a famed diva of the Port-a-Lucine opera and is [Hostile](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/hostile-attitude-xphb.md). She likes to humiliate her fans but loves flattery from other performers. She's dressed as an arctic fox.

**Julienne d'Honaire** (Medium, Neutral Good [Bandit](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/bandit-xmm.md)) is a Friendly human. She's bubbly and behaves in an unrefined manner. She claims to be related to the duchess but confides that she wasn't invited. Julienne wears a secondhand ballerina costume.

**Lord Governor Marcel Guignol** (Medium [Noble](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/noble-xmm.md)) is [Indifferent](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/indifferent-attitude-xphb.md) and didn't want to attend the event. The elderly human is jittery and hates loud noises, and he seeks an excuse to leave. He's dressed as a smiling jester.

**Raoul Rameau** (Medium [Guard Captain](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/guard-captain-xmm.md)) is a member of the city watch. He tries to guess who people are and why they've been invited—his hunches are poor. He's dressed as a toy monkey with cymbals.

###### Uncouth Exchange

After the second tableau, two revelers wearing the same costumes as two nearby characters spot their lookalikes. Outraged by this faux pas, these [Berserkers](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/berserker-xmm.md) fight them, wielding sharpened candelabras (these function as [Greataxes](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/greataxe-xphb.md)). If the characters defeat their attackers, their Renown Score increases by 2.

###### The Duchess Appears

After three tableaux, [Saidra d'Honaire](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/saidra-dhonaire-rhw.md) (see earlier in this chapter) appears. She is fabulous and terrible as she drifts over the flattering crowd. Nearing the characters, she halts, gasps in revulsion, and points. "You! Never have I seen such an audaciously incompetent impostor! Who do you think you are to violate these hallowed halls?!" Near a character, Julienne d'Honaire begins to reply, and the duchess instantly disintegrates her. A ghoulish servant soon appears with a dustpan to clean the spot where Julienne stood. If party members spent two or more tableaux with Julienne, the group's Renown Score decreases by 1.

###### Conclusion

If the group's Renown Score is 5 or less, the duchess shrieks, outraged to find more unworthies. Right away, four [Ghoul](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/ghoul-xmm.md) servants appear and fight the characters; two **Ghouls** arrive every round until the party flees the estate. The duchess doesn't fight.

If the characters' Renown Score is at least 6, the duchess compliments one of their costumes as she drifts by in time with the music. If the characters came to the masquerade to meet or influence someone, that individual appears soon after, impressed by the duchess's compliment. Other members of the city's nobility or individuals the characters met earlier in the night also might approach them with invitations or offers of employment. Each character earns a bonus 600 XP.

## Falkovnia

*Domain Besieged by the Dead*

> [!note] 
> 
> - **Darklord.** Vladeska Drakov  
> - **Genre.** Disaster horror  
> - **Hallmarks.** Dwindling resources, impending disaster, suspicion, totalitarianism, zombies  
> - **Mist Talismans.** Correspondence from the capital, Lekar; gear marked with the Blood Falcon; zombie flesh  
> - **Aligned Tarokka Card.** Dictator  
> - **Opposed Tarokka Card.** Executioner  
^14e

> [!gallery]
> ![](file://book/RHW/074-07-001.dictator-tarokka.webp#gallery)
> ![](file://book/RHW/075-07-002.executioner-tarokka.webp#gallery)

Falkovnia is a land besieged. Empty countryside surrounds ruined or crumbling cities. Only a few desperate pockets of civilization survive, carrying on not out of hope, but out of fear of the land's merciless soldiers. Led by [General Vladeska Drakov](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/vladeska-drakov-rhw.md), Falkovnia's military organizes a desperate and occasionally effective defense against an implacable foe: the ever-growing armies of the dead.

Every moon, a new zombie legion emerges from the Mists. Never appearing from the same place twice, the horde sweeps across the land, drawn to the densest populations of the living. That always includes the Falkovnian capital of Lekar, where unfit and underfed conscripts defend crumbling walls alongside General Drakov and her crimson-armored elite soldiers, the Talons. Causalities mount during the zombie sieges, but miracles and moments of desperate valor haven't abandoned Falkovnia. The people's numbers dwindle, but they soldier on.

In the aftermath of a zombie attack, the Falkovnians burn their dead, repair what they can, and whisper that now might be the time to flee the city. Invariably, someone speaks too loudly, and soldiers drag off the so-called traitor to be impaled as an example. The people might want to abandon their homes, but Vladeska Drakov refuses to accept defeat.

### Domain Features

Falkovnia is known for the following features:

- **Army of the Dead.** Every night of the new moon, thousands of ravenous zombies emerge from the Mists to feed on the living.  
- **Capital Punishment.** There is only one punishment for any crime in Falkovnia: impalement.  
- **Rotten Remnants.** Ruins cover Falkovnia—towns and villages crushed by zombie hordes and haunted by undead stragglers.  
- **Talon Soldiers.** Falkovnian soldiers known as Talons patrol the land, hunting for deserters and strangers to press into service. Talon officers bear prominent tattoos of the Blood Falcon, the symbol of Vladeska Drakov.  

### Locations in Falkovnia

Falkovnia is an unnervingly still domain, where people and animals hide to avoid attracting the attention of zombies and Drakov's brutal Talons. The city of Lekar is described below, and other notable locations are summarized on the "Falkovnia Locations table".

#### Lekar

The only city of the living left in Falkovnia, Lekar bears the brunt of the zombie invasion. The city has outgrown its walls multiple times since its founding, leaving its districts divided by fortifications. During the first zombie siege, General Drakov sacrificed the northern River Ward, leaving hundreds of souls to be slaughtered but allowing the remaining defenders to turn back the zombie horde.

Now the city's survivors face harsh conditions. Talon soldiers keep the peace in the cramped slums. Troops lead civilians outside the walls to scavenge from ruins and work the fields of abandoned farms, but their harvests are never enough for the city's survivors. Though bitter and desperate, soldiers live better than civilians, assured of rations and housing in the Bastion Ward—the Talons-only district around General Drakov's command center at Custodian's Hall. From there, Drakov orders daily public executions as conscripts dispense supplies to the suffering masses.

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.10: Falkovnia](file://book/RHW/076-map-07-01.falkovnia.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/077-map-07-01.falkovnia-player.webp#gallery)

![Falkovnia Locations](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/falkovnia-locations-rhw.md)

### Vladeska Drakov

*Darklord Who Wars Against the Dead*

![](file://book/RHW/078-07-003.vladeska-drakov.webp#center)

> [!quote] A quote from Vladeska Drakov  
> 
> If you're reinforcements, I expect you to prove you're worth the gear you're wearing. I need soldiers, not more bait for the undead.

General of a demoralized occupying army, Vladeska Drakov rules what little of Falkovnia hasn't been overrun by the dead. A cunning authoritarian, she believes any tactics—no matter how immoral—are permissible in the pursuit of victory. The Mists torment her by keeping her ever on the edge of defeat, exhausting her and forcing her to watch her precision fail in the face of an endless string of emergencies and an undefeatable enemy horde. Drakov is ever being pushed to the edge. Hunger, sleep deprivation, and the endless demands of terrified troops and civilians drive her toward outbursts of paranoia and violence.

> [!embed-monster]- Vladeska Drakov
> ![Vladeska Drakov](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/vladeska-drakov-rhw.md#^statblock)

#### Drakov's Tale

In the world of her birth, Vladeska Drakov was known as the Crimson Falcon, leader of a peerless mercenary army called the Falcon's Talons. In a land of bitterly feuding royal families, she and her troops executed a thousand ancient grudges and petty atrocities. Drakov amassed a fortune and planned to retire young and buy a title and a realm to rule.

The sacking of Yeivere changed her plans. During that city's razing, Drakov's mercenaries went too far. The Falcon's Talons killed a unique soul during the slaughter. None can say who the soul was—a royal, a saint, a witch, an angel—but with its death, the world turned against them.

The ruling families united to hunt the Talons. Thanks to her tactical genius, Drakov repelled her pursuers and went on the offensive. One by one she attacked her former benefactors, burning villages, pressing citizens into service, and impaling anyone with a drop of noble blood. Over years of work, Drakov forged a bloody empire. But while sacking the burning city of her last remaining foe, Drakov and her troops were engulfed by smoke. When it cleared, everything they knew was gone.

Transported to an unfamiliar land, Drakov and her troops wasted little time subjugating it. This unprepared realm fell quickly, almost willingly. On taking the city of Lekar, Drakov named herself ruler of her new empire: Falkovnia.

However, under a moonless sky, the dead rose against Drakov, claws scraping against Lekar's walls before alarms could be raised. Drakov's brilliant and desperate strategies eventually turned back the zombies during the days-long First Siege of Lekar, but victory came at the cost of most of her veteran troops.

Since then, Drakov has nearly lost her nation. Every moon, a new desperate battle unfolds. She prepares ceaselessly for each one, certain of her ultimate victory but doubtful of her troops' mettle. With threats and public impalings, she keeps her people more terrified of her than of the undead. And with every new moon, she faces an unconquerable foe, never revealing a secret only she knows: that each zombie bears the face of an innocent her soldiers once put to the sword.

![Custodian's Hall rises over the few remaining wards of Lekar that haven't fallen to the zombie hordes](file://book/RHW/079-07-004.custodians-hall.webp#center)

#### Drakov's Domain

Falkovnia is altered by Drakov's presence, creating the following effects:

- **Authoritarian Regime.** Drakov's allies have [Advantage](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/advantage-xphb.md) on Wisdom saving throws.  
- **Closing the Borders.** Drakov can't close or open the borders of her domain. Falkovnia's borders are usually closed, but they open one week every month starting on the night of the new moon.  
- **Endless War.** Whenever a creature other than Drakov or her allies finishes a Long Rest in the domain, roll `dice:1d20|noform|noparens|avg` (`1d20`). On a 1, the creature doesn't remove any [Exhaustion](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/conditions.md#Exhaustion) levels as a result of finishing that rest, and the creature gains 1 Exhaustion level.  

If Drakov dies, these effects end immediately.

#### Drakov's Lair

When she conquered the city, Vladeska Drakov claimed Lekar's seat of governance, Custodian's Hall, as her army's headquarters. Since the First Siege of Lekar, one emergency after another has forced Drakov and her Talon troops to repurpose the building's chambers for military purposes.

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.11: Custodian's Hall](file://book/RHW/080-map-07-02.custodians-hall.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/081-map-07-02.custodians-hall-player.webp#gallery)

##### Custodian's Hall

The polished marble and hopeful mosaics of Custodian's Hall now bear the dirt and scars of invaders' boots and tools of war. The site is depicted on "map 2.11" and has the following features:

- **Chamber of Peers.** The chamber of Lekar's dissolved senate now serves as a command center for Drakov's officers.  
- **Drakov's Chambers.** Drakov has repurposed offices at the heights of Custodian's Hall as her personal chambers. Her bedroom is cold and simple and features little more than a hard cot. Nearby, she maintains a war room full of maps and reports where she obsesses over desperate battle scenarios. Across the hall is a well-used chamber full of torture devices, many of her own design.  
- **Plaza Stairs.** Daily, Talons disseminate meager rations to Lekar's citizens while other soldiers execute supposed traitors by impaling them on pikes.  

### Adventures in Falkovnia

Adventures set in Falkovnia involve zombie hordes, cruel soldiers, and Drakov herself. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

#### Horror in Falkovnia

Adventures in Falkovnia often include the following elements.

##### Zombie March

Zombies emerge from the Mists on the night of the new moon. This surge brings a recurring threat to besiege the walls of Lekar, but it also makes encountering droves of zombies more likely throughout the domain. Use the zombies from chapter 5, the "Monster Manual" or other sources to create surprising and terrifying encounters.

##### The Falcon's Talons

Drakov's military forces are both completely overwhelming and entirely outnumbered. Though relatively few in number, the Talons are organized enough to oppress Falkovnia's survivors and enforce Drakov's totalitarian laws. In the face of zombie hordes, though, the Talons are fighting a losing battle. Talon soldiers are [Warrior Infantry](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/warrior-infantry-xmm.md), while officers are [Warrior Veterans](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/warrior-veteran-xmm.md).

##### Martial Law

Lekar is a martial dictatorship. Drakov's troops carry out example-setting impalings as punishment for even the slightest crimes. These executions impose order through terror and make it clear that zombies aren't the realm's only monsters.

##### Only Bad Choices

There is one simple truth in Falkovnia: The dead are going to kill everyone. This sets the stage for countless bad decisions, from leaders making terrible sacrifices or permitting immoral acts to individuals making fatalistic choices. Locals behave as if it's their last day alive—because it probably is.

##### Trapped with the Dead

Falkovnia's borders are usually closed, and Vladeska Drakov has no control over when they open. Anyone who enters the Mists surrounding Falkovnia encounters endless numbers of zombies. Travelers who somehow avoid these shambling corpses emerge from the Mists back in Falkovnia, pursued by the undead. For one week following the night of the new moon, the Mists are empty of zombies and the borders open. During this time, Drakov sends patrols of Talons to sweep the edges of the Mists for deserters. These patrols are difficult to avoid, and battles with them often attract zombies.

##### Falkovnia Campaign Arc

Falkovnia is one of the few domains where the characters and the Darklord might be on the same side, united against unrelenting hordes of zombies. The characters might try to defend Falkovnia's people alongside Drakov, but as the Darklord's obsession with victory becomes clear, they must balance keeping her trust and upholding their principles. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–4.** The characters save a group of commoners and outmatched Talons from [Zombies](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/zombie-xmm.md). The thankful band takes the characters to Lekar, where people hail them as heroic "Trueborn of Falkovnia." [Vladeska Drakov](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/vladeska-drakov-rhw.md) recruits them to bring scattered pockets of common folk to safety in Lekar.  
- **Levels 5–8.** The characters witness the suffering in Lekar and see some of those they've saved impaled for disloyalty. Rebels entreat them to help smuggle people out of Lekar to hidden encampments in the mountains.  
- **Levels 9–12.** The characters are captured by Talons, but Drakov offers them freedom if they defend the city's southern gate, the Gate of Torches, from the impending zombie siege. Unknown to the characters, Drakov plans to sacrifice the gate as detailed in the "Siege of Lekar" adventure.  

#### Siege of Lekar

*Adventure for Level 9 Characters*

- **Situation.** Zombie hordes attack Lekar. Vladeska Drakov seeks to defeat them by sacrificing the characters and a district of Lekar.  
- **Hook.** The characters are ordered by Drakov or entreated by citizens to defend the Gate of Torches.  

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.12: Lekar Gate](file://book/RHW/082-map-07-03.lekar-gate.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/083-map-07-03.lekar-gate-player.webp#gallery)

##### Lekar Gates

This adventure takes place at a gate in Lekar's southern wall, the Gate of Torches, and a second gate to Lekar's central district, Loyalist's Gate. The Gate of Torches shows the scars of countless zombie claws, but otherwise the gates are identical. Both have the following features:

- **Fortifications.** The walls of Lekar are 30 feet tall, with the gatehouse's towers rising 40 feet. Crenelations atop both provide defenders with [Three-Quarters Cover](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/cover-xphb.md) from beyond the wall.  
- **Gates.** The gatehouse's battle-scarred gates are Huge objects with AC 19, 72 HP, and Immunity to Poison and Psychic damage. Any character adjacent to the mechanism over the gate can open or close the gate in 1 round.  

##### Encounters

These encounters begin at the Gate of Torches, which uses "map 2.12". Characters can position themselves where they please. Describe inexperienced soldiers guarding other posts or zombies beyond the map, but don't track their actions in battle. When you're ready to begin the siege, the Siege Events by Round table outlines what occurs each round. The following sections further detail these events.

**Siege Events by Round**

| Round | Siege Event |
|-------|-------------|
| 1 | Eight [Zombies](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/zombie-xmm.md) and six [Ogre Zombies](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/ogre-zombie-xmm.md) appear. |
| 3 | Four [Ogre Zombies](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/ogre-zombie-xmm.md) and a [Beholder Zombie](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/beholder-zombie-xmm.md) appear. |
| 5 | Two [Zombie Clots](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/zombie-clot-rhw.md) appear. Talons roll a wagon to the gate from the north. |
| 6 | Talons light fuses on the wagon. |
| 7 | Four [Ogre Zombies](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/ogre-zombie-xmm.md) appear. Talons flee. |
| 8 | Wagon explodes (if not prevented). |
| 9 | Explosion (see "Siege Climax"). |
^siege-events-by-round

###### Zombie Attack

Zombies shamble from the south and attack the gatehouse's gates. Rather than having foes make individual attacks on the gates, assume the gates take `dice:4d6|noform|noparens|avg` (`4d6`) damage every time a round ends with a zombie adjacent to them. When reduced to 0 Hit Points, the gate is destroyed. If this occurs, troops flee as detailed in "Siege Climax."

###### Drakov's Talons

Starting on round 5, any character on or behind the walls who succeeds on a DC 12 Wisdom ([Perception](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Perception)) check notices Talons (four [Warrior Veterans](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/warrior-veteran-xmm.md)) behind the gate. The Talons are supposedly allied troops, so this shouldn't cause concern. The Talons behave as detailed on the Siege Events by Round table. They flee if fought.

###### Talon Wagon

This wagon contains kegs of gunpowder. A character adjacent to the wagon who spends a round investigating discovers these explosives. On round 6, any character who has noticed the Talons and is within sight of them sees them setting fuses. If no one prevents the soldiers from lighting the fuses or extinguishes the lit fuses, the wagon explodes at the end of round 8. Creatures within 30 feet of it when it explodes make a DC 12 Dexterity saving throw, taking `dice:12d6|noform|noparens|avg|text(42)` (`12d6`) Fire damage on a failed save or half as much damage on a successful one. The explosion destroys the gatehouse's gate, regardless of its remaining Hit Points.

###### Siege Climax

The siege continues until either the gatehouse's gate is destroyed or the end of round 9. At the end of round 9, an explosion hundreds of feet to the west destroys part of the city wall, and [Zombies](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/zombie-xmm.md) pour into Lekar. Surviving soldiers abandon their posts—it's clear the Gate of Torches will be overrun. These survivors race through the slums to Loyalist's Gate.

###### Loyalist's Gate

Loyalist's Gate is identical to the Gate of Torches and uses "map 2.12: Lekar Gate". When the characters arrive from the south, the gate is closed. Hundreds of surviving soldiers and slum residents scream for the guards to let them through. Talon soldiers (eight [Warrior Infantry](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/warrior-infantry-xmm.md)) and [Vladeska Drakov](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/vladeska-drakov-rhw.md) (see earlier in this chapter) guard the gate. Drakov thanks the panicking assemblage for their sacrifice and reveals her plan to set the slums ablaze once the zombies flood in. The characters can open the gate to admit the crowd using the mechanism in the gatehouse, but Drakov and her troops fight to prevent this.

The characters have 4 rounds before groups of `dice:1d6|noform|noparens|avg` (`1d6`) [Zombies](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/zombie-xmm.md) begin appearing from the south at the end of each round. Narrate these zombies attacking the crowd, but don't track the crowd's Hit Points. If the characters open the gate before the zombies appear, each of them earns 5,900 bonus XP.

###### Drakov's Defeat

If Drakov is defeated, Falkovnia's borders open, and no zombies appear from the Mists for several moons. Some people rebuild, others flee into the Mists. After this time, though, Drakov reappears and slowly retakes control of Falkovnia. The borders close, and zombies return soon afterward.

## Har'Akir

*Domain of the Ancient Dead*

> [!note] 
> 
> - **Darklord.** Ankhtepot  
> - **Genre.** Dark fantasy  
> - **Hallmarks.** Ancient tombs, desert perils, lost gods, mummies  
> - **Mist Talismans.** Canopic jar, lapis lazuli scarab, scroll of hieroglyphics  
> - **Aligned Tarokka Card.** Monk  
> - **Opposed Tarokka Card.** Raven  
^169

> [!gallery]
> ![](file://book/RHW/084-08-001.monk-tarokka.webp#gallery)
> ![](file://book/RHW/085-08-002.raven-tarokka.webp#gallery)

Untold generations of tombs and monuments choke on the obsidian sands of the desert domain of Har'Akir. Here, past splendors lie forgotten, and the living bow in service to the mummified god-king, [Ankhtepot](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ankhtepot-rhw.md).

From a golden pyramid in the City of the Dead, Ankhtepot reigns as speaker for the gods and immortal pharaoh. The deathless ruler cares nothing for his domain or mortal concerns. Rather, he relentlessly sends servants in search of his one desire: his ka, the missing piece of his fractured soul.

As the pharaoh obsesses over his lost soul, his servants plague the domain in his name. In hidden tomb-courts, mummies known as the Children of Ankhtepot dominate cults as emissaries of mysterious gods. And in the mud-brick city of Muhar, Ankhtepot's priests oversee all aspects of life, apportioning food to the worthy and punishing blasphemers. But all the pharaoh's servants also pursue the Darklord's quest for his mysterious ka, though only his Children know the truth of this "treasure" he seeks. Each of them is desperate for some clue to placate Ankhtepot and spare them from his wrath.

### Domain Features

Har'Akir is known for the following features:

- **Distant Pharaoh.** The people of Har'Akir know their ruler is an immortal who resides in the golden mountain called Pharaoh's Rest. Only priests can enter this massive pyramid.  
- **Extreme Environs.** [Intense heat](3-Mechanics/CLI/traps-hazards/extreme-heat-xdmg.md) and [winds](3-Mechanics/CLI/traps-hazards/strong-wind-xdmg.md) are common in Har'Akir (see the "Dungeon Master's Guide"), and water is scarce.  
- **Forgotten Ruins.** The deserts of Har'Akir are littered with the remnants of a strange and glorious empire. The origins of these ruins remain a mystery.  
- **Mysterious Gods.** Har'Akir's people worship a pantheon of false or silent gods. Manipulative or deluded priests oversee all aspects of society in these gods' and the pharaoh's names.  
- **Preserved Dead.** Akirrans mummify their dead so the pharaoh might call them to service. It is a crime to burn the dead.  

### Locations in Har'Akir

Har'Akir is dominated by treacherous, surreal deserts that obey Ankhtepot's will. The Labyrinth and city of Muhar are described below, and other notable locations are summarized on the "Har'Akir Locations table".

#### Labyrinth

Har'Akir's countless trap-laden ruins interconnect beneath the desert in a hidden maze called the Labyrinth. Monstrous [Mummies](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/mummy-xmm.md) and stranger creatures stalk these sprawling tunnels. Nevertheless, some priests use the few mapped sections to move about the domain unseen.

#### Muhar

The city of Muhar is the only permanent settlement in Har'Akir. Here, pious people thank the gods for the water and food of the Muhar Oasis. From the city's largest structure, the Temple of Ese, High Priest Isu Rehkotep speaks for Pharaoh Ankhtepot in all matters; her word is considered both royal decree and divine edict. Ankhtepot doesn't care how Isu runs Muhar so long as she maintains order and uses her influence to continue his unending search. Those who displease Isu or oppose her priest-guards are thrown into the Mouth of Oru, a pit that connects to the Labyrinth.

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.13: Har'Akir](file://book/RHW/086-map-08-01.harakir.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/087-map-08-01.harakir-player.webp#gallery)

![Har'Akir Locations](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/harakir-locations-rhw.md)

### Ankhtepot

*Darklord Who Pursues Death*

![](file://book/RHW/088-08-003.ankhtepot.webp#center)

> [!quote] A quote from Ankhtepot  
> 
> Bow before the pharaoh—whether as a servant or as dust.

Ankhtepot has known treachery and conquest. He has known divinity and rule. But now he knows simply boredom and despair. He desires only to recover his lost ka, which he knows lies hidden in Har'Akir. With it, he hopes to become mortal again, die, and face his gods' judgment. Whether this means peace or oblivion matters not to him. Ankhtepot seeks only an end, and he and his followers will be a plague on Har'Akir until he finds it.

> [!embed-monster]- Ankhtepot
> ![Ankhtepot](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ankhtepot-rhw.md#^statblock)

#### Ankhtepot's Tale

In a nation called the Land of Reeds and Lotuses, Ankhtepot served the royal family as high priest. As old pharaohs died and new ones rose, the influential priest came to believe that the gods wanted a wiser leader to rule. On the day of a new pharaoh's ascension, Ankhtepot rallied his priests and murdered their liege. But he had misjudged the people's will, and an outraged mob rose up and executed the traitorous priests.

Moreover, Ankhtepot had misjudged the will of the gods. As he stood before them in death, the immortals forsook him, cursing him and denying him entry to the afterlife. They returned him to the world but stripped away a piece of his soul, his ka—the vital essence that inspires all living beings.

Ankhtepot awoke, trapped within his corpse, as he was mummified along with his treacherous followers. Untold centuries passed, but on the day the last memory of Ankhtepot faded from the Land of Reeds and Lotuses, the high priest's bindings rotted away, and Ankhtepot crawled forth from his sarcophagus. He emerged from his tomb in an unfamiliar land: Har'Akir.

In this new land, Ankhtepot found a pious people devoted to the same gods he once served. Over generations, he wiped out that religion, replacing it with false divinities of his own imagining for whom he alone could speak. Ankhtepot also resurrected the priests buried alongside him as [mummy lords](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/mummy-lord-xmm.md), replacing their heads with those of beasts and monsters holy to his new faith. These Children of Ankhtepot served him as they did in life, and together the dead conquered the souls of Har'Akir.

In the ages since, Ankhtepot hasn't forged the land of his ambitions. His servants scheme against him, his people don't flourish, and his monuments crumble to dust in mere centuries. Ankhtepot's ambitions have withered. Now he seeks only to reclaim his soul and use it to put an end to his accursed immortality.

#### Ankhtepot's Domain

Har'Akir is altered by Ankhtepot's presence, creating the following effects:

- **Blistering Sun.** Any outdoor area of [Bright Light](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/bright-light-xphb.md) in Har'Akir is an area of [extreme heat](3-Mechanics/CLI/traps-hazards/extreme-heat-xdmg.md) (see the "Dungeon Master's Guide").  
- **Closing the Borders.** While in his domain, Ankhtepot can close or open the borders to Har'Akir at will. While the borders are closed, whirling sands fill the Mists surrounding Har'Akir. A creature that enters the Mists for the first time on a turn or starts its turn there takes `dice:2d6|noform|noparens|avg` (`2d6`) Slashing damage.  
- **Control Undead.** Undead of CR 5 or lower in Har'Akir have the [Charmed](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/conditions.md#Charmed) condition and obey Ankhtepot's orders.  

If Ankhtepot dies, these effects end immediately.

#### Ankhtepot's Lair

A mountain-size black pyramid, Ankhtepot's tomb—called Pharaoh's Rest—looms over the City of the Dead. It can be seen from all across Har'Akir.

##### Pharaoh's Rest Features

Ancient and ornate, Pharaoh's Rest holds countless carvings of mysterious deities and Ankhtepot as an idealized pharaoh. A labyrinth of trapped tombs, embalming rooms, and treasure chambers fills the majority of this massive pyramid. Broad paths used by Ankhtepot's servants lead past deadly side passages to the heights of the monument. Prominent locations are depicted on "map 2.14" and have the following features:

- **Ankhtepot's Tomb.** The burial treasures and reliefs lining Ankhtepot's tomb's walls are shattered, having suffered ages of Ankhtepot's frustration. Hidden behind a bejeweled throne is a thoroughly defaced sarcophagus. Within, Ankhtepot awaits word of his ka's discovery, rising only when disturbed by trespassers or at the call of servants from the funeral barge chamber below.  
- **Funeral Barge.** Ankhtepot envisions his trip to the afterlife taking place on a river. In an ornate ritual site, he has prepared a funeral barge and other ceremonial trappings necessary for his journey after his ka's recovery.  
- **Lesser Tombs.** Throughout the pyramid are shrines, mummification chambers, and the crypts of Ankhtepot's servants. These include the burial chambers of several Children of Ankhtepot and the Darklord's son, Thutepot.  
- **Shrine of Ankhtepot.** A vast, open shrine holds ominous statues of Har'Akir's gods and columns etched with exaggerated and fictitious events from Ankhtepot's rule. On the night of the full moon, a hidden magical elevator activates, granting access to the tombs above.  

### Adventures in Har'Akir

Adventures set in Har'Akir involve ancient secrets, manipulative cultists, the ancient dead, and the search for Ankhtepot's missing ka. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

![From the Temple of Ese, the priests of Pharaoh Ankhtepot control the people of Muhar](file://book/RHW/089-08-004.temple-of-ese.webp#center)

#### Horror in Har'Akir

Adventures in Har'Akir often include the following elements.

##### Children of Ankhtepot

Ankhtepot resurrected the priests who died alongside him as [Mummy Lords](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/mummy-lord-xmm.md), granting each the head of an animal or monster corresponding to the fictitious gods he imposed on Har'Akir. The Children of Ankhtepot style themselves as harbingers of these gods while they manipulate cults or the domain's priesthood. Some have grown tired of Ankhtepot's detachment and seek to depose the pharaoh—particularly the treacherous mummy lord Senmet.

##### Gods of Har'Akir

Ankhtepot has destroyed all evidence of the deities the people of Har'Akir worshipped in ages past, replacing that pantheon with gods of his own creation, as summarized on the Gods of Har'Akir table.

![Gods of Har'Akir](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/gods-of-harakir-rhw.md)

##### Pharaoh's Priests

The priests of Har'Akir work Ankhtepot's will, not realizing their deities are false. They keep alert for strangers and omens related to the treasure their pharaoh covets without knowing its true nature. Promising strangers are brought to High Priest Isu Rehkotep at the Temple of Ese in Muhar. The decadent high priest wants to possess what her pharaoh seeks, planning to use it to manipulate Ankhtepot.

##### Pharaoh's Soul

Ankhtepot seeks his ka, the missing piece of his soul. It's up to you what form this takes. Roll on or choose a result from The Darklord's Soul table to determine the form of Ankhtepot's ka.

**The Darklord's Soul**

`dice: [](3-chapter-2-domains-of-ravenloft.md#^the-darklords-soul)`

| dice: 1d8 | Ankhtepot's Ka Is... |
|-----------|----------------------|
| 1 | An ankh holy to the old gods of Har'Akir. |
| 2 | A blessing granted to those who survive trials within the domain's endless sandstorms. |
| 3 | A canopic jar containing the pharaoh's heart hidden within a forgotten tomb. |
| 4 | A hawk or giant eagle that circles the sun. |
| 5 | Manifested in a joyous song sung by Muhar's people. |
| 6 | Pieces of a jewel hidden within each of the Children of Ankhtepot. |
| 7 | The soul of a character, perhaps one with the [Echoing Soul](3-Mechanics/CLI/feats/echoing-soul-rhw.md) feat. |
| 8 | The spirit of an innocent healer who resembles the pharaoh as he was in life. |
^the-darklords-soul

Once the Darklord recovers his ka, Ankhtepot can restore his soul by completing an elaborate 1-hour ritual involving the sacrifice of a living person. Only then might he journey to the afterlife—whether he succeeds is up to the Dark Powers.

![Frightful monuments such as Ousa's Pyramid rise from the haunted, black-sand deserts of Har'Akir](file://book/RHW/090-08-005.ousas-pyramid.webp#center)

#### Har'Akir Campaign Arc

Campaigns set in Har'Akir often involve the domain's treacherous priests, its ancient tombs, and the hunt for Ankhtepot's ka. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–4.** The characters help a priest named Basras search a trap-laden, buried palace complex for a mysterious treasure. Within, they discover a set of oversize canopic jars. They take them to Isu Rehkotep in Muhar, but the high priest deems them worthless. Basras is thrown into the Mouth of Oru.  
- **Levels 5–10.** Isu Rehkotep hires the characters to search for the pharaoh's missing treasure. She sends them to Senmet's Tomb to recover an ark full of ancient scrolls, claiming these are what the pharaoh desires. (She doesn't actually know the object of the pharaoh's search.)  
- **Levels 11–15.** After the characters return the scrolls to Isu, Basras (now an Undead), reveals that the high priest seeks to use them to control a [Mummy Lord](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/mummy-lord-xmm.md) and oppose Ankhtepot, as detailed in the "Scrolls of the Dead" adventure.  

#### Scrolls of the Dead

*Adventure for Level 12 Characters*

- **Situation.** High Priest Isu Rehkotep claims to have found the treasure Ankhtepot has been searching for and prepares to offer it to him during a ritual at the pyramid of Pharaoh's Rest. In truth, she plans to use a scroll that controls the Child of Ankhtepot called Senmet to destroy the pharaoh and claim his throne.  
- **Hook.** The priest De'rah fears the pharaoh will vent his wrath on the people of Muhar when the high priest is discovered. She offers the characters 5,000 GP and a random magic item from the [Relics—Rare table](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/relics-rare-xdmg.md) in the "Dungeon Master's Guide" if they stop Isu.  

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.14: Pharaoh's Rest](file://book/RHW/091-map-08-02.pharohs-rest.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/092-map-08-02.pharohs-rest-player.webp#gallery)

##### Encounters

This adventure uses map 2.14 and consists of these encounters.

###### Exploring the Pyramid

Rehkotep's ritual takes place during the full moon, when the entrance to Pharaoh's Rest stands open. Pharaoh's Rest is a vast structure, but the path Rehkotep and her followers followed through the thick dust and sand of the lower reaches is obvious. Details of the pyramid's lower levels are beyond the scope of this adventure.

###### Pyramid Heights

When the characters reach the Shrine of Ankhtepot in the upper levels of Pharaoh's Rest, and when they enter the Lesser Tombs, roll on the following table to determine what lurks within.

`dice: [](3-chapter-2-domains-of-ravenloft.md#^1-encounter)`

| dice: 1d6 | Encounter |
|-----------|-----------|
| 1 | A [Dao](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/elemental/dao-xmm.md) compelled to defend the pyramid |
| 2 | Three [Invisible Stalkers](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/elemental/invisible-stalker-xmm.md) that chant curses |
| 3 | Four [Mummies](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/mummy-xmm.md) and two [Death Dogs](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/death-dog-xmm.md) |
| 4 | Two [Mummies](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/mummy-xmm.md) and two [Shield Guardians](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/construct/shield-guardian-xmm.md) |
| 5 | Two [Stone Golems](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/construct/stone-golem-xmm.md) dressed as pharaohs |
| 6 | Four [Wraiths](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/wraith-xmm.md) made of black sand |
^1-encounter

###### Ritual Site

On the funeral barge level of the pyramid, Isu Rehkotep (Medium, Lawful Evil [Archpriest](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/archpriest-xmm.md)) readies to call forth Ankhtepot from his tomb using a ritual involving a gong on the ceremonial ship. Meanwhile, two [Priests](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/priest-xmm.md) and two [Death Cultists](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/death-cultist-xmm.md) defend her. Isu avoids battle, but if any of her allies fall, she produces an ancient papyrus scroll and reads it, summoning Senmet.

###### The Mummy

If Isu reads her scroll, 1 round after her allies are defeated, the [Mummy Lord](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/mummy-lord-xmm.md) Senmet appears. Isu orders him to destroy the characters, and he obeys. Senmet fights until he or the scroll the high priest holds is destroyed. Isu doesn't join the battle and attempts to escape if Senmet is destroyed.

###### The Scroll

A character adjacent to Isu can steal the scroll from her by succeeding on a DC 16 Dexterity ([Sleight of Hand](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Sleight%20of%20Hand)) check or by taking an action if she has the [Incapacitated](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/conditions.md#Incapacitated) or [Restrained](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/conditions.md#Restrained) condition. Any character can take an action to destroy the scroll but can't use it to command Senmet. If it is destroyed, Senmet turns [Hostile](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/hostile-attitude-xphb.md) toward Isu.

###### The Pharaoh

Once Isu and Senmet are dealt with, [Ankhtepot](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ankhtepot-rhw.md) (see earlier in this chapter) appears at the path leading up to his tomb. He demands the characters depart immediately but return with his missing ka. If they do so, fabulous riches will be theirs. If they don't, they will know his wrath. Characters who escape the tomb after the encounter with Ankhtepot earn a bonus 4,700 XP.

## Hazlan

*Domain Doomed by Magic*

> [!note] 
> 
> - **Darklord.** Hazlik  
> - **Genres.** Dark fantasy and disaster horror  
> - **Hallmarks.** Amoral spellcasters, magical experiments, magic-ravaged environment, wild magic  
> - **Mist Talismans.** Eye of Hazlik amulet, gremishka foot, scrap from a red robe  
> - **Aligned Tarokka Card.** Diviner  
> - **Opposed Tarokka Card.** Ghost  
^183

> [!gallery]
> ![](file://book/RHW/093-09-001.diviner-tarokka.webp#gallery)
> ![](file://book/RHW/094-09-002.ghost-tarokka.webp#gallery)

Hazlan is a domain drained of vitality, frayed by magical disasters, and overrun with abominations. Here the amoral, spellcasting elite have so exploited magic that it's turned erratic and dangerous to use.

Encouraging these magical abuses is [Hazlik](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/hazlik-rhw.md), the domain's zulkir, a title meaning wizard-overlord. The Darklord postures as the domain's most powerful wizard and views all others as either apprentices or test subjects. All the while, Hazlik hides the fact that he's lost the ability to learn new magic. Paranoid and controlling, Hazlik constantly spies on those in his domain through the Eyes of Hazlik. These pervasive, eye-shaped symbols appear on structures, decorations, clothing, and individuals across the domain—and through these eyes, the Darklord watches. Hazlik surveils his domain endlessly, reveling in the fear of his people, encouraging rivalries between his apprentices, and searching for magical innovations he can claim as his own.

### Domain Features

Hazlan is known for the following features:

- **Eye of Hazlik.** Inhabitants claim the eyelike design called the Eye of Hazlik bears Hazlik's blessing and wards off dangerous magic. In truth, the symbol is a sensor for Hazlik's magical surveillance.  
- **Magocracy.** The wizard Hazlik rules Hazlan. His apprentices have free rein to exploit the land and its people to further their magical experiments.  
- **Shattered by Magic.** The effects of magical disasters disfigure the domain, poisoning rivers with alchemical runoff, scarring the land with magical blasts, and unleashing unpredictable hazards.  
- **Wild Magic.** Magic is unreliable in Hazlan, resulting in dangerous side effects (see "Hazlan Wild Magic").  

### Locations in Hazlan

Magical disasters and supernatural environments make Hazlan's arid landscape even deadlier and its natural rock monuments even stranger. The settlements of Sly-Var and Toyalis are described below, and other notable locations are summarized on the "Hazlan Locations table".

#### Sly-Var

In Sly-Var, mages obsessed with earning the Darklord's favor raise architecturally discordant towers that defy physical laws. The residents magically create whatever they need, resulting in little need for trade. This leaves the labyrinthine streets and knotted bridges between intertwined compounds eerily empty. The few common folk who traverse these surreal streets often disappear—the victims of magical guardians or of wizards who see the magically deficient as stock for their experiments.

#### Toyalis

The largest town in Hazlan, Toyalis boasts a population of poor, hardworking commoners united by terror of the domain's magic-using elite. Colorful depictions of magical creatures, arcane symbols, and the Eye of Hazlik cover the town's rough wooden and adobe structures. Every few weeks, one of Hazlik's apprentices leads a procession of attendants and magical wonders to Toyalis in search of replacement servants, new apprentices, or stock for magical experiments. A carnival atmosphere ensues, with the apprentice displaying their magical accomplishments and setting up competitions to assess the locals' capabilities—magical or otherwise. When a mage's procession leaves, it takes townsfolk deemed valuable with it.

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.15: Hazlan](file://book/RHW/095-map-09-01.hazlan.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/096-map-09-01.hazlan-player.webp#gallery)

![Hazlan Locations](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/hazlan-locations-rhw.md)

### Hazlik

*Darklord of Desperation and Magical Disaster*

![](file://book/RHW/097-09-003.hazlik.webp#center)

> [!quote] A quote from Hazlik  
> 
> You're new, I can tell. Impress me, and maybe I'll let you be my newest apprentice.

The paranoid, egomaniacal archmage Hazlik clings to his power despite his magical ambitions being supernaturally smothered. Since Hazlik entered Hazlan, his magic has become unstable. Spells he casts behave erratically and fade swiftly—most lasting no more than an hour—while his magical creations fall apart in about a day. The idea of others learning this terrifies the Darklord, which leads him to claim others' works as his own, spy on potential rivals, and order reckless research into the nature of magic and his domain.

Hazlik suffers vivid nightmares wherein past rivals taunt and torment him. The Darklord avoids sleeping, employing magical tinctures to stay awake, but this causes him to vacillate between bouts of exhaustion, jitters, and paranoia.

Hazlik knows that his domain is being ripped apart by magical disasters—many of his own creation. He openly denies the realm's devastation, though, his fear of cascading ruin clashing with his inability to admit he's wrong.

> [!embed-monster]- Hazlik
> ![Hazlik](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/hazlik-rhw.md#^statblock)

#### Hazlik's Tale

On the world of Toril, Hazlik rose among the ranks of the merciless Red Wizards of Thay. Arrogant and convinced mortality was a weakness, he sought hidden truths of magic, ways to visit realms within the psyche, and command of reality.

As Hazlik's power increased, he developed rivalries with other Red Wizards, many of which ended with his foes magically scarred. But one rival Hazlik couldn't defeat: the wizard Indreficus. Hazlik gradually came to obsess over Indreficus, viewing him as his only worthy opponent. Indreficus shared Hazlik's genius and arrogance, and they spent seasons as vicious adversaries and passionate lovers. They drove one another to feats of magical brilliance both revolutionary and unspeakable. This culminated when Hazlik discovered that Indreficus planned to betray Hazlik to garner the favor of Thay's ruling zulkirs. Heartbroken and enraged, Hazlik captured Indreficus and subjected him to nightmarish magical manipulations that permanently transformed him into a pain-wracked, living magical portal. Hazlik presented his creation to the zulkirs, hoping to gain their patronage

The zulkirs revealed that Indreficus hadn't betrayed Hazlik. Rather, the ruling mages had watched the pair's ascent and, wary of their ambitions, undermined them before they became threats. Moreover, they deemed Hazlik's transformation of Indreficus an abomination. As punishment, the zulkirs decreed that every mage Hazlik had scarred could do the same in return to him, marking him with their personal symbols. As the first brand-wielding member of the mob of Hazlik's rivals closed on the wizard, Hazlik fled through the groaning portal that was Indreficus.

Hazlik emerged amid the pain-wracked dreamscapes of Indreficus. Unwittingly, Hazlik had entered the Domain of Dread known as the Nightmare Lands, where Indreficus's shrieking and condemnation hounded him. After months of torment, Hazlik escaped into the Mists and eventually emerged into a realm that knew nothing of magic. His Thayan tattoos had turned gold and warped into symbols meaning "traitor." Undaunted, Hazlik used his magic to dominate the people of this new realm, claiming the title of zulkir and dubbing his realm Hazlan.

#### Hazlik's Domain

Hazlan is altered by Hazlik's presence, creating the following effects:

- **Closing the Borders.** While in his domain, Hazlik can close or open the borders to Hazlan at will. While the borders are closed, the Mists surrounding Hazlan are filled with monstrous magical experiments. A creature that enters the Mists for the first time on a turn or starts its turn there must succeed on a DC 15 Dexterity saving throw or take `dice:1d10|noform|noparens|avg|text(5)` (`1d10`) Force damage and have the [Restrained](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/conditions.md#Restrained) condition until the start of its next turn. A creature makes this save only once per turn.  
- **Frayed Magic.** Whenever a creature (excluding Hazlik and his allies) casts a spell using a level 5+ spell slot, it rolls on the [Wild Magic Surge table](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/wild-magic-surge-xphb.md) in the "Player's Handbook" to create a magical effect.  
- **Magic Nightmares.** While in his lair, Veneficus, Hazlik can cast [Clairvoyance](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/clairvoyance-xphb.md), requiring no spell components and using the same spellcasting ability as his Spellcasting action. When the spell is cast this way, its range is all of Hazlan, Hazlik can see but can't hear through the sensor, and the sensor can appear only on an Eye of Hazlik.  

If [Hazlik](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/hazlik-rhw.md) dies, these effects end immediately. The effects resume if Hazlik gains a new body (see his Darklord Restoration trait).

#### Hazlik's Lair

Hazlik's crimson-towered palace, Veneficus, stands atop the jagged mesa called the Red Rise. The Darklord is attended by a staff of magical creations and his most accomplished apprentices.

##### Veneficus Features

Veneficus is littered with frivolous magic effects and magic items that no longer keep Hazlik's attention. The site is depicted on "map 2.16" and has the following features:

- **Halls of Triumph.** Multiple audience chambers, display galleries, and pleasure gardens rival one another in decadence, each exhibiting grotesque artwork and trophies of Hazlik's achievements.  
- **House of Solitude.** The secluded House of Solitude is magically locked, and Hazlik forbids anyone from entering. At night, muffled screams and flickering lights emanate from within.  
- **Red Tower.** Hazlik's personal chambers fill the Red Tower. Magical portals connect the untold numbers of demiplanar chambers that make up the tower. Somewhere within lies Hazlik's orrery, a multistory magical device that allows the Darklord to see through any Eye of Hazlik in the domain.  

### Adventures in Hazlan

Tales in Hazlan involve radical magical experiments, supernatural environments, rivalries between mages, and magical surveillance. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

![The Eye of Hazlik watches the city of Sly-Var and the approaching retinue of one of the Darklord's apprentices](file://book/RHW/098-09-004.eye-of-hazlik.webp#center)

#### Horror in Hazlan

Adventures set in Hazlan often include the following elements.

##### Eyes of Hazlik

Hazlik spies on his domain's inhabitants using the Eye of Hazlik. This eyelike sigil adorns buildings, clothing, talismans, and creatures across the domain. Locals claim the symbol protects them from dangerous magic and creatures. Hazlik uses the eyes to spy on useful or threatening mages and to reinforce his reputation as an ever-present overlord.

Hazlik often sends loyal apprentices or magical creatures to capture those whose behavior witnessed through the eyes offended him. He turns such individuals into fodder for experimentation in Sly-Var or Veneficus.

##### Hazlan Wild Magic

As a result of unchecked arcane experimentation, magic functions erratically in Hazlan. Whenever a creature in Hazlan expends a spell slot to cast a spell or activates a magic item, it rolls `dice:1d10|noform|noparens|avg` (`1d10`). On a 1, it unleashes a random magical effect. Roll on the [Wild Magic Surge table](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/wild-magic-surge-xphb.md) in chapter 3 of the "Player's Handbook" to determine the effect. Consider describing these results in unsettling ways that don't change their effects, as in these examples:

- Summoned creatures use the proscribed stat blocks but are cosmetically warped to resemble undead or aberrant creatures.  
- Effects that teleport the caster relocate the caster into a misty expanse full of threatening shapes.  
- Effects on creatures cause unsettling sensations, such as the feeling of earwigs wriggling beneath one's skin or one's teeth struggling free.  

Anyone who openly wears an Eye of Hazlik can choose not to roll on the Wild Magic Surge table in this way once per day.

##### Hazlik's Apprentices

Dozens of mages serve as Hazlik's apprentices. Between infrequent, demeaning group lessons with the Darklord, these apprentices pit themselves against one another to impress Hazlik by pushing the boundaries of magical innovation. Those who gain Hazlik's favor are promised arcane secrets known only to the Darklord—secrets that might not exist. This creates a cadre of Hazlani mages who recklessly seek to impress Hazlik by the following means, among others:

- Changing the nature of reality to suit their whims  
- Creating monuments in Hazlik's honor  
- Devising new magic items, spells, or supernatural materials  
- Forging unique magical servants for Hazlik  
- Stealing rare magic items  
- Unleashing dramatic displays of magical might  

Hazlik's current favorite apprentices include the masked wizard Yhal the Skygazer, the shadow-cloaked Ruzelo, and the daring genius Eleni.

#### Hazlan Campaign Arc

Campaigns set in Hazlan often involve mages abusing their power to garner Hazlik's fickle favor. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–3.** The characters arrive in Toyalis, where servants of the mage Khrinitov abduct locals with supposed psychic potential. Eleni, an apprentice of Hazlik, believes Khrinitov's experiments are pointless. She hires the characters to rescue the villagers from Khrinitov's tower amid the Orbitoclasts. In doing so, the characters reveal Khrinitov to be an [Intellect Devourer](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/aberration/intellect-devourer-xmm.md), a [Brain in a Jar](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/brain-in-a-jar-rhw.md) (see chapter 5), or another aberrant being.  
- **Levels 4–8.** Eleni reveals that she's trying to undermine Hazlik and protect the people of Hazlan. She tells the characters of a magic mineral in the Mound of the Worm that [Purple Worms](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/purple-worm-xmm.md) pursue. She encourages the party to collect the mineral and use the purple worms to destroy locations like the Marks. As the characters do so, they face magical guardians and hazards. During their travel, they're exposed to strange magic and might gain Dark Gift feats (see chapter 1).  
- **Levels 9–12.** Eleni asks the characters to come to Sly-Var to plan a raid on Hazlik's palace. There, she reveals that she's been exposing them to dangerous magic from across the domain. She entraps them with a portal that leads to arena-like laboratories connected to Veneficus, where [Hazlik](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/hazlik-rhw.md) pits them against terrors his other apprentices have created. The characters must escape, potentially facing Eleni and Hazlik along the way.  

#### Eyes of the Darklord

*Adventure for Level 10 Characters*

- **Situation.** Subjects of magical experimentation seek to escape Hazlan, but every time they try, they're spotted through the Eyes of Hazlik, and the Darklord's apprentices hunt them down.  
- **Hook.** Allies hire the characters to help them escape Hazlan by destroying Hazlik's orrery in Veneficus. They offer to pay the party 4,000 GP once they're guided to another domain.  

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.16: Veneficus](file://book/RHW/099-map-09-02.veneficus.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/100-map-09-02.veneficus-player.webp#gallery)

##### Encounters

The adventure uses map 2.16 and consists of these encounters:

###### Greeting at Veneficus

The rooms within Veneficus (see map 2.16) and the walls outside all bear at least one Eye of Hazlik. If the characters are spotted, one of Hazlik's former apprentices (Medium, Chaotic Evil [Archmage](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/archmage-xmm.md)) appears. This apprentice has been transformed to look and behave like the Darklord. The duplicate belittles the characters and fights to the death.

###### Galleries of Suffering

As the characters explore Veneficus, roll on the following table to determine what they find within.

`dice: [](3-chapter-2-domains-of-ravenloft.md#^1-encounter)`

| dice: 1d6 | Encounter |
|-----------|-----------|
| 1 | Another [Archmage](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/archmage-xmm.md) that behaves like Hazlik (see above), or a similarly disguised [Incubus](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fiend/incubus-xmm.md) |
| 2 | Artwork that releases a [Bone Devil](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fiend/bone-devil-xmm.md) if touched |
| 3 | Three [Mages](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/mage-xmm.md) arguing about who's greatest |
| 4 | Three [Waxworks](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/construct/waxwork-rhw.md) (see chapter 5) disguised as mages arguing about who's Hazlik's favorite |
| 5 | One [Stone Golem](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/construct/stone-golem-xmm.md) sculpted to look like Hazlik |
| 6 | Flawed Magic (see below) |
^1-encounter

###### Flawed Magic

Among mundane decorations, this room contains a random magic item. Roll on the [Arcana—Common table](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/arcana-common-xdmg.md) in chapter 7 of the "Dungeon Master's Guide". The item functions once, causes a wild magic surge (see "Hazlan Wild Magic"), and then crumbles to dust.

###### Red Tower

Shifting portals connect the passages in the Red Tower. Every time the characters pass through a portal in the tower, roll `dice:1d8|noform|noparens|avg` (`1d8`). If the number rolled is lower than the number of portals passed through, the characters arrive in the orrery chamber. On an 8, the characters appear at the entrance to Veneficus.

###### Orrery Chamber

This room is dominated by a magical orrery only Hazlik can use. It is defended by a [Relentless Juggernaut](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fiend/relentless-juggernaut-rhw.md). The orrery has AC 19, HP 25, and Immunity to Psychic damage. Every time the orrery takes damage, roll on the [Wild Magic Surge table](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/wild-magic-surge-xphb.md) in chapter 3 of the "Player's Handbook". Negative effects affect the character who damaged the orrery, while beneficial effects affect the juggernaut.

###### Hazlik

After the orrery is destroyed, [Hazlik](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/hazlik-rhw.md) (see earlier in this chapter) appears and offers a magic-using character power and influence as his apprentice. If the character accepts, he commands that character to murder the others. If the character declines, Hazlik mocks the party. The Darklord uses magic to flee if he takes any damage, swearing revenge. Characters who destroy the orrery and escape Veneficus earn a bonus 3,100 XP.

## Innsmouth

*Domain of the Imprisoned Apocalyptic*

> [!note] 
> 
> - **Darklord.** Cthulhu  
> - **Genre.** Cosmic horror  
> - **Hallmarks.** Cosmic horror creatures, invasive alien dreams, surreal locations, warring cults  
> - **Mist Talismans.** Effigy of Great Cthulhu, starmetal rod or amulet with eldritch runes, sahuagin-tooth fishing lure  
> - **Aligned Tarokka Card.** Bishop  
> - **Opposed Tarokka Card.** Donjon  
^19c

> [!gallery]
> ![](file://book/RHW/101-10-001.bishop-tarokka.webp#gallery)
> ![](file://book/RHW/102-10-002.donjon-tarokka.webp#gallery)

Hidden amid the Domains of Dread lies a hideous realm defiant of reason and smothered by the Mists. From a violent, murky sea rises a crescent of shattered peaks, mangled spires broken like the jaws of some slain thalassic titan. From noxious fumaroles, miasmic pillars lurch from this accursed isle into a sky inconsistently lit by a distant, drowned light.

Strange ruins dot this island's rocky coasts, some suggestive of forgotten peoples, others alien in form and purpose. Massive statues of crimson-flecked bloodstone loom over sheer cliffs, each a towering effigy of some profane monstrosity or alien god. One shore bears the wreckage of a few dozen collapsing wooden structures. Little evidence remains of this settlement's residents, but at its edge lies a toppled sign bearing a word in Common that gives the island its name: Innsmouth.

Despite its forsaken appearance, the isle of Innsmouth isn't abandoned. Cults vie for control of the island, among them the servants of Great Cthulhu, a harbinger of world-rending aberrance. At the island's hidden heart, [Cthulhu](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/cthulhu-rhw.md) lies dreaming, its alien mind reaching across the Domains of Dread and beyond, drawing to it those who might rouse its full might and unleash it from its prison in the Mists.

### Domain Features

Innsmouth is known for the following features:

- **Cosmic Horror Visions.** Cthulhu's dreams draw aberrant beings and shape Innsmouth as an amalgamation of cosmic horrors, from disparate ruins on the surface to stranger realms in the depths.  
- **Cult Haven.** Evil cults devoted to the entities Cthulhu, Dagon, Olhydra, and Zhudun struggle to control the domain. These cults view strangers as useful allies (see "Cults of Innsmouth" for details).  
- **Dreams of Cthulhu.** Cthulhu seeks freedom. It manipulates the dreams of those on the island, sharing visions of their escape from the domain resulting from the same rituals that would free it.  

### Locations in Innsmouth

Innsmouth is an inhospitable expanse of alien mountains and ruin-littered coasts. The village of Innsmouth and the mazelike Vaults are described below, and other notable locations are summarized on the "Innsmouth Locations table".

#### Innsmouth

The ruined coastal village of Innsmouth is the most obvious shelter from the storms, alien creatures, and strange events on the island. The Cult of the Chthonic Night knows this and realizes its imprisoned master, Great Cthulhu, calls to strangers to aid the cultists in releasing it. This makes the ruined village a shadowy war zone, where cultists and their servants hunt for fresh acolytes and sacrifices.

#### The Vaults

Beneath the mountains of Innsmouth winds a labyrinth of improbable passages. Dramatic caverns narrow into the corridors of buried palaces that transform into the wooden halls of forgotten farmhouses. Regularly, these underground paths open into vast cavities, many with their own strange environments, weather, and celestial bodies. What lies among the Vaults? Cultists speak of the realms of alien beings, ghoul empires, countrysides ravaged by sapient energies, the dwellings of reclusive witches, and a thin place in the walls of the prison where Great Cthulhu lies trapped.

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.17: Innsmouth](file://book/RHW/103-map-10-01.innsmouth.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/104-map-10-01.innsmouth-player.webp#gallery)

![Innsmouth Locations](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/innsmouth-locations-rhw.md)

### Cthulhu

*Darklord What Eternal Lies*

![](file://book/RHW/105-10-003.cthulhu.webp#center)

> [!quote] A quote from Cult of the Chthonic Night chant  
> 
> Ph'nglui mglw'nafh Cthulhu R'lyeh wgah'nagl fhtagn.

Cthulhu was—and inevitably will be once more—a threat to the entire multiverse. For untold ages, the Dark Powers have bound this harbinger of doom. Unlike the other prisoners of the Domains of Dread, Cthulhu isn't plagued by ironic torments or thwarted ambitions. Rather, this ageless terror remains physically bound and can exert only a fraction of its terrible might. Nevertheless, Cthulhu's dreams slip beyond its prison, manipulating minds and orchestrating events to ensure its release and a new epoch of multiversal doom.

> [!embed-monster]- Cthulhu
> ![Cthulhu](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/cthulhu-rhw.md#^statblock)

#### Cthulhu's Tale

Spawned beyond the borders of the multiverse in realities where time and life have little worth, Cthulhu is a servant of elder evils and a harbinger of their inevitable ruin. For untold eons, Cthulhu's will influenced receptive minds across the multiverse, reaching out in dreams and using them to open gateways to the Far Realm. Through such portals, Cthulhu visited the Material Plane, corrupted and laid waste to civilizations, and erected city-size monuments to its mighty predecessors.

Such distortion and defilement didn't go unnoticed by the Dark Powers. Multiple times the Mists closed around dread Cthulhu, and multiple times the terror evaded them. It was drawn into the Shadowfell when an extinct cabal of mages summoned it onto a sepulchral world of the Material Plane during a once-in-an-era alignment of eclipses. With the magic of the Shadowfell enhanced, the Mists rose and drew in Cthulhu. Raging and grasping, Cthulhu dragged with it remnants of past conquests and violent minds linked to its own. These disparate nightmares became the foundation of its prison: a surreal island hidden amid the Domains of Dread.

#### Cthulhu's Domain

Innsmouth is altered by Cthulhu's presence, creating the following effects:

- **Choking Depths.** A creature can [hold its breath](3-Mechanics/CLI/traps-hazards/suffocation-xphb.md) for only 30 seconds while in the domain.  
- **Closing the Borders.** While in its domain, Cthulhu can close or open the borders of Innsmouth at will. While the borders are closed, those who enter the Mists surrounding Innsmouth become lost at sea amid inky fog for `dice:3d4|noform|noparens|avg` (`3d4`) days before arriving once more at Innsmouth.  
- **Something in the Air.** Creatures other than Cthulhu and its allies have [Disadvantage](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/disadvantage-xphb.md) on saving throws to avoid or end the [Frightened](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/conditions.md#Frightened) condition.  

If Cthulhu dies, these effects end immediately.

#### Cthulhu's Lair

Amid surreal expanses within Innsmouth's depths lies the entrance to Cthulhu's Vault, a prison within the Mists where Cthulhu lies trapped. The entrance to Cthulhu's Vault is a ritual site etched with symbols of power from across time and hundreds of worlds. Those who perform the proper rituals, guided by visions from Cthulhu itself, might free themselves from the domain of Innsmouth, and, in so doing, unleash Cthulhu on the multiverse.

##### Cthulhu's Vault Features

Cthulhu's Vault is a hidden realm, but the entrance to it lies amid the Vaults beneath the island. The vault is depicted on "map 2.18" and has the following features:

- **Noisome Brine.** A dark, frothy waterway winds through the Vaults, ultimately emerging from either the Cleft of Dreams or the mouth of the Drowned Colossus.
