- **Ritual Site.** A partially toppled monument bearing a tentacled visage marks a weak point in Cthulhu's prison. Before it stands an altar etched with bizarre runes. These symbols are of otherworldly design, but each cult of Innsmouth knows the meaning of a few. Only cultists imbued with the might of all four cults can perform the ritual these runes describe and force open Cthulhu's prison.  
- **The Perceptive.** A small ship called the Perceptive lies beached here, a remnant of a group of cultists' past attempt to access Cthulhu's Vault. The bowsprit is broken, ending in a jagged point.  
- **The Providence.** The shattered remains of a ship called the Providence serves as the shelter of a mysterious seer. It's said this former cultist knows more of Cthulhu's Vault than any other creature.  

### Cults of Innsmouth

Four cults operate in Innsmouth, each with its own vile ends. While these groups are ruinously evil, characters might temporarily ally with one or more to oppose another foe or to escape the domain.

#### Cults and Cultists

The following groups vie for power on and under Innsmouth. Following each cult's name are the ritual words cult members use in their blasphemous practices, along with other details.

##### Cult of the Chthonic Night

*Hail, Hail, Cthulhu Awaits*

- **Worships.** Cthulhu  
- **Leader.** King-Priest Eeyog-Yah  
- **Goal.** Free Cthulhu from imprisonment  
- **Lair.** The village of Innsmouth and the Vaults  

Initiates of the Cult of the Chthonic Night open their minds to the whispers of Great Cthulhu and seek to free the imprisoned terror from the Domains of Dread. Predominantly composed of [Aberrant Cultists](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/aberrant-cultist-xmm.md) and [Kuo-toa](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/aberration/kuo-toa-xmm.md) that dwell amid waterlogged ruins deep below the Graven Peak, the cult interprets visions from Cthulhu as omens, calls for sacrifice, and signs of their god's coming.

King-Priest Eeyog-Yah, an ageless and desiccated [Kuo-toa Archpriest](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/aberration/kuo-toa-archpriest-xmm.md), leads the cult. Eeyog-Yah occupies a state of perpetual somnambulism and narrates its visions. The priest's attendants decipher their leader's rambling as directives from their god.

Those who join the cult and participate in its induction rituals hear the voice of Cthulhu more clearly than others do (see "Cult Dark Gifts").

![Symbol of the Cult of the Chthonic Night Symbol of the Cult of the Drowning Wave Symbol of the Cult of the Heavenly Doom Symbol of the Cult of the Scaly Abyss](file://book/RHW/106-10-004.cult-symbols.webp#center)

##### Cult of the Drowning Wave

*Make Clean for the Aeon Wave*

- **Worships.** Olhydra  
- **Leader.** Draa Shoom  
- **Goal.** Sink Innsmouth below the waves  
- **Lair.** Eyes of Olhydra  

Those who await the Drowning Wave seek to make Innsmouth and all its inhabitants part of Olhydra's realm on the Elemental Plane of Water. Olhydra, the Prince of Evil Water, then could use the might of Cthulhu and the mass sacrifice of the island to dominate the Elemental Planes and flood the Material Plane.

Draa Shoom, the cult's [Aboleth](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/aberration/aboleth-xmm.md) leader, believes Olhydra will return the cult to a place of dominance over countless worlds in return for its sacrifice. To effect this, Draa Shoom coaxes [Elemental Cultists](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/elemental-cultist-xmm.md) and shipwrecked individuals to the Eyes of Olhydra. There, amid boggy ruins and the lairs of murky elemental creatures, rises the Fathomless Gate. This ancient stone arch, thought to connect to the Elemental Plane of Water, is covered by bars of starmetal, which prevent passage by solid creatures. The cult seeks the proper rituals to open the gate, allowing Olhydra's scouring waters to flood the domain.

Those who participate in the cult's induction rituals are infused with a draught of Olhydra's sapient form (see "Cult Dark Gifts").

##### Cult of the Heavenly Doom

*Empty Yourself to Gorge on the Stars*

- **Worships.** Zhudun  
- **Leader.** Celesta Grayl  
- **Goal.** Open gateways to join Zhudun  
- **Lair.** Blind Observatory and the Map of the Eclipse  

Among the broken heights of the domain, the obsessed astronomers of the Cult of the Heavenly Doom seek signs in the heavens and omens from Zhudun, the Corpse Star, an Elder Evil that wanders space and knows the secrets of extinction. These cultists hope to climb into the heavens and join Zhudun.

The cult's leader, Celesta Grayl, has sought Zhudun for centuries. While documenting her observations, Grayl discovered a path to immortality and became a [Vampire Umbral Lord](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/vampire-umbral-lord-xmm.md). [Death Cultists](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/death-cultist-xmm.md), along with desperate and deluded souls, have flocked to the ancient stargazer, forming the cult around Grayl and her discoveries despite their leader's protestations and predations. The vampire suffers the cultists only so long as they help her decipher secrets from ruins around the island and retrieve knowledge from the grip of other cults. She believes their discoveries will help her reveal when the stars are right to join Zhudun in the dark places between the stars.

Those who join the cult and participate in its induction rituals release a portion of their life to the stars (see "Cult Dark Gifts").

##### Cult of the Scaly Abyss

*The Prince Awaits—Become the Way*

- **Worships.** Dagon  
- **Leader.** Xr'gh  
- **Goal.** Summon Dagon  
- **Lair.** Dagon's Claws  

The followers of Dagon, Demon Prince of the Darkened Depths, lurk among and beneath the waves of Innsmouth. Ancient even among inhabitants of the Abyss, Dagon seeks to drag demon lords and their Abyssal realms into its demesne of Shadowsea. Once sated on the flesh of its foes, Dagon aspires to unleash its might across the multiverse in a sanity-shattering wave.

Xr'gh, a [Sahuagin Baron](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fiend/sahuagin-baron-xmm.md) fanatically devoted to Dagon, seeks to turn all who dwell beneath the waves to the demon lord's worship. Xr'gh seeks enough sacrifices to turn the sea red with blood, an offering great enough to attract Dagon's notice and draw the demon lord to Innsmouth. The cult leader expects Dagon then to feed on Cthulhu and begin its conquest of the Abyss. Ravenous [Sahuagin](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fiend/sahuagin-warrior-xmm.md) follow Xr'gh, as do [Fiend Cultists](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/fiend-cultist-xmm.md) and murderers desirous of the eerie gold treasures the sahuagin offer from their submerged vaults. The Cult of the Scaly Abyss hunts the domain's ruined villages, abducting anyone who seeks shelter amid the wreckage. Those they find, they drag through secret paths beneath the waves to their ritual site under the island called Dagon's Claw.

Those who join the cult and participate in its induction rituals develop shark-like organs (see "Cult Dark Gifts").

#### Cult Rites

The cults of Innsmouth seek initiates to aid in their unfathomable works. Those who prove themselves reliable devotees gain access to the transformative power of strange gods.

##### Cult Renown

The cults of Innsmouth reward those who honor their obscene patrons. Use the "guidance" in the "Dungeon Master's Guide" to track characters' individual standing within Innsmouth's cults. Characters can gain renown with a cult by performing deeds such as those in the Innsmouth Cults Renown table.

![Innsmouth Cults Renown](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/innsmouth-cults-renown-rhw.md)

##### Cult Dark Gifts

Characters who have a Renown Score of 10+ with an Innsmouth cult are honored as the chosen of the cult's patron. They are urged to take part in a ritual that inducts them into the cult and bestows on them a supernatural boon. A character who participates in such a ritual gains the Dark Gift (see chapter 1) noted on the Innsmouth Cults Dark Gifts table.

![Innsmouth Cults Dark Gifts](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/innsmouth-cults-dark-gifts-rhw.md)

These Dark Gifts include magical transformations associated with the cult's patron and its members. This magic can make it easier to navigate parts of the domain and bypass seals made by cult magic. This includes the binding sigils that mark Cthulhu's Vault. A character with one of these Dark Gifts can't gain another. A character with one of these gifts who leaves Innsmouth can choose to lose the Dark Gift or keep it.

### Adventures in Innsmouth

Adventures in Innsmouth involve cults, degenerate rituals, nightmarish visions, and aberrant transformations. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

![Nightmarish monuments and reality-defying ruins cover the island called Innsmouth](file://book/RHW/107-10-005.nightmarsh-monuments.webp#center)

#### Corruptive Horror

The cults of Innsmouth are monstrous and dangerous, but not unwelcoming. Each seeks to bring a different terrifying cataclysm to Innsmouth. As characters interact with these cults and learn more of the island's secrets, bizarre dreams encourage the characters to accept the Dark Gifts the cults offer and balance rivalries to gain the might of each. Groups that engage with each cult might have strange adventures across Innsmouth and undergo bizarre transformations. Those that do will find themselves with the power to free Cthulhu from the island—and maybe themselves as well.

#### Dreams of Innsmouth

Cthulhu sends dreams to those in Innsmouth—and in realms beyond—that might help it escape its prison. These dreams include strange images spurring the dreamers to seek the cults of Innsmouth, gain their powers, and then dispel the sigils in Cthulhu's Vault. Dreams sent by Cthulhu might focus on the following topics and imagery:

- **Cult of the Chthonic Night.** The village of Innsmouth, the Graven Peak, desiccated fish, tentacles  
- **Cult of the Drowning Wave.** The Eyes of Olhydra, shipwrecks, tidal waves, three eyes underwater  
- **Cult of the Heavenly Doom.** The peaks of Innsmouth, corpses in space, monoliths, whirling stars  
- **Cult of the Scaly Abyss.** Dagon's Claws, deep-sea predators, sharks eating sharks, undersea ruins  
- **Cthulhu's Vault.** The Cleft of Dreams, the Drowned Colossus, dark passages, strange sigils  

Any of these dreams might end with a vision of the Mists parting and the characters' home or a similarly tantalizing location appearing beyond.

#### Old One's Bargain

Cthulhu's dream-messages tempt characters to release the entity to win their own escape from its domain. Whether Cthulhu can or will fulfill this offer is up to you, but the characters might not wish to jeopardize reality to escape. In the course of exploring Innsmouth, they can find the writings of obsessed wizards and cult heresies that suggest the following secrets:

- **Cthulhu's Disruption.** Cthulhu's power is such that, should someone release it, the Mists around Innsmouth would open and those in the domain could escape.  
- **Cthulhu's Might.** Cthulhu wouldn't emerge from its prison at full strength. For approximately one hour after its release, heroes might force Cthulhu back into its prison, should they subject the terror to potent magic such as [Imprisonment](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/imprisonment-xphb.md) or [Wish](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/wish-xphb.md), or a blow powerful enough to disrupt its physical form, like a powerful lightning strike, a massive explosion, or a strike from a large sailing ship.  

Elaborate on these possibilities as characters explore Innsmouth, and encourage them to believe they might be able to outwit a Great Old One.

#### Otherworldly Relics

The monsters noted in the "Cosmic Horror" section of "chapter 4" make appropriate inhabitants of the ruins and vaults of Innsmouth. These beings often possess evidence of alien technologies and cultures. Innsmouth's cults covet such relics. Roll on or choose a result from the Alien Relics table to inspire what otherworldly beings might possess.

**Alien Relics**

`dice: [](3-chapter-2-domains-of-ravenloft.md#^alien-relics)`

| dice: 1d6 | The Alien Being Possesses... |
|-----------|------------------------------|
| 1 | A crystalline wand with a monstrous face. |
| 2 | A faintly glowing trapezohedron. |
| 3 | An jade amulet shaped like a sphinx. |
| 4 | A metallic cluster of globes and half globes. |
| 5 | An oversize, pattern-etched silver key. |
| 6 | A preserved brain in a glass cylinder. |
^alien-relics

#### Innsmouth Campaign Arc

Campaigns set in Innsmouth involve warring cults, unfathomable beings, and bizarre transformations. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–2.** The characters wash up on Innsmouth island and shelter in the village. They experience strange dreams. Soon after, they encounter cultists who seek to initiate them and others who seek to sacrifice them. The characters gain allies among one of the island's cults.  
- **Levels 3–5.** The allied cult sends the characters to disrupt other cults and retrieve relics from the ruins. In return, the cult offers insights into the characters' dreams and suggests ways to escape the island. After proving their worth, a character receives the cult's Dark Gift (see "Cult Rites").  
- **Levels 6–16.** Led by their dreams and duplicitous cult members, the characters move from cult to cult, gaining influence by delving into ruins and strange vaults. In doing so, they collect Dark Gifts, as well as hints about Cthulhu's Vault and ways to undermine the Great Old One (see "Old One's Bargain").  
- **Levels 17–20.** After collecting a Dark Gift from each cult, the characters follow a treacherous path through the Vaults to Cthulhu's Vault. There, they can risk releasing [Cthulhu](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/cthulhu-rhw.md) to escape the island.  

#### Vault of the Elder

*Adventure for Level 11 Characters*

- **Situation.** Cult lore tells of a vault that is home to a wise elder who knows the secrets of escaping the island.  
- **Hook.** A cult leader shares directions to the vault but wants one of the strange relics the elder is said to hoard.  

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.18: Cthulhu's Vault](file://book/RHW/108-map-10-02.cthulhus-vault.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/109-map-10-02.cthulhus-vault-player.webp#gallery)

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.18: Cthulhu's Vault Surroundings](file://book/RHW/110-map-10-04.cthulhus-vault-surroundings.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/111-map-10-04.cthulhus-vault-surroundings-player.webp#gallery)

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.18: Wreck of the Providence](file://book/RHW/112-map-10-03.wreck-of-the-providence.webp#gallery)

##### Encounters

The adventure uses map 2.18 and consists of these encounters:

###### Vault Ambush

On the way to the vault, two [Cult Fanatics](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/cultist-fanatic-xmm.md) and a [Fiend Cultist](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/fiend-cultist-xmm.md) (or another enemy cultist selected from those mentioned in "Cults of Innsmouth") ambush the characters.

###### Frigid Spires

The Vault of the Elder lies in a realm of icy mountains gripped by extreme cold (see ""Environmental Effects"" in the "Dungeon Master's Guide"). The towers of a gravity-defying stone city protrude from one mountain.

###### Hollow City

The characters find the city filled with narrow ramps and abandoned, tubelike structures etched with eerie hieroglyphs. Of particular note is an out-of-place collection of tents and a templelike building.

###### Encampment

Brown mold covers the tents (see [chapter 3](3-Mechanics/CLI/traps-hazards/brown-mold-xdmg.md) of the Dungeon Master's Guide). If the characters remove the mold, they find five cultists frozen inside the tents, wrapped in blankets. One wears a [Ring of Mind Shielding](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/ring-of-mind-shielding-xdmg.md).

###### Elder Temple

The templelike building bears carvings depicting five-winged beings fighting giant, fungus-like insects. Through the temple lies a path leading deeper into the mountain—and defended by a [Shoggoth](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/aberration/shoggoth-rhw.md) (see chapter 5).

###### Frozen Warning

Ice encrusts the walls of the deeper temple, covering more strange carvings. Etched into the ice over a depiction of another five-winged creature is a warning in Common: "Beware the Elder."

###### Elder's Reliquary

The passage ends in a chamber with four pillars of ice. Perched on one is a [Hostile](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/hostile-attitude-xphb.md) [Elder Thing](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/aberration/elder-thing-rhw.md) (see chapter 5).

###### Ice Tombs

The pillars of ice each hold a shadowy shape. These pillars have AC 14, HP 20, Immunity to Poison and Psychic damage, and Vulnerability to Fire damage. The pillars contain the following:

- **Alien Relic.** The first pillar contains a strange relic. Roll on the ""Alien Relics"" table earlier in this chapter to determine what it is.  
- **Mi-Go.** Two pillars contain [Mi-Go](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/aberration/mi-go-rhw.md) (see chapter 5), which awake 1 round after being freed.  
- **Vault Map.** A hieroglyph-etched slab in the final pillar charts a route from Innsmouth's surface to Cthulhu's Vault. It also provides information from the "Old One's Bargain" section. However, only someone with the "Dark Gift" of the Cult of Heavenly Doom can decipher its alien language.  

## Kalakeri

*Domain of Betrayal and Revenge*

> [!note] 
> 
> - **Darklord.** Ramya Vasavadan  
> - **Adventure Genres.** Gothic horror and dark fantasy  
> - **Hallmarks.** Monstrous leaders, family intrigue, war-torn nation  
> - **Mist Talismans.** Rusted tulwar, shield with a wyvern-and-lotus emblem, a polished skull  
> - **Aligned Tarokka Card.** Avenger  
> - **Opposed Tarokka Card.** Artifact  
^1c0

> [!gallery]
> ![](file://book/RHW/113-11-001.avenger-tarokka.webp#gallery)
> ![](file://book/RHW/114-11-002.artifact-tarokka.webp#gallery)

Deceptively beautiful, Kalakeri is a land of verdant rainforests and a web of rivers and lakes known as the Backwaters. At the height of its prosperity, Kalakeri was a robust center of art, commerce, and religion, with merchants spreading wild tales of the land, using fanciful names such as Sri Raji and the Steaming Lands. Now Kalakeri is a conflict-torn shadow of its past glory. The remnants of the Vasavadan dynasty—three heirs transformed into monsters by their depravity and hatred—trap the land in an endless cycle of war.

The people of Kalakeri live in fear of [Maharani Ramya Vasavadan](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ramya-vasavadan-rhw.md), the domain's Darklord, as well as her treacherous siblings, Arijani and Reeva. The Darklord's curse manifests both in her deathless desire to rule Kalakeri and in her siblings' endless rebellions. Both sides escalate their atrocities against one another, drawing the powerful and the innocent alike into their squabbles. As the maharani's siblings court allies, the Darklord's forces hunt and execute renegades, adding skulls to the grim Tower of Traitors.

### Domain Features

Kalakeri is known for the following features:

- **Factions in Conflict.** Two factions claim Kalakeri's Sapphire Throne: the soldiers and loyalists of Maharani Ramya Vasavadan, and the nobles and merchants who support the younger royal siblings, Arijani and Reeva Vasavadan.  
- **Jadurai, a City at War.** The vast city of Jadurai is Kalakeri's capital, the site of the royal palace, and a battlefield where factions struggle to claim or hold it as a symbol of rule.  
- **The Backwaters.** Rare creatures and extraordinary magical plants flourish in the Backwaters, the collective name for the wilderness away from Kalakeri's cities. Scattered refugee groups hide in the wilds and organize dangerous, desperate attacks on the Vasavadan factions.  

### Locations in Kalakeri

Tropical rainforests isolate Kalakeri's communities. While the domain's residents are adept at navigating these wildernesses, strangers often fall prey to the domain's myriad hazards and predators.

The capital of Jadurai is detailed below, and other notable locations are summarized on the "Kalakeri Locations table".

#### Jadurai

Ancient structures adorned with the artistry of past dynasties stand alongside modern buildings in Kalakeri's capital, Jadurai. The city retains its splendor, but the conflict between the Vasavadan siblings takes an enormous toll as they struggle over the Cerulean Citadel, the nation's capitol, as well as the Sapphire Throne within. Sections of the city lie in ruins.

On the outskirts of Jadurai rises the Tower of Traitors. Rows of skulls taken from the Darklord's enemies fill depressions in this stone tower. Two skulls hold places of special prominence: the original human skulls of Arijani and Reeva Vasavadan. The Darklord's skeletal soldiers build the tower as part of her plan to rid Kalakeri of evil and receive the gods' blessings.

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.19: Kalakeri](file://book/RHW/115-map-11-01.kalakeri.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/116-map-11-01.kalakeri-player.webp#gallery)

![Kalakeri Locations](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/kalakeri-locations-rhw.md)

### Ramya Vasavadan

*Darklord Perpetually Denied Control*

![](file://book/RHW/117-11-003.ramya-vasvadan.webp#center)

> [!quote] A quote from Ramya Vasavadan  
> 
> Are you loyal to your maharani? Or are you yet more rebel skulls to add to the Tower of Traitors?

Ramya Vasavadan desperately fights to claim and hold power over Kalakeri in a brutal cycle of victory and loss with her equally uncompromising siblings. Unlike most Darklords, Ramya struggles to control her domain, leading her to seek allies in opposing her siblings and their treacherous allies.

In her true form, Ramya is an undead horror, but illusions mask her monstrous appearance. Her true nature is revealed by her chilled skin and her reflection, which always appears withered and terrifying.

Although Ramya's siblings, Arijani and Reeva, aren't Darklords of Kalakeri, they motivate the rebellions in Kalakeri and Ramya's torments. This monstrous pair is detailed in "Arijani and Reeva."

> [!embed-monster]- Ramya Vasavadan
> ![Ramya Vasavadan](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ramya-vasavadan-rhw.md#^statblock)

#### Ramya's Tale

The Vasavadan dynasty has ruled Kalakeri since ancient times. Ramya Vasavadan was handpicked by her father to succeed him, but on the bleak day of his death, Ramya's brother, Arijani, declared himself the new maharaja.

Ramya refused to yield to her brother, and with her allies, she captured and prepared to execute him. But Ramya's sister, Reeva, counseled mercy. Instead, Ramya imprisoned Arijani and ascended as Kalakeri's maharani, Queen of Kings.

In the years that followed, Ramya ruled justly. But in the shadows, Reeva plotted with rebels, who eventually freed Arijani and spurred nobles across the nation to revolt.

Regretting her mercy, Ramya sent her army to crush the rebels and mercilessly execute the treacherous. Reeva and Arijani combated Ramya's superior forces with ambushes and deceptions. Once again exploiting Ramya's sympathies, the pair tricked Ramya, invaded the Cerulean Citadel, and executed their sister by strangling. With her final gasps, Ramya cursed her brother and sister, calling them bloodthirsty beasts. Soon after, a terrible monsoon struck Kalakeri, bringing with it the Mists.

The storm lashed Kalakeri for weeks. At its height, Ramya returned from the dead and called on those who had fallen in her service. Loyal in death, a corpse legion joined the revitalized maharani, besieged the Cerulean Citadel, and slaughtered Arijani and Reeva. Ramya then stole their skulls and built them into the foundations of what would become the Tower of Traitors.

Arijani and Reeva's plots didn't end with their lives. They too were reborn, transformed into monstrous reflections of their ravenous desires.

Now in the Land of the Mists, the conflict gripping Kalakeri continues, trapping the nation in an endless war and forcing its people to swear loyalty to monsters.

#### Ramya's Domain

While Ramya is in control of the Sapphire Throne, Kalakeri is altered by Ramya's presence, creating the following effects:

- **Closing the Borders.** While in her domain, Ramya can close or open the borders to Kalakeri at will. While the borders are closed, the Mists surrounding Kalakeri sap the life of those within them. A creature that enters the Mists for the first time on a turn or starts its turn there and isn't a Construct or an Undead must succeed on a DC 20 Constitution saving throw or gain 1 [Exhaustion](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/conditions.md#Exhaustion) level. A creature makes this save only once per turn.  
- **Everlasting Army.** A Medium or Small Humanoid slain in combat rises 24 hours later as a [Wight](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/wight-xmm.md) under Ramya's control, unless the Humanoid is restored to life or its body is destroyed.  

If Ramya dies or if her siblings control the Sapphire Throne, these effects end immediately.

#### Ramya's Lair

The Cerulean Citadel is Kalakeri's royal palace. It derives its name from the blue sandstone used in its construction. Control of the citadel and the Sapphire Throne within regularly passes between Ramya and her siblings.

##### Cerulean Citadel

Bas-reliefs adorn the palace, depicting the history, heroes, and legends of the kingdom. The site is depicted on "map 2.20" and has the following features:

- **Domed Court.** The central domed court houses the Sapphire Throne. It hosts guardians and treasures gathered by the paranoid Vasavadans. Towers guard the surrounding walls, which are accessible via bridges from the court's upper floors.  
- **War-Torn Courtyards.** Within the palace walls lie marble pavilions arranged among baths, ponds, and gardens. Some are intact, but sieges and repeated conflicts have ravaged others.  

### Adventures in Kalakeri

Adventures set in Kalakeri involve suspicion and power struggles. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

![Evidence of the endless conflict between the Vasavadan siblings lies rotting before the Cerulean Citadel](file://book/RHW/118-11-004.cerulean-citadel.webp#center)

#### Horror in Kalakeri

Adventures in Kalakeri often include the following elements.

##### Arijani and Reeva

Ramya's rule is jeopardized by her siblings' pursuit of power. Arijani and Reeva Vasavadan promise their followers wealth and freedom, but in truth, their agendas serve only them. Ramya still loves her siblings, making her vulnerable to their promises and lies. So long as Ramya exists, the Dark Powers resurrect Arijani and Reeva as if they had [Ramya's](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ramya-vasavadan-rhw.md) Darklord Restoration trait.

###### Arijani

Arijani is the charming face of resistance for all who oppose Ramya. Now a [Rakshasa](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fiend/rakshasa-xmm.md), gregarious Arijani has decadent tastes. When in control of the Cerulean Citadel, he hosts parties for Kalakeri's elite that conceal private feasts featuring obscene delicacies and mortal flesh.

###### Reeva

Reeva's adoration of Ramya gave way to jealousy when Ramya eclipsed her in their family's esteem. Now an [Arcanaloth](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fiend/arcanaloth-xmm.md), Reeve uses insidious magic from beneath the Cerulean Citadel to summon fiends and manipulate foes from afar. Behind her back, many mockingly call Reeva "Inajira," her charismatic Arijani's opposite.

#### Renown in Kalakeri

You can track the characters' influence with Ramya's loyalist faction and her siblings' rebel faction, using the "renown rules" from the "Dungeon Master's Guide" to track the characters' standing with these groups. Characters might gain renown with either faction by performing missions such as these:

- Capturing or killing a rival agent  
- Planting evidence that a rival committed a crime  
- Conscripting a powerful ally for the faction  
- Revealing the location of a rival's hold  
- Revealing traitors within the faction  

Anytime the characters complete a mission for either group, their Renown Score with that group increases by 1, but their Renown Score with the other group decreases by 1 (to a minimum of 0). After the first time characters gain renown with either faction, any faction the characters have a Renown Score of 0 with treat the characters as follows:

- **Loyalist Faction.** Members of this faction are [Hostile](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/hostile-attitude-xphb.md) toward the characters. The faction sends troops of [Wights](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/wight-xmm.md) or other Undead to capture the characters weekly.  
- **Rebel Faction.** Members of this faction are Hostile toward the characters. The faction sends [Assassins](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/assassin-xmm.md) or [Wraiths](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/wraith-xmm.md) under Reeva's command to kill the characters weekly.  

Characters can gain renown with a faction they have a Renown Score of 0 with by presenting proof of an action that undermines the other group. Even if betrayed, the factions seek the party's aid, as they view the characters as useful pawns.

If the characters have a Renown Score of 5+ with either group, their deeds might benefit the faction enough for it to take control of Jadurai and claim the Sapphire Throne. The longer either faction controls the capital, the more extreme its reign becomes, its atrocities escalating week after week. The characters must balance aiding and opposing both factions to maintain equilibrium.

#### Kalakeri Campaign Arc

Campaigns set in Kalakeri typically involve balancing the horrors committed by the Vasavadan factions. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–4.** Agents from the rebel faction contact the characters, presenting Arijani and Reeva Vasavadan as misunderstood heroes seeking to overthrow a tyrant. They entreat the characters to save the heir of an allied noble family from a compound controlled by Ramya's [Wight](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/wight-xmm.md) soldiers and return him to a hidden safe house.  
- **Levels 5–8.** The characters meet Arijani and Reeva in their disguises as charming human royals. They thank the characters for their aid and ask them to reclaim the shield of an ancient hero petrified in the Forest of the Still, hoping the shield will be a symbol of their right to rule. As the characters travel to the forest, a messenger delivers a request from [Ramya](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ramya-vasavadan-rhw.md) to do the same. The characters must face [Basilisks](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/basilisk-xmm.md) and the [Wraiths](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/wraith-xmm.md) of the petrified dead to recover the shield and then decide who to return it to.  
- **Levels 9–12.** Arijani and Reeva plot to attack Jadurai to claim the Sapphire Throne and request the characters' help. Ramya's spies have informed her of this plot, and she also seeks the characters' aid. In the ensuing conflict, the characters might strike at any of the Vasavadan siblings.  

#### Tower of Traitors

*Adventure for Level 11 Characters*

- **Situation.** Arijani and Reeva Vasavadan seek to recover the skulls of their mortal bodies from the Tower of Traitors. They believe the skulls will grant them greater power.  
- **Hook.** Arijani or Reeva order the characters to recover two skulls from the Tower of Traitors but don't say who the skulls belong to. They offer to pay the party with 10,000 GP in gemstones and a [Candle of Invocation](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/candle-of-invocation-xdmg.md).  

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.20: Cerulean Citadel](file://book/RHW/119-map-11-02.cerulean-citadel.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/120-map-11-02.cerulean-citadel-player.webp#gallery)

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.20: Tower of Traitors](file://book/RHW/121-map-11-03.tower-of-traitors.webp#gallery)

##### Encounters

This adventure assumes you are tracking the characters' renown with Kalakeri's loyalist and rebel factions (see "Renown in Kalakeri" earlier in this section). It includes these encounters.

###### Stolen Skulls

The skulls Arijani and Reeva seek are from their own corpses, which were defiled by Ramya. The skulls are among hundreds in the Tower of Traitors. The pair don't reveal who the skulls belong to but insist they're vital to the rebel faction's allies. To aid in the search, the siblings give the characters two [Spell Scrolls](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/spell-scroll-level-2-xdmg.md) of [Locate Object](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/locate-object-xphb.md). However, they don't provide the characters with enough details for the spell to pinpoint the skulls.

###### Learning About the Skulls

The characters must learn three details about the skulls for them to be familiar enough to the characters that a spell like Locate Object can locate them. Characters can learn details in three ways:

- **Research.** Characters who spend a day searching for rumors or investigating records in one of Kalakeri's settlements learn a detail by succeeding on a DC 16 Charisma ([Persuasion](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Persuasion)) check or Intelligence ([Investigation](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Investigation)) check respectively.  
- **Renown.** A character can spend a day questioning non-[Hostile](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/hostile-attitude-xphb.md) members of a faction. After doing so, the characters learn a detail, but their Renown Score with that faction is reduced by 1. The group can do this only once.  
- **Magic.** The [Legend Lore](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/legend-lore-xphb.md) spell reveals one detail; each character can use this spell once.  

Each time the party learns a detail about the skulls, reveal a portion of the story from the "Ramya's Tale" section, obscuring the names of the maharani and the traitors until the end.

###### Tower of Traitors

The Tower of Traitors is depicted on "map 2.20" and is guarded by patrols of two [Revenants](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/revenant-xmm.md) and four [Wights](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/wight-xmm.md). If the characters have a Renown Score of 3+ with the loyalist faction, the undead are [Indifferent](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/indifferent-attitude-xphb.md) and tell the party to move along—they fight only if characters linger for more than 5 minutes or remove a skull from the tower. If the characters have less renown with the loyalists, the undead are Hostile. A new patrol appears `dice:2d6|noform|noparens|avg` (`2d6`) rounds after a patrol is defeated.

###### Searching the Tower

The tower is composed of thousands of skulls, and the ones the rebels want can be found via magic such as the [Locate Object](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/locate-object-xphb.md) spell. Once discovered, a skull can be removed in 1 minute using a sharp implement. When both skulls are freed, the hatred lurking in the skulls manifests as two Hostile [Gallows Speakers](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/gallows-speaker-rhw.md) (see chapter 5).

###### Loyalty or Treachery

The next time the characters rest, Arijani ([Rakshasa](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fiend/rakshasa-xmm.md)) appears and demands the skulls. If the characters give him the skulls, he compensates them and the characters' Renown Score with the rebel faction increases by 4. If the characters refuse to give him the skulls, Arijani fights them. The party's Renown Score with the rebels decreases by 4 if Arijani is slain. Soon after, Ramya invites the characters to discuss future plans.

Regardless of how the adventure concludes, each character earns a bonus 4,100 XP.

## Kartakass

*Domain of Tarnished Dreams*

> [!note] 
> 
> - **Darklord.** Harkon Lukas  
> - **Adventure Genres.** Dark fantasy and gothic horror  
> - **Hallmarks.** Hidden identities, dangerous performances, exploitative ambitions, werewolves  
> - **Mist Talismans.** Handbill advertising remarkable performances, rustic woodcut of hunting wolves, wolf's tooth necklace  
> - **Aligned Tarokka Card.** Swashbuckler  
> - **Opposed Tarokka Card.** Beast  
^1d8

> [!gallery]
> ![](file://book/RHW/122-12-001.swashbuckler-tarokka.webp#gallery)
> ![](file://book/RHW/123-12-002.beast-tarokka.webp#gallery)

Life in Kartakass feels staged and surreal, as every plant, beast, and person strives to prove their greatness. Trees and flowers erupt into bloom; songbirds sing themselves hoarse; and every local knows that dreams, fame, and immortal adulation are theirs should they prove worthy. And where talent and expertise fail, obsession and duplicity reign, leading to cycles of triumph, betrayal, and despair. Predators flourish in this land of unrealistic hopes, consuming passions, and vicious secrets.

With each full moon, the truth of Kartakass is exposed, as the domain's many werewolves and other lycanthropes indulge their hunger for dominance and blood. After the full moon passes, the idyllic facade returns. Locals don't speak of why most bar their doors and shutter their windows on the nights of the full moon, but they acknowledge that the path to greatness is messy.

### Domain Features

Kartakass is known for the following features:

- **False Idylls.** Kartakass is supernaturally picturesque and outwardly serene. Every season is strikingly beautiful, communities appear idyllic, and many animals are affected as if by the [Awaken](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/awaken-xphb.md) spell. This makes deceptions and violence all the more stark.  
- **Meistersingers.** Kartakass has no unified government. Each settlement is governed by a meistersinger, the acknowledged mayor and embodiment of local art. Meistersingers maintain creative rivalries with one another largely for show.  
- **Theatricality.** Settlements pride themselves on performative traditions, such as distinctive dress, traditional dances, or song stylings.  
- **Wolves and Werewolves.** Wolves roam the land freely, and [Werewolves](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/werewolf-xmm.md) lurk in the domain's settlements. Residents seldom venture outside during the full moon, fearing the lycanthropes' hunger.  

### Locations in Kartakass

Kartakass is a land of rolling hills, light forests, clear lakes, and pastoral farmlands. Communities are welcoming and host frequent festivals. The settlements of Harmonia and Skald are detailed below, and other notable locations are summarized on the "Kartakass Locations table".

#### Harmonia

Artists vie to perform at the town of Harmonia's popular Crystal Club, a members-only venue inside a cave that features a stage constructed from a massive geode. The club features dramatic decor and discerning clientele. Rumors say that performers who fail to impress are exiled. The bloodier truth is that the club restricts membership to lycanthropes. Talented artists gain the curse and join their ranks, while the mediocre get devoured.

#### Skald

The largest community in Kartakass, Skald is a bustling hub of commerce and creativity. The lure of overnight celebrity and fawning crowds attracts the ambitious. Yet behind the facade of creativity and freethinking, business owners and celebrities prey on creativity, while performers struggle viciously over paltry opportunities. Vice, criminality, dark bargains, and supernatural predators flourish amid Skald's many stages and frequent festivals. Among Skald's most popular venues is the Old Kartakan Inn and Taverna, owned by the performer and Darklord Harkon Lukas.

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.21: Kartakass](file://book/RHW/124-map-12-01.kartakass.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/125-map-12-01.kartakass-player.webp#gallery)

![Kartakass Locations](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/kartakass-locations-rhw.md)

### Harkon Lukas

*Darklord Who Preys on Talent*

![](file://book/RHW/126-12-003.harkon-lukas.webp#center)

> [!quote] A quote from Harkon Lukas  
> 
> I must say, your skill is unlike any I've ever seen. The name's Harkon. I'm sure you've heard of me.

The charming werewolf Harkon Lukas manipulates those around him to satisfy his narcissistic needs for adulation and control. Endlessly seeking fame, Harkon travels widely, earning applause and accolades. Yet, whenever he returns to a town he's performed in, he finds he's been forgotten. Lukas believes he needs just the right song or inspiration to make himself unforgettable. To that end, he searches for talented protégés, cultivating their skills, then stealing their work. He ensures their loyalty by gifting them copies of his cursed wolf-tooth necklace, [Harkon's Bite](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/harkons-bite-rhw.md), or by transforming them into werewolves. He then manipulates these victims into believing only he will accept them.

Harkon wears a signature wide-brimmed hat and wolf-tooth necklace, and he carries a violin he calls Bleeding Heart. He uses flattery to charm those he takes an interest in. A skilled artist who declines the offer to become his protégé often earns his obsession. The Darklord might go to any extreme to claim such performers' talents as his own.

> [!embed-monster]- Harkon Lukas
> ![Harkon Lukas](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/harkon-lukas-rhw.md#^statblock)

#### Harkon's Tale

Harkon Lukas weaves numerous self-aggrandizing tales of his origins. Among them, Harkon tells of being spurned for his ambitions by the werewolves that raised him. Through talent and sacrifice, he became a legendary performer, and people flocked to bask in his remarkable presence.

Eventually, the rulers of Harkon's homeland realized the threat posed by Harkon's growing fame. Officials tried to imprison him for invented crimes, but Harkon's fans defended him. When royal agents came for him, Harkon feigned his death, and his followers revolted. When outraged masses bearing Harkon's coffin besieged the royal palace, Harkon ended his ploy. He burst from his crimson coffin in wolf form and devoured the land's monarch. Drenched in blood, the "resurrected" Harkon returned to his human form and donned the monarch's crown amid the cheers of his deluded followers. Yet before Harkon's reign could begin, the Mists rose around him. When they cleared, Harkon found himself in an unfamiliar land called Kartakass.

#### Harkon's Domain

Kartakass is altered by Harkon's presence, creating the following effects:

- **Beast Spies.** From dawn until dusk, Tiny Beasts in the domain magically gain the ability to understand Common and can communicate telepathically with other Beasts and Monstrosities.  
- **Children of the Night.** Harkon exerts influence over the animals of his domain. From dusk until dawn, Medium or smaller Beasts within 1 miles of Harkon have the [Charmed](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/conditions.md#Charmed) condition. If Harkon pleases, these animals become [Hostile](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/hostile-attitude-xphb.md) to creatures other than Harkon and his allies.  
- **Closing the Borders.** While in his domain, Harkon can close or open the borders to Kartakass at will. While the borders are closed, a strange melody fills the Mists surrounding Kartakass. A creature that enters the Mists for the first time on a turn or starts its turn in them must succeed on a DC 15 Wisdom saving throw, or it has the [Unconscious](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/conditions.md#Unconscious) condition for `dice:1d6|noform|noparens|avg` (`1d6`) hours, then awakes within sight of the town of Harmonia in Kartakass. A creature makes this save only once per turn.  

If Harkon dies, these effects end immediately.

#### Harkon's Lair

The Darklord owns a tavern in Skald called the Old Kartakan Inn and Taverna. The inn occupies a small island on the Sing Song River. Nightly, Harkon Lukas or artists under his tutelage perform there.

##### Old Kartakan Inn and Taverna

Welcoming and rustic, the Old Kartakan features subtle wolf-themed decor. The site is depicted on "map 2.22" and has the following features:

- **Bedrooms.** The inn's rooms are insulated to block the sounds of performances and maulings alike.  
- **Harkon Lukas's Room.** Several secret doors and a trapdoor lead to Harkon's tower bedroom, where he hides evidence of his own uninspired music and trophies from past victims.  
- **Secret Doors and Chambers.** The inn is riddled with secret spaces to spy into other chambers, hide bodies, or indulge in bestial meals.  
- **Taproom.** Among the drinks the taverna offers is Meekulbrau, a blood-red berry wine that soothes the throat and improves vocal performances.  

### Adventures in Kartakass

Adventures set in Kartakass involve art, werewolves, and sinister ambitions. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

![Locals celebrate during a festival in Skald, unaware of the predators lurking among them](file://book/RHW/127-12-004.festival-in-skald.webp#center)

#### Horror in Kartakass

Kartakan adventures often include the following elements.

##### Harkon's Curse

Harkon Lukas can create a copy of his signature necklace once per month on the night of the full moon. This cursed copy is called *Harkon's Bite*.

##### Harkon's Bite

Wondrous Item, Uncommon (Requires Attunement by a Humanoid)

A dire wolf's tooth dangles from this simple cord necklace. You gain a +1 bonus to ability checks and saving throws while you wear this necklace.

###### Curse

This necklace is cursed. Attuning to the necklace curses you; this curse can't be removed until [Harkon Lukas](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/harkon-lukas-rhw.md) dies. As long as you remain cursed, you become a [Werewolf](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/werewolf-xmm.md) serving Harkon Lukas under the DM's control during the night of a full moon.

##### Harkon's Manipulations

Harkon Lukas seeks to win the attention and trust of artistic and charismatic individuals. This might include characters—especially bards—or their allies. Harkon might do this to further a grand plot, but he also does so to assuage his perpetually bruised ego and satisfy his need for control. Harkon also seeks supernatural forces he can exploit, including magic items or beings with performative powers—such as an [Instrument of the Bards](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/instrument-of-the-bards-xdmg.md), [harpies](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/harpy-xmm.md), or [satyrs](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fey/satyr-xmm.md).

Harkon presents himself as a charming admirer or mentor seeking to aid others. He tries to manipulate those he pursues and earn their trust by encouraging them to do the following:

- Collaborate in creating a new song or show  
- Compete in performances against the domain's meistersingers  
- Join him for tutoring or training exercises  
- Protect him from a jealous former student  
- Find a performer who stole one of his songs  
- Travel with him on a tour of other towns  

Harkon's requests eventually turn criminal or violent. He might then blackmail those who aided him or threaten their reputations, or he might isolate them by gifting them [Harkon's Bite](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/harkons-bite-rhw.md). Harkon continues such manipulations until it bores him, at which point he consumes his prey.

##### The Lukas Pack

An ever-changing entourage of followers and victims surrounds Harkon Lukas, but three individuals are constants in the Darklord's life:

- **Akriel Lukas.** Harkon's eldest daughter, Akriel (Medium, Chaotic Evil [Performer Legend](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/performer-legend-xmm.md)), idolizes Harkon and pursues her own performing career. The Dark Powers don't torment Akriel as they do her father, and her reputation steadily grows—much to her father's resentment. Akriel is a human and isn't a lycanthrope.  
- **Casimir Lukas.** Harkon's eldest son, Casimir (Medium, Chaotic Neutral [Spy Master](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/spy-master-xmm.md)), is seeking his place in the world. He wants nothing to do with Harkon, preferring to travel, even to other domains. Whether at the whims of his father or the Mists, Casimir always finds his way back to Skald. Casimir is a human and isn't a lycanthrope.  
- **Haldrake Moonbaun.** Harkon's oldest ally, Haldrake (Medium [Werewolf](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/werewolf-xmm.md)) appears as a heavily tattooed human. He serves as the Old Kartakan Inn and Taverna mixologist and head bouncer. When Harkon isn't in Skald, he ensures things at the taverna run smoothly. Haldrake aids Harkon in his plots and knows many of the Darklord's secrets, so Harkon compensates him well.  

##### Traces of Terror

Kartakass's charm masks its horrors. Roll on or choose a result from the Kartakass Sights table to inspire unsettling scenes in the domain.

![Kartakass Sights](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/kartakass-sights-rhw.md)

#### Kartakass Campaign Arc

A campaign in Kartakass might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–2.** The characters meet Maria, a human woman whose idealistic son, Frantosh, ran away to Harmonia to become a performer. She gives the characters an Uncommon [Instrument of the Bards](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/instrument-of-the-bards-xdmg.md) and will allow them to keep it if they return Frantosh home safely. Along the way to Harmonia, the characters are plagued by [Wolves](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/beast/wolf-xmm.md) and people-eating Goblins.  
- **Levels 3–6.** In Harmonia, the characters find Frantosh has begun performing with a skilled bard named [Harkon Lukas](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/harkon-lukas-rhw.md). Harkon encourages the characters to help Frantosh follow his dreams. To help Frantosh, Harkon asks the characters to fetch voice-enchanting waters from a mystical silver spring near Argent Falls Conservatory. The spring is guarded by dead performers risen as [Banshees](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/banshee-xmm.md) and a covetous [Young Copper Dragon](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/dragon/young-copper-dragon-xmm.md).  
- **Levels 7–8.** On returning to Harmonia, the characters find Frantosh went to Skald with Harkon. There, Frantosh is performing nightly with Harkon at the Old Kartakan Inn and Taverna. Frantosh—now wearing a wolf-tooth necklace Harkon gave him—refuses to leave with the characters until after his first solo performance. The "Hungry for More" adventure below details this performance. After this Harkon might resent the characters or start obsessing over one of them.  

#### Hungry for More

*Adventure for Level 7 Characters*

- **Situation.** The singer Frantosh has fallen under the sway of Harkon Lukas. He refuses to return to his family until after he performs at the Old Kartakan Inn and Taverna on the night of the full moon.  
- **Hook.** Frantosh's mother, Maria, offers the party an Uncommon [Instrument of the Bards](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/instrument-of-the-bards-xdmg.md) if they return her son.  

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.22: Old Kartakan Inn and Taverna](file://book/RHW/128-map-12-02.old-kartakan-inn-and-taverna.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/129-map-12-02.old-kartakan-inn-and-taverna-player.webp#gallery)

##### Encounters

This adventure uses map 2.22 and includes these encounters.

###### Frantosh's Debut

Frantosh (Medium [Performer](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/performer-xmm.md)) is performing on his own for the first time tonight. If the characters seek him out and mention his mother, he agrees to leave with them after his performance—it ends around midnight. If the characters try to abduct Frantosh, three [Tough Bosses](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/tough-boss-xmm.md) (or more) in Harkon Lukas's service intervene.

###### Full-Moon

Mention that the performance is on first night of the full moon only if a character asks.

###### The Old Kartakan

The taverna is a popular spot in Skald. Crowds of [Commoners](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/commoner-xmm.md) fill the first floor of the Old Kartakan. [Harkon Lukas](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/harkon-lukas-rhw.md) (detailed earlier in this section) is here, but he avoids combat unless otherwise mentioned.

###### The Show

During his 1-hour performance, Frantosh makes a DC 15 Charisma ([Performance](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Performance)) check every 15 minutes. Characters can aid him with the [Help](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/actions.md#Help) action or in other ways. Track how many of these checks Frantosh succeeds on. During the performance, these events occur:

- **Heckler.** A drunk **Commoner** heckles Frantosh. If he's not silenced within 3 rounds, Frantosh has [Disadvantage](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/disadvantage-xphb.md) on his next ability check.  
- **Brawl.** A fight breaks out between three [Bandits](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/bandit-xmm.md). After the first round of combat, a **Bandit** with bad aim targets Frantosh with its Light Crossbow action each round. If Frantosh is struck, he automatically fails his next ability check.  
- **Howl.** A wolf howls outside, distracting the audience. The characters have 1 round to direct attention back to Frantosh, perhaps with flashy magic or by making a DC 18 Charisma ([Performance](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Performance)) check. If they don't, Frantosh has [Disadvantage](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/disadvantage-xphb.md) on his next ability check.  

###### After the Show

After the show, the characters see Frantosh vanish through a secret door. The next events take place in the inn's hidden areas.

If Frantosh succeeded on three or more checks during the show, Harkon Lukas seeks to keep Frantosh. He won't fight the characters, but he uses the necklace Frantosh wears to transform the singer into a [Werewolf](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/werewolf-xmm.md). Frantosh and four more **Werewolf** servants of Harkon assault the characters.

If Frantosh didn't succeed on three or more checks during the show, Harkon has grown bored with Frantosh. The characters find Frantosh [Bloodied](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/conditions.md#Bloodied) and being attacked by four **Werewolves**.

###### Conclusion

If the characters escape the Old Kartakan with Frantosh (potentially now a **Werewolf**), each earns a bonus 1,700 XP. Even if forced into battle, Harkon Lukas won't kill the characters—they've intrigued the Darklord, and he might appear to toy with them later.

## Lamordia

*Domain of Snow and Stitched Flesh*

> [!note] 
> 
> - **Darklord.** Viktra Mordenheim  
> - **Adventure Genres.** Body horror and gothic horror  
> - **Hallmarks.** Amoral science, bizarre constructs, frigid wilderness, mutagenic radiation  
> - **Mist Talismans.** Animated digits, glowing minerals, preserved humanoid limb  
> - **Aligned Tarokka Card.** Transmuter  
> - **Opposed Tarokka Card.** Marionette  
^1f4

> [!gallery]
> ![](file://book/RHW/130-13-001.transmuter-tarokka.webp#gallery)
> ![](file://book/RHW/131-13-002.marionette-tarokka.webp#gallery)

A domain of amoral science, Lamordia shudders amid the icy environment and terror of its residents' creations. Revolutions of steam and steel spur Lamordia's people into frenzies of amoral invention. From industrialized communities and the iron walls of Ludendorf, the domain's largest city, flow streams of scrap and chemical poisons that taint the land and transform creatures into horrors. Yet, the domain's reckless scientists don't pursue just mechanized inventions—the greatest goal is reinvention of life itself, transmuting people into ideals and unlocking generations of potential. In the name of such ambitions, the depraved reshape life and unleash abominations. And no aspirations have unleashed greater evils than those of the domain's Darklord, [Dr. Viktra Mordenheim](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/viktra-mordenheim-rhw.md).

### Domain Features

Lamordia is known for the following features:

- **Frigid Environs.** Lamordia is a frigid land of bleak mountains, frozen swaps, and icy seas. Few voluntarily trek into its wilderness, fearing freak blizzards and starving beasts.  
- **Mutated Creatures.** Creatures warped by alchemy roam Lamordia. The most infamous are the monstrous "whales" of the Sea of Secrets—violent, unnatural leviathans, no two of which are alike.  
- **Rational Culture.** The people of Lamordia are direct and skeptical of superstition. They revere scientific innovation—as it's all that stands between them and a life of frigid starvation. Magic is acknowledged but widely considered backward.  
- **Steam Technology.** Steam power driven by boiling sewers fuels clockwork inventions and massive cranes in the city of Ludendorf.  

### Locations in Lamordia

Lamordia is a frigid land. In the north, the Sea of Secrets is choked with ice, while the mountains known as the Sleeping Beast are never without snow. The cities of Ludendorf and Neufurchtenburg are detailed below, and other notable locations are summarized on the "Lamordia Locations table".

#### Ludendorf

The city of Ludendorf is a morass of steam-powered factories operating at the behest of morally bankrupt barons. Boiling sewers and steam tunnels thread the city's foundations, heating cramped tenements and powering cranes serving the city's fleet of ironclad ships. These ice-breaking, whaling vessels dare the Sea of Secrets to bring back massive beasts that provide vital food and fuel for the city.

At the city's heart, the unscrupulous Ludendorf University conducts risky investigations into such fields as alchemical combustion, automated ingenuity, chemical sentience, and speculative anatomy. The university continually needs new subjects for experiments and hires volunteers or pays individuals for "flesh rights"—ownership of their cadavers once they die. A secret society within Ludendorf University idolizes Viktra and follows the reckless paths laid by her work.

#### Neufurchtenburg

The smoking refineries of Neufurchtenburg process minerals harvested from the Sleeping Beast. These rare, little-understood elements are then shipped to Ludendorf's factories. Radiation-warped monsters from the nearby bogs frequently attack, disrupting operations, but the town's people use hulking clockwork machines, cutting-edge firearms, and destructive alchemy to fend off incursions.

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.23: Lamordia](file://book/RHW/132-map-13-01.lamordia.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/133-map-13-01.lamordia-player.webp#gallery)

![Lamordia Locations](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/lamordia-locations-rhw.md)

### Viktra Mordenheim

*Darklord Who Pursues Perfection*

![](file://book/RHW/134-13-003.viktra-mordenheim.webp#center)

> [!quote] A quote from Viktra Mordenheim  
> 
> Ah. You're conscious. Good. Test your limbs, and get accustomed to your new body.

From her laboratory at Schloss Mordenheim, Dr. Viktra Mordenheim uses her scientific genius to create horrors and wonders. All manner of undead and constructs march from her laboratory, but such flawed creations don't satisfy Mordenheim. Rather, she seeks to re-create or reclaim her greatest creation, the Unbreakable Heart, a miraculous device that grants life to Mordenheim's elusive reanimated victim, Elise.

> [!embed-monster]- Viktra Mordenheim
> ![Viktra Mordenheim](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/viktra-mordenheim-rhw.md#^statblock)

#### Viktra's Tale

From an early age, Viktra Mordenheim sought to understand the complexities of anatomy. She pursued medicine not to aid patients but to reveal the secrets of life. Eventually, her research bent toward reanimating dead flesh and improving humanoid bodies. When Viktra began employing thieves to procure specimens for her tests, she met Elise, a beautiful resurrectionist whose spontaneity entranced the methodical surgeon. Viktra was smitten, and with Elise she discovered there might be more to life than chemical reactions.

When Elise started exhibiting signs of an incurable disease, Viktra hastened her experiments. On the doctor's operating table, victims were killed, returned to life, and died again as Viktra sought a breakthrough. When finally Elise passed away, Viktra refused to accept failure. The doctor worked feverishly crafting her masterpiece, an artificial organ she called the Unbreakable Heart. But as she fitted the device into Elise's corpse, constables burst into the lab and accused the doctor of numerous murders. As Viktra struggled against arrest, smoking chemicals, arcing electricity, and a strange mist filled the laboratory.

When the chaos cleared, Viktra awoke in Lamordia, an unfamiliar land where her genius was celebrated. Elise and the Unbreakable Heart were nowhere to be found, but the doctor soon heard rumors of a wondrous and terrifying figure who wandered the icy realm and whose chest glowed as though her heart were the sun. Ever since, Viktra has continued her experiments, striving to re-create her successes but failing every time. Between disappointments she searches for whatever Elise has become—and with her, the miracle of the Unbreakable Heart.

#### Viktra's Domain

Lamordia is altered by Viktra's presence, creating the following effects:

- **Air of Obsession.** When a creature fails a Constitution saving throw to maintain [Concentration](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/conditions.md#Concentration), that creature takes `dice:1d6|noform|noparens|avg|text(3)` (`1d6`) Psychic damage.  
- **Closing the Borders.** While in her domain, Viktra can close or open the borders to Lamordia. While the borders are closed, lightning storms roll through the Mists surrounding Lamordia. A creature that enters the Mists for the first time on a turn or starts its turn there makes a DC 15 Dexterity saving throw, taking `dice:4d6|noform|noparens|avg` (`4d6`) Lightning damage on a failed save and half as much on a successful one. A creature makes this save only once per turn.  

If Viktra dies, these effects end immediately.

#### Viktra's Lair

Schloss Mordenheim is a castle that stands amid dramatic cliffs overlooking the sea. Travelers from Ludendorf reach Schloss Mordenheim by crossing the ice and following a treacherous road.

##### Schloss Mordenheim

Schloss Mordenheim holds dozens of rooms, but most are empty or have furnishings pushed aside to make room for scientific supplies. Prominent locations from this site are depicted on map 2.24 and have the following features:

- **Auxiliary Workshops.** Viktra's assistants toil in workshops where they craft tools and devices to the doctor's exacting specifications.  
- **Disused Chambers.** Rooms originally constructed for relaxation serve as storage rooms, act as extra laboratories, or sit eerily empty. A dining hall half filled with crates is set for a single diner, but it's rarely used.  
- **Gate and Entry.** A stone bridge crosses a chasm leading to the castle's keep. Stairs flanked by grim statuary lead to the keep's entrance.  
- **Laboratory Tower.** A heavily renovated turret holds Viktra's laboratory. Mechanisms allow the tower's roof to part and its operating table to rise 30 feet, exposing subjects to lightning during the island's frequent storms.  

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.24: Schloss Mordenheim–Laboratory Tower](file://book/RHW/135-map-13-03.schloss-mordenheim-laboratory-tower.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/136-map-13-03.schloss-mordenheim-laboratory-tower-player.webp#gallery)

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.24: Schloss Mordenheim–Gate and Entry](file://book/RHW/137-map-13-03.schloss-mordenheim-gate-and-entry.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/138-map-13-03.schloss-mordenheim-gate-and-entry-player.webp#gallery)

### Adventures in Lamordia

Lamordia provides a stage for adventures featuring amoral science and altered or resurrected beings. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

![Schloss Mordenheim hosts the laboratories and obscene experiments of Viktra Mordenheim](file://book/RHW/139-13-004.schloss-mordenheim.webp#center)

#### Horror in Lamordia

Adventures in Lamordia often include the following elements.

##### Elise von Brandthofen

Elise knows she died yet finds herself alive again. She is now a [Mordenheim's Monster](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/construct/mordenheims-monster-rhw.md) (see chapter 5), and her life is sustained by the Unbreakable Heart (see the following section). Elise is learning to accept her new life but avoids Lamordia's people, who label her as an outcast and a monster. She also knows that Viktra Mordenheim seeks to recover the Unbreakable Heart. The doctor's actions—as well as the mercenaries she sends to abduct Elise—have shattered the pair's bond. Now Elise hides at a secret sanctuary in the Isles of Agony called Hope's Heart. Here, she shelters other victims and creations of Viktra, showing them the esteem their creator denies them. Those in Elise's care have taken to calling themselves the Children (detailed below).

##### Mordenheim's Masterpiece

The Unbreakable Heart is a nonmagical scientific wonder. Despite being the creator of the Unbreakable Heart, Viktra can't re-create it and is obsessed with reclaiming it and rediscovering its secrets.

##### Unbreakable Heart

This heart-shaped, clockwork device installs itself, fastening into place if positioned where a creature's heart used to be. A creature that contains the device is affected as if by the [Raise Dead](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/raise-dead-xphb.md) spell. After this, the creature is immune to disease, ceases to age, and doesn't die of old age. The Unbreakable Heart glows, shedding [Bright Light](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/bright-light-xphb.md) in a 10-foot radius and [Dim Light](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/dim-light-xphb.md) for an additional 10 feet. While inside a creature, the device causes the creature to shed Dim Light in a 10-foot radius.

##### The Children

The Children are discarded creations of Dr. Viktra Mordenheim who have found shelter with Elise. Composed a few dozen Constructs and chemically animated Undead, the Children follow Elise's lead and seek to live peacefully away from those who would misunderstand and harm them.

The exception to this is Adam, a [Mordenheim's Monster](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/construct/mordenheims-monster-rhw.md) who recently joined the Children. Adam was created by Viktra to capture Elise, but Elise convinced him to join her instead. Unlike Elise, Adam was created from disparate parts and knows no previous life. Although Elise seeks to teach Adam humanity, he shows little respect for the lives of more fragile beings. Moreover, Adam is fascinated by Mordenheim's work and quietly seeks ways to create life that will serve him.

![A desperate crew of Ludendorf whalers runs afoul of Rahab, a fleshless leviathan that hunts the Sea of Secrets](file://book/RHW/140-13-005.sea-of-secrets.webp#center)

#### Lamordia Campaign Arc

Campaigns set in Lamordia often make the characters subjects or accomplices to Viktra's schemes. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–2.** A dean of Ludendorf University hires the characters to escort the coach of students traveling to an assistantship at Schloss Mordenheim. Along the way, they are plagued by mismatched [Homunculi](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/construct/homunculus-xmm.md) that sabotage their travels. These are members of the Children, seeking to stymie folk they take for Mordenheim's allies.  
- **Levels 3–6.** At Schloss Mordenheim, Viktra Mordenheim hires the character to recover her invention, the Unbreakable Heart. She explains it was stolen by a monster that dwells on the Isles of Agony. Viktra wishes the characters to bring back the heart and the monster. The characters face dangers in the wilds, but the quest culminates in the "Isles of Agony" adventure (see below).  

The conclusion of the campaign depends on whether the characters aid Viktra or Elise. When they return to Schloss Mordenheim, events might play out in the following ways:

- **Levels 7–9 (Aiding Viktra).** If the characters aid Dr. Mordenheim, the doctor seeks to remove the Unbreakable Heart from Elise or test it by reanimating a new being. This results in a dramatic operation where an enraged [Mordenheim's Monster](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/construct/mordenheims-monster-rhw.md) (see chapter 5) breaks free and rampages through the castle.  
- **Levels 7–9 (Aiding Elise).** If the characters aid Elise, the characters must free innocent victims of the doctor from the castle and prevent Dr. Mordenheim from animating new terrors by destroying her laboratory. Ultimately the characters must face [Viktra Mordenheim](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/viktra-mordenheim-rhw.md) (detailed earlier in this section) and two [Flesh Golems](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/construct/flesh-golem-xmm.md) made from the assistants the characters brought to the castle.  

The campaign might continue with the characters continuing to aid or being targeted by the Children.

#### Isles of Agony

*Adventure for Level 5 Characters*

- **Situation.** The characters must recover the Unbreakable Heart (detailed earlier in this section). They don't know it's inside the outcast Elise.  
- **Hook.** Viktra hires the characters to recover the Unbreakable Heart, which was stolen by a monster. They are offered 2,500 GP, plus a 1,000 GP bonus if they capture the monster.  

##### Encounters

The adventure begins when the characters reach the Isles of Agony and consists of these encounters.

###### Shipwreck

Soon after reaching the icy isles, the characters find six human survivors of a wrecked whaling ship. These sailors ([Pirates](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/pirate-xmm.md)) are led by Mate Herzogin, and their captain was carried off by a half-human, half-machine monster. The survivors seek help returning home but want to recover their captain's corpse (and their pay, which he carried).

###### The Monster

The monster the survivors fear is one of the Children, a [Flesh Golem](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/construct/flesh-golem-xmm.md) named Kartad. He's peaceful, but the survivors' captain, Hans Giesbrecht (Medium [Pirate Captain](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/pirate-captain-xmm.md)), attacked him on sight. Kartad knocked out Hans, panicked, picked him up, and fled to Hope's Heart.

###### Track of the Monster

Characters who succeed on a DC 12 Wisdom ([Survival](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Survival)) check find and can follow Kartad's tracks to Hope's Heart. If the characters fail, a survivor points out the path. Roll on or choose results from the following table for three encounters that happen on the way (rerolling duplicates).

`dice: [](3-chapter-2-domains-of-ravenloft.md#^1-encounter)`

| dice: 1d4 | Encounter |
|-----------|-----------|
| 1 | Six [Dire Wolves](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/beast/dire-wolf-xmm.md) pursue a [Homunculus](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/construct/homunculus-xmm.md). The homunculus flees as soon as possible. |
| 2 | `dice:1d8\|noform\|noparens\|avg` (`1d8`) [Zombies](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/zombie-xmm.md) animated by mechanical apparatuses stare into the sky. They are Constructs and don't react, even if harmed. |
| 3 | A [Primeval Owlbear](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/primeval-owlbear-xmm.md) made of mismatched parts forages for food; it is a Construct. It is [Indifferent](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/indifferent-attitude-xphb.md) to the characters. |
| 4 | A [Troll](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/giant/troll-xmm.md) hunts alongside a [Winter Wolf](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/winter-wolf-xmm.md). |
^1-encounter

###### Hope's Heart

Hope's Heart is a hidden canyon home to numerous harmless Constructs that is accessed via a passage in an abandoned cabin. When the characters approach, Elise appears on the cliffs 20 feet above and demands to know their business. Elise is a [Mordenheim's Monster](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/construct/mordenheims-monster-rhw.md) (see chapter 5). The Unbreakable Heart glows from her chest.

###### Fighting Elise

Elise attacks to prevent entry to the cabin and to defend herself. She avoids killing and won't pursue those who flee. If the characters attack, they'll likely have to make multiple attempts to wear down Elise or use trickery to defeat her.

###### Negotiating with Elise

Elise is [Indifferent](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/indifferent-attitude-xphb.md) to the characters or [Hostile](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/hostile-attitude-xphb.md) if they harmed any Constructs on the isle. She's wary of those who working for Viktra and can share the details described in "Viktra's Tale." If a character explains they're seeking the missing captain, she brings forth Hans and Kartad. Kartad has nursed Hans back to health; he apologizes and releases the bewildered captain.

###### The Crew

The six survivors arrive to see the characters speaking with Kartad. They overreact on seeing the "monster" and initiate combat. Kartad panics and defends himself. Hans has 10 Hit Points but is too weak to command his crew or fight.

###### Aftermath

If the characters fight alongside the crew, Kartad and Elise defend themselves but flee after 3 rounds or if anyone is killed. Elise leads her followers to hide elsewhere on the island. The sailors thank the characters and offer to help them rally aid in Ludendorf to return and hunt the monsters.

If the characters deescalate the conflict or defend Kartad, Elise's attitude toward them improves. She won't give them the Unbreakable Heart or return to Schloss Mordenheim. Rather, she tries to convince the characters to see Viktra for the villain she is. She entreats them to return to the castle, save captive members of the Children, and thwart the doctor, as detailed in "Lamordia Campaign Arc." In return, Elise offers a trove of 4,000 GP and an [Immovable Rod](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/immovable-rod-xdmg.md).

Characters who defeat or choose to aid Elise earn a bonus 1,100 XP.

## Mordent

*Domain of the Haunted*

> [!note] 
> 
> - **Darklord.** Wilfred Godefroy  
> - **Adventure Genre.** Ghost stories  
> - **Hallmarks.** Ancestral curses, haunted mansions, mist-shrouded moors, vengeful spirits  
> - **Mist Talismans.** Broken jewelry, death mask, faded love letter, family portrait  
> - **Aligned Tarokka Card.** Miser  
> - **Opposed Tarokka Card.** Horseman  
^210

> [!gallery]
> ![](file://book/RHW/141-14-001.miser-tarokka.webp#gallery)
> ![](file://book/RHW/142-14-002.horseman-tarokka.webp#gallery)

In Mordent, the dead don't rest. Here, farmers and fishers toil in scattered villages, cleaving to stoic, hardworking traditions. In the manors of landed, aristocratic families, the bearers of noble names view themselves as conservators of the land and of stifling reputations. Tradition, memory, and expectation haunt the lives of Mordent's people, and when they die, nothing changes.

Little known to the living, the dead in Mordent rise as spirits, and for most—knowing no other ways—their work continues. Abandoned estates hide spectral generations of frustrated nobles and their downtrodden servants. While some spirits drift idly or deteriorate to mere impressions of their past selves, others greedily cling to their former possessions and ambitions. Some pernicious spirits become infamous hauntings, while others—such as the domain's Darklord, the ghostly [Lord Wilfred Godefroy](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/wilfred-godefroy-rhw.md)—seek to dominate the living and dead.

### Domain Features

Mordent is known for the following features:

- **Lingering Spirits.** All manner of spectral undead and other hauntings lurk in Mordent. Ghost stories and rumors of haunted sites are common.  
- **Local Nobility.** Mordent is governed by town mayors and local lords. Few nobles remain, and some have only decrepit manors left to their names.  
- **Old Faiths.** People casually worship vague deities in Mordent, but evidence of forgotten druidic traditions lies scattered around the wilds.  
- **Spiritualism.** Attempting to communicate with the dead is a popular pursuit for investigators, bored nobles, and charlatans.  
- **Tradition and Shame.** The people of Mordent follow traditions that prioritize hard work, self-sufficiency, and avoiding public embarrassment. Locals overlook blatant strangeness so not to shame their neighbors, and every family has secrets.  

### Locations in Mordent

Mordent is a foggy land of forests, fields, and moors that endures frequent rainstorms. The land is dotted with tiny farming hamlets and the rotting homes of forgotten nobles.

The town of Mordentshire is detailed below, and other notable locations are summarized on the "Mordent Locations table".

#### Mordentshire

Mordentshire is the largest community in Mordent. Sturdy fisherfolk work the town docks and, after dusk, fill crowded tavern common rooms. Cold winds frequently blow in from Arden Bay. When they stop, they're replaced by a shroud of fog the locals call "the breath of the dead."

To the chagrin of the town's no-nonsense populace, Mordentshire is home to a small community of scholars and adventurers. Saulbridge Sanitarium provides a refuge for the ill while also welcoming researchers from other domains. Across town, an unassuming herbalist shop is run by [Rudolph van Richten](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/rudolph-van-richten-rhw.md) (see chapter 5), an investigator of all things monstrous and mysterious.

The lands around Mordentshire host two prominent estates. Heather House is the home of the Weathermay family, regional lords who count numerous heroes among their number. To the east stands Gryphon Manor, the notorious House on Gryphon Hill. The mansion has a history of violence, tragedy, and hauntings and is the home of the domain's Darklord, Lord Wilfred Godefroy.

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.25: Mordent](file://book/RHW/143-map-14-01.mordent.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/144-map-14-01.mordent-player.webp#gallery)

![Mordent Locations](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/mordent-locations-rhw.md)

### Wilfred Godefroy

*Darklord Tormented by Ghostly Undeath*

![](file://book/RHW/145-14-003.wilfred-godefory.webp#center)

> [!quote] A quote from Wilfred Godefroy  
> 
> Speak your piece, then hold your tongue. No fools are more insufferable than the living.

Lord Wilfred Godefroy rules the afterlife of all who die in Mordent. Arrogant, impatient, and vengeful, the Darklord seeks any opportunity to exert his control and reinforce his undying noble standing.

Lord Godefroy haunts the House on Gryphon Hill, along with countless other spirits. Wilfred can send mobs of obedient spirits to do his will anywhere in the domain. He uses his control over the dead to influence the living, threatening to harm his victims' dead loved ones if they don't obey his fickle commands.

A generation ago, the creators of the mist-piercing device called the Apparatus vanished from Mordent. Lord Godefroy has discovered the hidden machine, but, to his frustration, lacks a way to use it.

> [!embed-monster]- Wilfred Godefroy
> ![Wilfred Godefroy](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/wilfred-godefroy-rhw.md#^statblock)

#### Wilfred's Tale

In life, Lord Wilfred Godefroy was an unremarkable minor aristocrat. He inherited the estate of Gryphon Hill near Mordentshire centuries ago by murdering his father and framing it as an accident. During a bloody night years later, the entire Godefroy family—Wilfred; his wife, Estelle; and their daughter, Penelope—died violently. But instead of passing on to the afterlife, the Godefroys' souls lingered at Gryphon Hill. In death, Wilfred is haunted by the ghosts of his family, recent and the past generations, who blame him for their deaths and the family's disgrace.

A generation ago, a mysterious alchemist created a device in Mordent called the Apparatus.
