This magical machine had many fantastic powers, including the ability to open passages between the planes and separate a creature's good and evil natures into separate beings. The Apparatus drew multiple powerful beings to Mordent and eventually attracted the Mists themselves when the device malfunctioned, causing a deadly disaster. The Mists collected Mordent into the Domains of Dread, and the mysterious alchemist vanished. With the departure of mightier beings, Lord Godefroy remained as the land's most fearful villain. He inherited the mantle of Darklord of the new domain of Mordent.

Since then, Wilfred has claimed lordship of all who die in Mordent. He knows the location of the Apparatus and seeks to master its powers, but how to do so and the location of a vital piece of the machine—the Rod of Rastinon—both elude him. He seeks to blackmail anyone who might be able to reveal the device's secrets or find the missing rod. Wilfred forces Alice Weathermay, mayor of Mordentshire, to keep him appraised of useful visitors to the domain, by holding her dead husband, Daniel Foxgrove, hostage.

#### Wilfred's Domain

Mordent is altered by Lord Godefroy's presence, creating the following effects:

- **Closing the Borders.** While in his domain, Lord Godefroy can close or open the borders to Mordent. While the borders are closed, the groans and whispers of the dead fill the Mists surrounding Mordent. Creatures in the Mists have the [Deafened](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/conditions.md#Deafened) condition.  
- **Ears Everywhere.** While in his domain, Lord Godefroy can cast [Sending](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/sending-xphb.md), requiring no Material components and using Charisma as the spellcasting ability. When casting the spell in this way, Lord Godefroy can target any Undead creature in Mordent, in addition to the usual targets.  
- **Spectral Serfs.** A Humanoid that dies in Mordent rises 7 days later as a [Specter](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/specter-xmm.md) under Lord Godefroy's control, unless the Humanoid is restored to life.  

If Wilfred dies, these effects end immediately.

#### Wilfred's Lair

The House on Gryphon Hill lies just outside Mordentshire and is home to Lord Wilfred Godefroy. Hundreds of spirits remain bound to the house and the surrounding grounds, and all serve the lord of the house and struggle to stay in his good graces. Spirits that rebel are punished—either forced to face Wilfred's kennel of spectral hounds or dragged into the deepest recesses of the house, which even the eldest spirits fear.

##### House on Gryphon Hill

Cobwebs and dust coat the House on Gryphon Hill. Lurking spirits remain out of sight until trespassers pose a threat or Lord Godefroy orders them to attack. The house has the following features:

- **Basement.** Lord Godefroy orders ghostly teams to endlessly dig deeper and wider basements beneath the house. As if creating his own underworld, Wilfred imprisons spirits who displease him in the expanding haunted dungeons beneath the house. Somewhere amid these dungeons, a passage connects to the site where the Apparatus is hidden.  
- **Haunted Rooms.** Estelle and Penelope Godefroy haunt the house's attic, avoiding Wilfred and doing all they can to frustrate the Darklord and stymie his ambitions. The house's other spirits obey Estelle and Penelope unless their commands contradict an order from Wilfred.  
- **Withered Estate.** Wilfred's ghostly hounds patrol the house's grounds, while spectral groundskeepers tend to dead topiaries and hedges as if they still thrived.  

### Adventures in Mordent

Mordent is a realm of ghost stories (see chapter 4). Moldering manors, lonely moors, neglected graveyards, and similar gothic sites provide natural settings for encounters with spirits and the tragic dead. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

![Fog locally known as the breath of the dead obscures mysterious shapes on the streets of Mordentshire](file://book/RHW/146-14-004.breath-of-death.webp#center)

#### Horror in Mordent

Adventures in Mordent often include the following elements.

##### The Apparatus

Wilfred is obsessed with control over the dead and the living. He knows where the magical device known as the Apparatus is hidden but has limited understanding of how to use it. Nevertheless, he knows it is powerful and can produce devastating effects. He cares nothing for the machine's remarkable abilities and seeks to use it as a weapon to force all in Mordent to obey him.

To fulfill his goals, Wilfred seeks individuals with magical and alchemical insights, as well as rumors of the Apparatus's missing piece, the Rod of Rastinon. He might threaten or blackmail the living into aiding him. Should he suspect the Rod of Rastinon or other vital information lies beyond Mordent, he might send his agents to other domains.

The Apparatus can exchange souls, open passages through the Mists, and create more dangerous effects, but the magical device might have any properties an adventure demands.

##### Bastion of Heroes

Despite the horrors lurking in Mordent, the domain hosts several quiet, relatively peaceful communities. Characters from Mordent might have had relatively peaceful, mundane lives before mysteries or tragedies led them to adventure. The abandoned estates of Mordent also make fine places to use the rules for Haunted Bastions, detailed in chapter 3.

##### Ghosts of Mordent

Ghost stories often involve spirits that linger as the result of some tragedy or unfinished work. In Mordent, spirits linger and might request help from the living. Roll on or choose a result from the Mordent Hauntings table to inspire adventures featuring the lingering dead.

![Mordent Hauntings](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/mordent-hauntings-rhw.md)

Even though spirits are trapped in Mordent, many find secluded places where they reflect on nature, their lives, and eternity. Over generations, such spirits often become little more than vague shapes or disembodied voices or emotions before fading away entirely.

##### Van Richten's Herbalist Shop

[Rudolph van Richten](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/rudolph-van-richten-rhw.md) (see chapter 5) is the foremost scholar of monsters and strange occurrences in the Domains of Dread. He lives and works from the Mordentshire herbalist shop (see "map 2.27"). Beyond the storefront, Rudolph's studies and prepares methods of combating evils plaguing the Land of the Mists. Adventurers might find lore and tools to combat all manner of monsters here.

When absent from his shop, Rudolph leaves it in the care of his protégés, [Gennifer](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/gennifer-weathermay-foxgrove-rhw.md) and [Laurie Weathermay-Foxgrove](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/laurie-weathermay-foxgrove-rhw.md) (detailed in chapter 5) and Beatrice Polk, an elderly local gardener and accomplished detective.

#### Mordent Campaign Arc

Mordent campaigns often involve ghostly mysteries. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–2.** Caarey Gelthik, a local ne'er-do-well in Mordent, has become a [Ghast](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/ghast-xmm.md) and lurks beneath the town docks. By night, he robs graves to consume the bodies within. The characters take note when silent spirits—perhaps of allies—begin wandering town, each missing limbs, tongues, and other soft features. Only finding and defeating Gelthik causes the dismember spirits to depart.  
- **Levels 3–4.** Beatrice Polk, caretaker at the Mordentshire herbalist shop, hires the characters to end a haunting afflicting the shop. See the adventure "The Ghost Hunter's Haunting."  
- **Levels 5–10.** Alice Weathermay, mayor of Mordentshire, hires the characters to find a lost piece of local history: the Rod of Rastinon. She shares leads involving various strange sites, but the rod doesn't appear. Eventually, [Lord Godefroy](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/wilfred-godefroy-rhw.md)—who has been working through Alice Weathermay—grows impatient. He threatens the party's dead loved ones, insisting the characters find the rod swiftly and help him use the Apparatus (see "chapter 3").  

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.26: Mordentshire](file://book/RHW/147-map-14-02.mordentshire.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/148-map-14-02.mordentshire-player.webp#gallery)

#### The Ghost Hunter's Haunting

*Adventure for Level 3 Characters*

- **Situation.** An accident at Rudolph van Richten's herbalist shop broke a strange relic and unleashed a deadly feline spirit from another domain.  
- **Hook.** Beatrice Polk, the shop's caretaker, offers the characters 400 GP if they end the haunting.  

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.27: Van Richten's Herbalist Shop](file://book/RHW/149-map-14-03.van-richtens-herbalist-shop.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/150-map-14-03.van-richtens-herbalist-shop-player.webp#gallery)

##### Encounters

This adventure uses map 2.27 and consists of these encounters.

###### Beatrice Polk's Aid

Beyond her folksy politeness and dislike of curse words, Beatrice Polk takes her stewardship of the herbalist shop seriously but doesn't enter the shop during the haunting. She can provide the characters with a number of [Potions of Healing](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/potion-of-healing-xdmg.md) equal to the party's members. She scuttles plans that involve harming or stealing Rudolph's possessions.

###### Ghost Cat

A [Wraith](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/wraith-xmm.md) that appears as a black cat the size of a panther haunts the shop. Whenever the characters enter a room without monsters present, roll a die. If the number is odd, the cat is in the room. If the cat has more than half its Hit Points, it fights for a round, then flees to another room or floor; otherwise, it flees without attacking. If destroyed, the wraith reappears 24 hours later with full Hit Points. Its threat ends only if the ritual in the cellar is completed.

###### Laboratory

Two [Poltergeists](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/poltergeist-xmm.md) haunt this room.

###### Stairs

An unnatural wind blows against anyone who tries to ascend either stairway to the second floor. A character must succeed on a DC 16 Strength ([Athletics](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Athletics)) check to climb the stairs.

###### Dumbwaiter

A dumbwaiter connects the kitchen and the upstairs hall. It can hold one Medium or smaller creature. A creature outside the dumbwaiter can use an action to raise or lower the dumbwaiter and its contents.

###### Upstairs Hall

Broken on the floor is a strange relic: a mummied cat. Shelves nearby hold accounts of Rudolph's travels in a land called "Har'Akir".

###### Library

Rudolph's library is filled with occult texts. Any character who spends a minute investigating the library finds a copy of Van Richten's Guide to Ghosts. Those who spend at least 10 minutes reading this book and have seen both the relic in the upstairs hall and the ritual room in the cellar understand how to use the cellar room to exorcise the ghostly cat. Additionally, a character who succeeds on a DC 12 Intelligence ([Investigation](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Investigation)) check finds a [Spell Scroll](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/spell-scroll-level-1-xdmg.md) of [Protection from Evil and Good](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/protection-from-evil-and-good-xphb.md).

###### Guest Room

Standing facing a corner of this room is [Gennifer Weathermay-Foxgrove](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/gennifer-weathermay-foxgrove-rhw.md). She is possessed by a [Ghost](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/ghost-xmm.md), which holds her in a catatonic state. Gennifer is freed of her possession if she's affected by a spell like Protection from Evil and Good or if she's removed from the shop. The feline-featured wraith attacks the party if its possession ends or if Gennifer is moved from the room. If freed from the ghost's control, Gennifer is aware of the ghostly cat, as she accidentally broke the relic in the hall. She knows how to exorcise the spirit using the wards in the cellar.

###### Cellar

A room in the cellar is prepared for magic rituals. A character who succeeds on a DC 12 Intelligence ([Arcana](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Arcana)) check realizes this space is warded to contain or dispel spirits. If the characters place the relic from the upstairs hall within the space, the ghostly cat appears 1 minute later and fights until destroyed. If the cat is defeated here, the relic repairs itself and the haunting ends. Each character gains a bonus 400 XP for ending the haunting.

## Shadowlands

*Domain of Faded Glory and False Virtue*

> [!note] 
> 
> - **Darklord.** Ebonbane  
> - **Genre.** Gothic horror  
> - **Hallmarks.** Cursed magic items, doomed quests, falls from grace, knightly lineages, obsessive zeal  
> - **Mist Talismans.** Broken holy symbol, religious relic, symbol of the Circle  
> - **Aligned Tarokka Card.** Torturer  
> - **Opposed Tarokka Card.** Broken One  
^22c

> [!gallery]
> ![](file://book/RHW/151-15-001.torturer-tarokka.webp#gallery)
> ![](file://book/RHW/152-15-002.broken-one-tarokka.webp#gallery)

For the knights of the Shadowlands, the struggle with evil isn't a philosophical trial—it is an active war. East of the rugged Theospine Mountains spreads the peaceful realm of Nidala, where the virtuous knights of the Circle guard their lands against wickedness beyond and within. To the mountains' west lies the ruined land of Avonleigh, the birthplace of the knightly Circle; this realm fell to evil long ago and has become overgrown by the spirit-stalked Phantasmal Forest. Many knights of the Circle view themselves as inheritors of a legacy of shame. They aspire to the heroism of their storied ancestors and battle to absolve themselves of imagined failures. They throw themselves into crusades against foes, real and imagined, sacrificing their lives—and those of their people—for redemption and glory.

For all the Circle's good intentions, these knights are cursed. Monsters and villains they've defeated reappear in the Shadowlands seeking vengeance. Most infamously, deep in the Phantasmal Forest lingers the evil that caused Avonleigh's downfall: [Ebonbane](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ebonbane-rhw.md), Darklord of the Shadowlands and the sapient sword of the Circle's founder, Kateri Shadowborn.

### Domain Features

The Shadowlands is known for the following features:

- **Bastions on the Borderlands.** The Circle seeks to reclaim a foothold in Avonleigh in a region called the Borderlands. They often reward allies with Bastions here (see chapter 3 and the "Dungeon Master's Guide" for details on "Bastions").  
- **The Circle.** The knights of the Circle (described in chapter 3) make their home in this domain.  
- **Nidala's Ruler.** Elena Faith-hold rules Nidala. But this knight is rarely present in the land, as she leads deadly quests beyond the domain's borders (see "Faith-hold's Crusades").  

### Locations in the Shadowlands

The Shadowlands is a dualistic domain: Avonleigh remains an overtly haunted wilderness home to lurking evils, while Nidala touts itself as the virtuous opposite. But the land's harmony is artificial, its people forced to smile while trapped in the service of Elena Faith-hold and her sycophants. Accordingly, the domain's conflict isn't one of good versus evil, but rather of overt and covert evils.

The Phantasmal Forest is detailed below, and other notable locations are summarized on the "Shadowlands Locations table".

#### Phantasmal Forest

The Phantasmal Forest dominates the haunted land of Avonleigh, a shifting, surreal woodland cloaked by perpetual night. A dreamlike place controlled by *Ebonbane*, the forest changes constantly, and locations within drift like flotsam on a dark sea. The River Avalon and the King's Highway—an overgrown route of misaligned stones—enter the forest, but within the woods they circle endlessly and never leave. Only those descended from the Circle's founding members can navigate the Phantasmal Forest without becoming lost. All others wander at *Ebonbane*'s whim, becoming prey for the wolves, corrupted fey, cursed knights, or wicked souls that haunt the forest.

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.28: Shadowlands](file://book/RHW/153-map-15-01.shadowlands.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/154-map-15-01.shadowlands-player.webp#gallery)

![Shadowlands Locations](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/shadowlands-locations-rhw.md)

### Ebonbane

*Darklord of Endless Vengeance*

![](file://book/RHW/155-15-003.ebonbane.webp#center)

> [!quote] A quote from Ebonbane  
> 
> Questing knights? Champions of the realm? Look upon thy sterling souls. Tell me, heroes, by what fair deeds art thou known in this rotted world?

[Ebonbane](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/ebonbane-rhw.md) is an evil, sapient blade that seeks to annihilate the legacy of the Shadowlands' greatest hero and her allies. This includes all with the Shadowborn name and every member of the Circle.

*Ebonbane* is a magic weapon (see "Ebonbane as a Magic Item" later in this section), but within Shadowborn Manor, it becomes a creature that can move on its own (see the **Ebonbane** stat block). Beyond the manor, it doesn't use its stat block—it requires a wielder to work its evil in the world.

Many who attempt to attune to the weapon are slain outright by its evil. Those who do manage to wield *Ebonbane* must endure the Darklord's constant demands and risk becoming its pawn (see ""Sentient Magic Items"" in the "Dungeon Master's Guide"). If unattended outside Shadowborn Manor, *Ebonbane* eventually finds its way back there. No one can carry *Ebonbane* out of the Shadowlands. If someone tries, the sword vanishes and reappears in Shadowborn Manor.

*Ebonbane* has a flamboyant personality and a penchant for the dramatic and sadistic. It has no regard for life and delights in animating the corpses of foes, then destroying them in front of their allies. When it speaks, it uses language that mocks the elevated speech of knights.

> [!embed-monster]- Ebonbane
> ![Ebonbane](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ebonbane-rhw.md#^statblock)

#### Ebonbane's Tale

Kateri Shadowborn was a great hero who, alongside her order of valorous knights called the Circle, spent her life in service of good. Among her greatest deeds was leading an army against a nation whose king had been possessed by a fiend. She defeated the fiend, though doing so caused her magic sword to shatter.

After a life of great deeds, Kateri Shadowborn retired to live in peace with her family at Shadowborn Manor. But the hero had made many enemies. Thinking her vulnerable, wicked cultists recovered the pieces of Kateri's broken sword and conjured the lingering malice of the evils she had thwarted. These the cultists forged into a terrible weapon, *Ebonbane*—and they became its first victims.

Animated by hatred for Kateri and her allies, *Ebonbane* took control of its creators and became a curse on the world. For years it worked to destroy what Kateri had created, ruin what she loved, and slaughter those who aided her. Many times the evil sword's wielder was captured, but none ever suspected that the weapon itself was behind the grisly crimes.

Finally, in the hands of an unassuming monk, *Ebonbane* found its way to Shadowborn Manor, where grim news had isolated Kateri and worn her down. Aged but still a mighty knight, Kateri recognized *Ebonbane*'s threat, and a great battle ensued. During the clash, Kateri kept *Ebonbane*'s attention and ensured her family and friends escaped the manor. When only the hero and the wicked sword remained, Kateri summoned her remaining might into a blow to destroy *Ebonbane*. But the wicked sword proved too powerful. Kateri's blade shattered, and *Ebonbane* struck down the legendary knight. Exalting in its victory, the evil weapon possessed Kateri's body and pursued her fleeing family. But as it did so, it witnessed its quarry fading into the rising Mists.

When the Mists receded, *Ebonbane* found itself in a realm where the residents regarded the ancestors of Kateri Shadowborn and her fellow knights as heroes. Thrilled to continue its spree, *Ebonbane* sought to leave Shadowborn Manor, but it had no one to carry it beyond the grounds. Now, the evil blade seethes in frustration, waiting for a worthy bearer to carry it into the world so it might destroy all the good that came from Kateri's work.

#### Ebonbane as a Magic Item

*Ebonbane*'s magic weapon form is described below.

##### Ebonbane

Weapon (Longsword), Artifact (Requires Attunement)

The Darklord of the Domain of Dread known as the Shadowlands is *Ebonbane*, a sapient sword. [Ebonbane](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ebonbane-rhw.md) uses its monster stat block while in Shadowborn Manor.

###### Bound to the Shadowlands

When you enter a space outside of the Shadowlands, your Attunement immediately ends and Ebonbane teleports to somewhere in Shadowborn Manor.

###### Insatiable Rage

The sword demands destruction. If the sword hasn't slain a Celestial or a Humanoid for 3 days, you make a DC 17 Charisma saving throw at the next dawn. On a successful save, you take `dice:8d8|noform|noparens|avg` (`8d8`) Force damage. On a failed save, you are dominated by the sword, as if by the [Dominate Monster](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/dominate-monster-xphb.md) spell, and the sword demands the blood of a Celestial or a Humanoid. The spell effect ends when the sword's demand is met.

###### Magic Weapon

You gain a +3 bonus to attack rolls and damage rolls made with this magic weapon. When you hit a Celestial or a Humanoid with it, that attack also deals `dice:3d6|noform|noparens|avg` (`3d6`) Necrotic damage.

While you hold this weapon, you have [Advantage](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/advantage-xphb.md) on saving throws against spells and other magical effects.

###### Sentience

Ebonbane is a sentient Chaotic Evil weapon with an Intelligence of 17, a Wisdom of 14, and a Charisma of 19. It has hearing and [Truesight](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/senses.md#Truesight) out to 120 feet. The weapon speaks Common and can communicate with its wielder telepathically. While you are attuned to it, Ebonbane also understands every language you know.

###### Personality

Ebonbane was created to kill the paladin Kateri Shadowborn, and it still possesses a burning hatred for goodly knights. Ebonbane revels in seeing good defeated and hope vanquished. The sword bonds with any wielder that assists in its goals but always views it wielder as a lackey.

###### Destroying Ebonbane

The only way to destroy Ebonbane is to forge a weapon from the Four Keys and reduce Ebonbane to 0 Hit Points with it (see the **Ebonbane** stat block).

#### Ebonbane's Domain

The Shadowlands is altered by *Ebonbane*'s presence, creating the following effects:

- **Closing the Borders.** While in its domain, Ebonbane can close or open the borders of the Shadowlands at will. While the borders are closed, whirling blades of magic fly through the Mists surrounding the Shadowlands. A creature that enters the Mists for the first time on a turn or starts its turn there must succeed on a DC 15 Dexterity saving throw or take `dice:3d10|noform|noparens|avg` (`3d10`) Force damage. A creature makes this save only once per turn.  
- **Haunted Woods.** The forest within 1 mile of Ebonbane's lair is wreathed in a powerful illusion. Whenever a creature other than Ebonbane or the sword's allies finishes a Short or Long Rest in that area, it must succeed on a DC 15 Intelligence saving throw, or it is lost in the forest, always finding itself at the location it started in until it finishes a Short or Long Rest.  
- **Turning Weapons.** While in its lair, Ebonbane can transform nonmagical [Greatswords](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/greatsword-xphb.md) and [Longswords](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/longsword-xphb.md) within 1 mile of the lair into [Animated Flying Swords](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/construct/animated-flying-sword-xmm.md) by completing a 24-hour ritual.  

If *Ebonbane* is destroyed, these effects end immediately.

#### Ebonbane's Lair

*Ebonbane* remains imprisoned in Shadowborn Manor, a fortified estate hidden in the Phantasmal Forest. The grounds are strewn with the bodies of those who sought the legendary blade and failed.

##### Shadowborn Manor

Though abandoned, Shadowborn Manor remains in decent repair. The estate is depicted on "map 2.29" and has the following features:

- **Dungeon.** The Circle understood that some evils needed to be contained. A secret stairway in the east wing leads to a dungeon that has remained hidden from Ebonbane.  
- **Great Hall.** This hall hosts the round table where members of the Circle once met. Ebonbane poses the bodies of knights here to possess as it pleases.  
- **Lady's Chambers.** Kateri Shadowborn's armored corpse lies in the largest bedroom on the second floor. It is Ebonbane's favorite body to reanimate, and if destroyed, it reappears in this chamber.  

### Adventures in the Shadowlands

Adventures set in the Shadowlands feature individuals striving to prove their worth or superiority. Characters might be welcome to join the knights of the Circle, or perhaps they belong to families with heroic histories. Such ties could connect characters to the domain's history and future quests. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

![The remains of failed quests and fallen knights lie near Shadowborn Manor in the Phantasmal Forest](file://book/RHW/156-15-004.phantasmal-forest.webp#center)

#### Horror in the Shadowlands

Adventures in the Shadowlands often include the following elements.

##### Faith-hold's Crusades

Elena Faith-hold rules Nidala, crushing its people under the weight of her intolerance and need to maintain her virtuous reputation. While she doesn't lead the Circle, she is its most respected member.

Elena leads forays of knights into the Mists on lengthy quests to defeat wicked foes in mysterious lands. An invitation to join one of Elena's crusades is a great honor and a death sentence. Whenever Elena returns from the Mists, she always does so alone, claiming to be the sole survivor of a great victory.

Elena Faith-hold isn't a Darklord, but should someone ever destroy *Ebonbane*, she might ascend to that position.

##### Quest of the Four Keys

One can destroy *Ebonbane* permanently using the sword of Kateri Shadowborn. However, the Dark Powers shattered her sword and scattered its pieces. These fragments are known as the Four Keys—emblems of Kateri's valor and faith. Each embodies a different virtue and one of the four elements.

###### The Keys' Locations

The Four Keys might appear anywhere in the Shadowlands or other domains. The ghost of Kateri Shadowborn or lore hidden amid tragic sites might point toward the keys.

###### Using the Keys

Should the characters collect the Four Keys, they can reforge them into a weapon that—if used to reduce [Ebonbane](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ebonbane-rhw.md) to 0 Hit Points—negates its Darklord Restoration trait. It's up to you whether this ends the Darklord's threat or unleashes a greater evil bound within.

#### Shadowlands Campaign Arc

Campaigns in the Shadowlands often involve quests that reveal evils steeped in tragedies and abuses of power. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–4.** The characters aid members of the Circle in defeating a dangerous [Basilisk](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/basilisk-xmm.md) in Nidala. Impressed, the knights charge the characters with reclaiming a fort in the Borderlands from a wicked knight. The knight—a Circle member who died trying to recover Kateri Shadowborn's sword—is now a [Revenant](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/revenant-xmm.md). Once the knight is defeated, the Circle gives the characters its fort as a Bastion ("detailed" in the "Dungeon Master's Guide").  
- **Level 5–8.** In their Bastion, the characters find a piece of a broken sword. The spirit of Kateri Shadowborn appears to the most virtuous character and asks for their help freeing her spirit and defeating Ebonbane. She shares the details in the "Quest of the Four Keys" section. The characters begin a journey across the Shadowlands and beyond to recover the other three sword fragments.  
- **Levels 9–11.** Once the characters have the Four Keys, Kateri's spirit instructs them to travel to the Stone Circle in the Phantasmal Forest, where the sword can be magically reforged as a [Holy Avenger](3-Mechanics/CLI/items/holy-avenger-xdmg.md). With this weapon, the characters journey to Shadowborn Manor and face [Ebonbane](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ebonbane-rhw.md).  

#### The Shadowborn Sword

*Adventure for Level 10 Characters*

- **Situation.** A knight seeks to prove herself by finding a hero's lost sword.  
- **Hook.** The human knight Lucia Lambert (Medium, Lawful Good [Questing Knight](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/questing-knight-xmm.md)) invites the characters to join her mission to recover the lost sword of the hero Kateri Shadowborn. In return, she'll reward them with 4,000 GP—or double that amount in additions to the characters' Bastions.  

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.29: Shadowborn Manor](file://book/RHW/157-map-15-02.shadowborn-manor.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/158-map-15-02.shadowborn-manor-player.webp#gallery)

##### Encounters

The adventure starts at the edge of the Phantasmal Forest and consists of these encounters.

###### Phantasmal Forest

The journey to Shadowborn Manor is 18 miles, with the forest's density and perpetual [Darkness](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/darkness-xphb.md) limiting characters to a "Slow pace". As Lucia's family members have belonged to the Circle since its founding, she can navigate the forest at a Normal pace, so the journey takes only 8 hours.

###### Fallen Knight

Outside the manor, a [Death Knight Aspirant](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/death-knight-aspirant-xmm.md) wearing the armor of a Circle knight bars the path and warns characters not to enter. A Good character who succeeds on a DC 16 Charisma ([Persuasion](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Persuasion)) check can convince the corpse to let them pass; otherwise, it attacks those who try to enter.

###### Shadowborn Manor

Armored corpses lie about Shadowborn Manor (use map 2.29). If the characters disturb them or enter the great hall, five rise as [Strahd Skeletons](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/strahd-skeleton-rhw.md) (see chapter 5).

###### Shadowborn's Ghost

The Lawful Good [Ghost](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/ghost-xmm.md) of Kateri Shadowborn haunts the manor. If the characters seem near defeat, she appears and can distract Ebonbane or lead them to the hidden dungeon.

###### Ebonbane

[Ebonbane](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/ebonbane-rhw.md) (see earlier in this chapter) lies in the great hall. If with the characters, Lucia claims the sword and is stricken dead by Ebonbane, who animates her body. Otherwise, Ebonbane animates another corpse. The Darklord tries to convince the characters to take it from the manor so it can slay their foes. If they reject it, Ebonbane fights.

###### Conclusion

Should the characters escape Shadowborn Manor, each of them earns a bonus 3,100 XP. If they don't take Ebonbane, Kateri's ghost appears to them the following night and explains that Ebonbane's evil isn't ended. She goes explains the Darklord's history and how to destroy it (see "Quest of the Four Keys"). The Circle rewards the characters in Lucia's stead if she is slain.

## Sithicus

*Domain of the Soul's Shadow*

> [!note] 
> 
> - **Darklord.** Lord Loren Soth  
> - **Genre.** Dark fantasy  
> - **Hallmarks.** Cataclysmic fire, malicious shadows, tormented memories, twisted fantasy  
> - **Mist Talismans.** Black rose, burnt armor, scrap of black fabric, three thorns  
> - **Aligned Tarokka Card.** Paladin  
> - **Opposed Tarokka Card.** Innocent  
^24d

> [!gallery]
> ![](file://book/RHW/159-16-001.paladin-tarokka.webp#gallery)
> ![](file://book/RHW/160-16-002.innocent-tarokka.webp#gallery)

Whatever Sithicus was or could have been, it will never be. The dramatic ruins of a fabulous elven realm cover a land realm forested by gigantic trees and burning with the flames of a forgotten magical disaster. Scattered communities appear among the dilapidation, the domain's predominantly elf population living like strangers amid structures to which they have no connection. At dusk, people withdraw, hiding from the domain's true residents: the shadows.

By night, the shadows of Sithicus reenact forgotten lives or mimic the deeds of questing knights, devoted lovers, and lurking monsters. Most of these shadows are harmless, if unnerving, and seem not to notice other beings. Some, however, resent the domain's other residents and torment the living.

Though few in the domain realize it, Sithicus has ties to the world of Krynn on the Material Plane. Ruins suggest the work of elves from that world, while the night sky blazes with the five-headed dragon constellation of the deity Takhisis. As on Krynn, the black moon Nuitari is visible only to evil beings. But the domain's clearest tie to Krynn is its Darklord, the accursed knight [Lord Soth](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/lord-soth-of-sithicus-rhw.md).

### Domain Features

Sithicus is known for the following features:

- **Bound to Krynn.** Sithicus is a warped reflection of the lands of Krynn. This world and its people, such as [kender](3-Mechanics/CLI/races/kender-dsotdq.md), are described in Dragonlance: Shadow of the Dragon Queen.  
- **Cataclysmic Fire.** Accursed flames blaze amid prominent ruins and turn shadows into monsters drawn from Lord Soth's past.  
- **Living Shadows.** Shadows in Sithicus move on their own. Most are harmless, but some are deadly creatures such a [Shadows](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/shadow-xmm.md) or [Shadow Demons](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fiend/shadow-demon-xmm.md).  
- **Soth's Traitor.** Lord Soth's undead soldiers hunt for the ghostly knight Caradoc, whom Soth blames for his imprisonment in Sithicus.  

### Locations in Sithicus

Two significant features of Sithicus are detailed below, and other notable locations are summarized on the "Sithicus Locations table".

#### Endless Ruins

Sithicus lies blanketed in endless ruins. Ancient forests rise from them, rivers flow in their broken avenues, and whole mountain ranges are sculpted with crumbled towers. These structures suggest the work of a vast, magical elven nation, but all evidence of these people has been reduced to enigmatic scraps of art and lore. At the heights of crumbling towers or in empty crypts blaze violet, cataclysmic fire (see "Cataclysmic Flames"). In rare cases, these phantasmal flames reveal glimpses of Lord Soth's past and details that the clever might use to win the Darklord's favor.

#### Great Chasm

The Great Chasm gapes in Sithicus like a wound. None can say how deep it goes, as light fails to pierce more than a few dozen feet into the ravine. Those who descend deeper vanish into the shadows and rarely return. Those who do tell of a malicious darkness beneath the domain, a cacophony of hateful voices, and shadows that hunger.

Hidden amid ruins spilling into the chasm is the home of Inza Kulchevich, a hateful witch who can speak to shadows and believes all virtue is a lie. Despite her cynicism, she might perform prophetic fortune-telling or share strange lore in return for her visitors' shadows.

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.30: Sithicus](file://book/RHW/161-map-16-01.sithicus.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/162-map-16-01.sithicus-player.webp#gallery)

![Sithicus Locations](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/sithicus-locations-rhw.md)

### Lord Soth

*Darklord Cursed by Memories*

![](file://book/RHW/163-16-003.lord-soth-of-sithicus.webp#center)

> [!quote] A quote from Lord Soth  
> 
> Explain why you have interrupted my reverie, or I will turn your waking hours into nightmares.

Lord Loren Soth seethes within a realm that mocks and frustrates him. Having known the rigid standards of knighthood and warfare, Soth finds Sithicus empty and chaotic, his people apathetic and undisciplined. The elven beauty that once captivated him lies ruined, the land burns with the flames of Krynn's Cataclysm, and the realm's shadows remind Soth of his past failures. Worse, no worthy foes exist to challenge him. So Soth broods on his throne in Nedragaard Keep, haunted by banshees that sing the tale of his disgrace and by rotted, undead copies of the knights who once served him.

Lord Soth cares nothing for his domain. But should noteworthy threats or remarkable individuals appear, he seeks to crush or enlist them. The only exception is the spirit of his treacherous former ally, Caradoc. Soth's undead servants and his werebadger seneschal, Azrael Dax, scour the land for the elusive ghost.

Soth shares his imprisonment in Sithicus with all in the domain by keeping its borders perpetually closed. Only those who rouse him to activity or invade Nedragaard Keep might convince him to let them escape. This risks provoking the mighty death knight's wrath, but Soth still thinks of himself as a true knight—he might assist those who present themselves as honorable warriors or show knowledge of his home (see "Influencing Lord Soth").

> [!embed-monster]- Lord Soth of Sithicus
> ![Lord Soth of Sithicus](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/lord-soth-of-sithicus-rhw.md#^statblock)

> [!note] Villain of Two Worlds
> 
> Lord Soth features in adventures in both the Dragonlance and Ravenloft campaign settings. If you want to give Soth a unique relationship to the Domains of Dread, consider these possibilities:
> 
> - The nature of Soth's curse creates aspects of the death knight in both Krynn and Sithicus. When Soth broods in his fortress in Krynn, he remains active in Sithicus. When the evil god, Takhisis, calls for his service on Krynn, Soth enters a magical torpor in his fortress in Sithicus.  
> - Soth traveled from Krynn to Sithicus and is destined to return. If he leaves Sithicus, the domain might be destroyed, or a villain like Inza Kulchevich might take over.  
> - Soth was trapped in Sithicus, escaped, and was trapped again, perpetuating a cycle of despair.  
> 
> Soth's story and where characters encounter him are for you to detail in your adventures.
^villain-of-two-worlds

#### Lord Soth's Tale

Lord Soth was given a quest to save the people of his world, Krynn, from the wrath of the gods. Possessed by baseless paranoia and possessiveness of his elf wife, Soth forsook that quest, and the world was devastated in a great Cataclysm. In punishment, Soth was resurrected as a death knight and, for centuries, brooded on his disgrace in the charred ruins of his fortress, Dargaard Keep.

When the evil god Takhisis whispered to Soth, promising to restore his glory and avenge him against the heroic knights who banished him long ago, Soth answered and served Takhisis. During this time, he called on his undead servants, including the ghost of the knight Caradoc. Seeking to forge a new knighthood of loyal dead, Soth became obsessed with Dragon Highlord Kitiara Uth Matar and charged Caradoc with claiming her soul. When Kitiara died in battle, Caradoc refused to capture her spirit unless Soth bargained with Takhisis to restore Caradoc to life. Enraged, Soth tried to destroy Caradoc as the Mists rose around them.

When the Mists faded, Soth found himself in the domain of "Barovia". For a time, he found an ally in [Count Strahd von Zarovich](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/strahd-von-zarovich-rhw.md), but the two villains couldn't abide one another for long. Soth eventually pursued rumors of his treacherous servant, Caradoc, into the Mists. When the Mists parted again, the domain of Sithicus spread before him.

#### Lord Soth's Domain

Sithicus is altered by Lord Soth's presence, creating the following effects:

- **Closing the Borders.** While in his domain, Lord Soth can close or open the borders to Sithicus. While the borders are closed, purple flames fill the Mists surrounding Sithicus. A creature that enters the Mists for the first time on a turn or starts its turn there takes `dice:1d10|noform|noparens|avg|text(5)` (`1d10`) Fire damage plus `dice:1d10|noform|noparens|avg|text(5)` (`1d10`) Necrotic damage.  
- **Fearless Soldiers.** Undead allies of Lord Soth have Immunity to the [Frightened](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/conditions.md#Frightened) condition.  
- **Guilt of Sithicus.** Few sleep soundly in Sithicus. Whenever a creature other than Lord Soth and his allies finishes a Long Rest in the domain, the creature must succeed on a DC 10 Constitution saving throw or gain 1 [Exhaustion](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/conditions.md#Exhaustion) level.  

If Lord Soth dies, these effects end immediately.

#### Lord Soth's Lair

![Nedragaard Keep](file://book/RHW/164-16-004.nedagaard-keep.webp#center)

Lord Soth rules from Nedragaard Keep, a twisted, copy of his accursed fortress on Krynn, Dargaard Keep. Nedragaard Keep grows and withers over time like a living thing. Undead soldiers patrolling the keep regularly forget their duties or collapse into lifelessness. The disorder within the rigid death knight's fortress endlessly frustrates Lord Soth.

##### Nedragaard Keep

Nedragaard Keep is a towerlike fortress of crumbling, flame-scarred stone. Prominent locations in the keep are depicted on "map 2.31" and have the following features:

- **Gatehouse.** Undead soldiers guard the gates to Nedragaard Keep, demanding to know trespassers' identities. Those who identify themselves with the proper passphrase, such as "a seeker of the rose" or "a servant of Nightlund's lord," are admitted. Stairs beyond the gate climb several floors to the top of the keep's walls.  
- **Garden.** Gardens on the keep's second floor are overgrown with thorny plants—use the rules for [razorvine](3-Mechanics/CLI/traps-hazards/razorvine-xdmg.md) from the "Dungeon Master's Guide". From here spread massive vines that bloom with black roses and strangle the entire castle.  
- **Throne Room.** High in the keep is Soth's throne room. Here Lord Soth spends much of his time dwelling on failures and twisted fantasies. Thirteen [Banshees](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/banshee-xmm.md) haunt the keep, and at any time, at least three linger here, singing of Soth's disgrace.  

### Adventures in Sithicus

Adventures set in Sithicus feature mysterious shadows, grim ruins, and strange foes from the warped memories of Lord Soth. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

#### Horror in Sithicus

Adventures in Sithicus often include the following elements.

##### Cataclysmic Flames

Illusory violet flames burn across Sithicus—fires from the Cataclysm that devastated Krynn. Powerful shadows guard prominent, bonfire-like pillars of these flames. These shadows might use the stat blocks of any monster, but they resemble dragons, knights, and figures from Soth's past.

Whenever someone defeats one of these guardians, the flame it protected reveals an illusory scene from the Darklord's past before vanishing. Any character who witnesses such a scene learns something of Soth's history, the world he comes from, or the knighthood he once belonged to. One of the viewers then gains the [Charm of the Black Rose](3-Mechanics/CLI/rewards/charm-of-the-black-rose-rhw.md) (see ""Supernatural Gifts"" in the "Dungeon Master's Guide" for additional details).

##### Influencing Lord Soth

Lord Soth is typically [Hostile](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/hostile-attitude-xphb.md) to strangers, but characters can adjust his attitude to [Indifferent](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/indifferent-attitude-xphb.md) by succeeding on a DC 20 Charisma ([Deception](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Deception) or [Persuasion](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Persuasion)) check. Soth might employ characters he deems worthy on quests, such as the hunt for the ghost Caradoc. Making a second successful DC 20 Charisma ([Deception](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Deception) or [Persuasion](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Persuasion)) check while offering Soth something he covets can improve Soth's attitude to [Friendly](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/friendly-attitude-xphb.md) for a short time, during which he might let others leave his domain.

##### Living Shadows

Shadows in Sithicus often act with a life of their own. Roll on or choose a result from the Shadows of Sithicus table to inspire these shapes' behavior.

![Shadows of Sithicus](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/shadows-of-sithicus-rhw.md)

##### Sithicus Campaign Arc

Campaigns set in Sithicus often involve trying to gain Lord Soth's favor and win escape from the domain. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–4.** Azrael Dax, Lord Soth's werebadger seneschal, brusquely recruits the characters to hunt down deadly shadows. These shadows take the form of and behave as noble knights.  
- **Level 5–9.** Impressed by the characters, Azrael sends them to Inza Kulchevich to ask the witch to use her powers to find Lord Soth's elusive former servant, Caradoc. Inza can do this, but first she requires the characters to collect the cataclysmic flame from three ruins across the domain in a magical iron pendant. Each flame is guarded by a shadow creature that resembles some foe from Soth's twisted memories—like a lance-wielding [Warrior Commander](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/warrior-commander-xmm.md) or a pompous [Archpriest](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/archpriest-xmm.md).  
- **Levels 10–14.** Inza uses the pendant to reveal that Caradoc's soul is trapped in a black sapphire that Azrael already possesses. The characters must recover the gem. They might then infiltrate Nedragaard Keep to offer it to [Lord Soth](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/lord-soth-of-sithicus-rhw.md). Soth is fickle though, and this approach might end in a confrontation with the death knight.  

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.31: Nedragaard Keep](file://book/RHW/165-map-16-02.nedragaard-keep.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/166-map-16-02.nedragaard-keep-player.webp#gallery)

#### Shadow of the Black Rose

*Adventure for Level 14 Characters*

- **Situation.** The characters seek to escape Sithicus or the Domains of Dread.  
- **Hook.** Inza Kulchevich (Medium, Neutral Evil [Death Cultist](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/death-cultist-xmm.md)) offers to tell the characters how to escape Sithicus if they recover a magical gem from Lord Soth's seneschal, Azrael Dax.  

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.31: Sithicus Ruins](file://book/RHW/167-map-16-03.sithicus-ruins.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/168-map-16-03.sithicus-ruins-player.webp#gallery)

##### Encounters

The adventure consists of these encounters.

###### Inza's Quest

The witch Inza loathes Lord Soth. She knows he has tasked Azrael with recovering a magical gem that holds the spirit of the Darklord's treacherous former ally, the knight Caradoc. Inza gives the characters an iron pendant bearing an image of a rose that's missing its central gem. She asks them to follow Azrael to a ruin in the Misttop Mountains, where he hunts the missing gem, and recover it before him.

###### Inza's Secret

Inza doesn't share that she seeks to release Caradoc to provoke Soth into a conflict with the characters.

###### Searching the Ruins

The ruins where Azrael hunts for the gem appear on map 2.31. For every 10 minutes the characters are exploring, roll `dice:1d6|noform|noparens|avg` (`1d6`) on the table below for an encounter. For each previous encounter rolled on this table, add 1 to the result.

![Encounters in the Ruins](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/encounters-in-the-ruins-rhw.md)

###### Kender Nosferatu

A morbidly whimsical pair of [Vampire Nosferatu](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/vampire-nosferatu-rhw.md) pesters the characters, hoping to be entertained. If the characters don't keep them amused, the nosferatu attack. Because these monsters were kender in life—mischievous folk from the world of Krynn—they are Small.

###### Shadow Highlord

A dragon rider made of shadows guards a pillar of illusory violet flame. It reflects one of Lord Soth's warped memories and uses the stat blocks of a [Dullahan](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/dullahan-rhw.md) (see chapter 5) riding a [Young Blue Dragon](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/dragon/young-blue-dragon-xmm.md), followed by a withered [Death's Head](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/deaths-head-rhw.md). The monsters are [Hostile](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/hostile-attitude-xphb.md). If they're defeated, the nearby pillar of flames shows a scene of Lord Soth being knighted and grants a character the benefits noted in "Cataclysmic Flames." If you roll this encounter a second time, treat it as a meeting with Azrael Dax.

###### Azrael Dax

Azrael Dax is Lord Soth's dwarf seneschal and a murderous werebadger (use the [Werebear](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/werebear-xmm.md) stat block). Azrael and the six [Strahd Skeletons](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/strahd-skeleton-rhw.md) (see chapter 5) attending him are Hostile. If reduced to 50 Hit Points or fewer, Azrael bargains for his life and offers the characters the black sapphire they're looking for, which he's been hiding from Soth for moons. After this, don't roll for more encounters in the ruins.

###### Repairing the Pendant

Place the black gem in Inza's iron amulet releases Caradoc (Neutral Evil [Ghost](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/undead/ghost-xmm.md)). The arrogant creature is [Indifferent](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/indifferent-attitude-xphb.md) to the characters. If they don't free Caradoc, Inza does when the group returns the gem and pendant to her.

###### Soth Appears

Three rounds after Caradoc is freed, [Lord Soth of Sithicus](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/lord-soth-of-sithicus-rhw.md) (see earlier in this chapter) appears from the shadows. Soth fights Caradoc and mistakes the characters for the ghost's allies. A character might convince him otherwise—see "Influencing Lord Soth."

###### Escape

Characters who flee or defeat Lord Soth gain an additional 6,200 XP. Those who change the Darklord's attitude to [Friendly](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/friendly-attitude-xphb.md) or help him defeat Caradoc can convince him to let them leave Sithicus. Defeating Soth also causes the domain's borders to open. If the characters confront Inza about her method for leaving Sithicus, she cryptically explains that the only route to do so leads through Soth, encouraging them to seek the Darklord's aid or confront the death knight again.

## Tepest

*Domain of Nature's Cruel Secrets*

> [!note] 
> 
> - **Darklord.** Mother Lorinda  
> - **Adventure Genre.** Folk horror  
> - **Hallmarks.** Fey bargains, rural cults, secret sacrifices, sinister festivals  
> - **Mist Talismans.** Bloodstained farm implement, dried crown of white camellias, straw doll  
> - **Aligned Tarokka Card.** Druid  
> - **Opposed Tarokka Card.** Executioner  
^26b

> [!gallery]
> ![](file://book/RHW/169-17-001.druid-tarokka.webp#gallery)
> ![](file://book/RHW/170-17-002.executioner-tarokka.webp#gallery)

All is well in Tepest. Fields shimmer with bountiful harvests, and horned village children recite sing-song rhymes. But those who linger among this land's pastures and colorful cottages can't escape the feeling of being watched or the impression that strange forms move amid the fields. Locals dismiss such worries as the work of fey tricksters, but their smiles fail to mask the desperation in their eyes.

Brutality wears a welcoming face in Tepest, a truth embodied by the ancient hag Lorinda, who betrayed her coven in pursuit of adoration. Taking the guise of a deity called Mother, [Lorinda](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fey/mother-lorinda-rhw.md) adopted the village of Viktal, protecting its people from nature's whims so they can worship her even as they sacrifice themselves to feed her monstrous offspring. In the wilderness beyond, resentful fey watch and plot, offering cruel bargains to those who stray beyond Mother's sight. The people of Viktal do what they must to survive, using tradition to cloak their fear and complicity in a cycle of murder. Strangers become symbols of hope for Viktal's citizens—welcome alternatives to slaughtering their families in Mother's name.

### Domain Features

Tepest is known for the following features:

- **Children of the Fey.** Few children are born in Viktal. Would-be parents must bargain with Mother or the fey to bring them a child.  
- **Fey Threats.** Caves dot the land, connecting to depths where dangerous fey dwell. The people of Viktal fear them and blame them for every ill.  
- **The Last Village.** Viktal is the only community in Tepest. The others displeased Mother and suffered terrible fates.  
- **Mother.** Viktal's residents devoutly follow the optimistic faith of the nature deity called Mother.  
- **Mother's Minders.** Mother's most zealous faithful are called Mother's Minders. These devotees sacrifice their left eyes to Mother to show their faith.  
- **The Tithe.** Viktal's festivals include a fertility celebration called the Tithe that occurs once a season.  

### Locations in Tepest

The valley of Tepest is rocky, ill-suited to farming, and plagued by dangerous fey. Nevertheless, those who worship Mother are protected from the worst of the land's dangers. Mother's Sight and Viktal are detailed below, and other notable locations are summarized on the "Tepest Locations table".

#### Mother's Sight

A mile outside Viktal, in a field apart from the surrounding farms, stands Mother's Sight: an array of rune-etched standing stones. These stones rise as tall as thirty feet, and several have pieces that defy gravity. Within the central and largest stone floats a disk reminiscent of a great eye.

Here the people come to worship, celebrate, and sacrifice. Colorful crafts adorn long tables, where the villagers play games and feast in celebration of Mother's bounty. Meals here are tasty, and guests are encouraged to eat and drink beyond their fill.

During rituals here, Viktal's community leaders give thanks to Mother before a dramatic fire surrounded by an eight-foot scaffold. (See "The Tithe" adventure for additional details.)

#### Viktal

Mother ensures peace in Viktal. The village consists of a few dozen cottages, a market square, and an inn on the banks of Lake Kronov. Wicker scarecrows guard the rich fields blessed by Mother, and friendly people go about their daily lives. Cheery villagers welcome visitors, show them hospitality, and demonstrate interest in their stories.

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.32: Tepest](file://book/RHW/171-map-17-01.tepest.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/172-map-17-01.tepest-player.webp#gallery)

![Tepest Locations](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/tepest-locations-rhw.md)

### Mother Lorinda

*Darklord Who Demands Adoration*

![](file://book/RHW/173-17-003.mother-lorinda.webp#center)

> [!quote] A quote from Mother Lorinda  
> 
> What precocious moppets you are! Little ones who show Mother love get rewarded, but bad children get punished. Which sorts of tots are you?

Mother Lorinda desires a family over all else, not realizing she's destroyed every family she's ever had. A creator of monstrosities, this ancient green hag obsesses over unnatural maternalistic pursuits.

Over generations, Tepest's villagers have come to view Lorinda not as a powerful witch, but as a god of the land and fertility called Mother. Lorinda doesn't dissuade her fragile mortal followers from their baseless cult practices. The villagers provide willing sacrifices for the hag's flawed magical attempts to create life, and their adoration gradually soothes the violent, magical outbursts that follow her failures.

Lorinda's walking tower of bones, the Gurgyl, ranges across Tepest. Those who seek her here find a distracted but deceptively cunning hag clinging to grotesque dolls of her family. She laments the loss of her sisters, Laveeda and Leticia, never acknowledging that they remain alive as her prisoners. She often speaks of her daughter, Laoirse (pronounced "LUR-shuh")—the name she uses over and over again for each of her monstrous creations.

When Lorinda visits Viktal, she appears in her illusory guise as Mother, an ancient, powerful woman wearing a mothlike cloak and bearing a branch with burning limbs. She calls on the people to prove their love for her through sacrifice, whether of food and crafts, their left eyes, or their lives. Sometimes her arrival is sudden and terrifying, such as when she magically appears to crawl from one of her followers' empty eye sockets.

Lorinda seeks new ways to create a permanent family. This might involve great sacrifices, stolen fey magic, strange adoptions, or all manner of supernatural bargains.

> [!embed-monster]- Mother Lorinda
> ![Mother Lorinda](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fey/mother-lorinda-rhw.md#^statblock)

#### Mother Lorinda's Tale

The sisters Lorinda, Laveeda, and Leticia Mindefisk lived desperate lives at the wooded edge of a terrible land. Their brutish family claimed the girls were unnatural fey in disguise and forced them to toil constantly. After years of harsh treatment from their cruel father and brothers, the hopeless sisters snapped and killed an abusive traveler during a chance encounter. They butchered the body and served the remains to their unwitting family. Thus began a cycle of murder and cannibalism that persisted for years.

The Mindefisk sisters' crimes were finally revealed when they all fell in love with a charming stranger. They squabbled, and unwilling to relent or share, they murdered the stranger in full view of their horrified family. With nothing left to lose, the sisters killed the rest of their family as the Mists rose around them.

The horror of the Mindefisk sisters only grew in the Domains of Dread. Finding themselves in Tepest, the sisters discovered their new nature as hags. Over generations, mortals and fey alike came to know them as fickle miracle workers. Despairing families came to them often, willing to trade much for [hexblood](3-Mechanics/CLI/races/hexblood-rhw.md) children born from the hags' magic.

Eventually, Lorinda grew fascinated by others' pursuit of family. She entreated her sisters to help her create a child, but Laveeda and Leticia refused, loathing the idea of any one of them having greater happiness than the others.

Defying her sisters, Lorinda assembled a monstrosity of animal parts and foul magic in secret. With her new daughter's help, the hag trapped her sisters inside their magic cauldron and stole their powers. Yet Lorinda's joy with her creation was short—the monster's magic quickly waned, and it rotted away. Ever since, Lorinda has sought to create a family of her own, producing countless monstrosities in experiments and approaching the villagers of Viktal in her guise as Mother. Over generations, this has given rise to the cult of the Mother in Viktal, but it has brought Lorinda no closer to attaining the lasting family connection she covets.

#### Mother Lorinda's Domain

Tepest is altered by Lorinda's presence, creating the following effects:

- **Closing the Borders.** While in her domain, Mother Lorinda can close or open the borders to Tepest at will. While the borders are closed, a violent storm fills the Mists surrounding Tepest. A creature that enters the Mists for the first time on a turn or starts its turn there must succeed on a DC 15 Strength saving throw or take `dice:2d8|noform|noparens|avg` (`2d8`) Lightning damage and be pushed up to 30 feet straight toward Tepest. A creature makes this save only once per turn.  
- **Mother's Watchers.** Creatures that have sacrificed an eye to Mother can take a [Magic](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/actions.md#Magic) action and pray to her. When they do so, Lorinda can perceive through the creature's senses as well as her own until the end of the creature's next turn. When perceiving through a creature's senses, Lorinda benefits from any special senses it has.  
- **Sun and Storms.** While in Tepest, Lorinda can cast [Control Weather](3-Mechanics/CLI/spells/control-weather-xphb.md), requiring no Material components and using the same spellcasting ability as Spellcasting. When casting the spell this way, Lorinda can control the weather within 5 miles of herself, regardless of whether she is inside or outside.  

If Lorinda dies, these effects end immediately.

#### Mother Lorinda's Lair

Ranging across the domain is Mother Lorinda's home, the Gurgyl. This towerlike structure of thorns, wicker, and giants' bones walks on three skeletal dragon legs.

##### The Gurgyl

The villagers of Viktal know the Gurgyl serves their god in some way, but sighting it portends bad luck. The site has the following features:

- **Kitchen-Laboratory.** The Darklord concocts foul creation magic in this central chamber.  
- **Nursery-Oubliette.** This room is home to whichever monster Lorinda calls her daughter, Laoirse.  
- **Old Cauldron.** Lorinda's hag sisters languish in this plugged, oversize pot.  

### Adventures in Tepest

Adventures set in Tepest feature rural cults, deceptive fey, and dread of nature's mysteries. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

![Celebrants parade from Viktal to Mother's Sight to honor their god on the day of the Tithe](file://book/RHW/174-17-004.parade-to-mothers-sight.webp#center)

#### Horror in Tepest

Adventures in Tepest often include the following elements.

##### Strangeness in Viktal

The locals seem welcoming and vigorous in their worship of the nature deity, Mother. The village leader, Wyan, guides them in their faith, assisted by elders called Mother's Minders—all of whom are missing their left eye.

Residents invite visitors to stay at the village's only inn, the Fisher's Rest, free of charge for as long as they please. They encourage new arrivals to linger and participate in their upcoming festival, called the Tithe (detailed later in this section).

##### Mother's Children

Multiple times a year, Lorinda goes through a cycle of trying to magically create a new child. She calls this monstrous being Laoirse and dotes on it for a time. She believes that sacrifices to Laoirse during the Tithe can extend her child's life, but inevitably, the monster's magic fades, and it becomes mud and bones once more. For weeks afterward, Lorinda remains inconsolable, and violent storms and strange disasters plague Tepest.

Lorinda's children take varied forms. To create such a monster, choose a stat block appropriate to challenge your characters, then consider how that creature might appear if it were made from different parts. For example, a [Minotaur of Baphomet](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/minotaur-of-baphomet-xmm.md) or [Werewolf](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/werewolf-xmm.md) might be a bipedal mixture of ram, stag, and wolf parts, while a [Shambling Mound](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/plant/shambling-mound-xmm.md) might be a person made of wicker. These descriptions should seem outlandish but reflective of the creature's traits and actions. And no matter how bizarre her children are, Lorinda loves them all the same.

#### Tepest Campaign Arc

Campaigns set in Tepest often involve Viktal's cult and the dangerous spirits of the wilds. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–2.** Characters find themselves welcomed in Viktal and encouraged to take part in the Tithe (see the adventure below). At the rite's conclusion, the villagers try to sacrifice one or more characters to one of Mother's children. The characters defeat the monster, earning the enmity of both the villagers and Mother Lorinda.  
- **Level 3–5.** Fey creatures or druids who have been victims of Lorinda aid the characters; they reveal that she is no god, but a powerful hag who wanders the land in a walking tower called the Gurgyl. They send the group on a quest to learn from a mystical site or elder forest spirit how to infiltrate the hag's lair.  
- **Levels 6–8.** After learning how to infiltrate the Gurgyl, the characters locate and break into Lorinda's lair, finding some of the hag's bizarre creations and her diminished, imprisoned sisters. When they emerge from the mobile fortress, they find themselves near Viktal, where [Lorinda](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/fey/mother-lorinda-rhw.md) confronts them, backed by her fanatical followers.  
- **Levels 9+.** If the group defeats Lorinda, the land spirals into chaos as fey from Mount Arak run wild. The characters might become involved in a power struggle between the good and evil fey of Arak. Lorinda's return might drive the fey back—but the Darklord will help only if someone becomes her new child.  

#### The Tithe

*Adventure for Level 2 Characters*

- **Situation.** The characters participate in a religious celebration, at the end of which they are poised to become sacrifices.  
- **Hook.** The human leader of Viktal, Wyan (Medium, Neutral Evil [Priest](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/priest-xmm.md)) invites the characters to participate in the Tithe, a rite honoring their god, Mother.  

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.33: Viktal](file://book/RHW/175-map-17-02.viktal.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/176-map-17-02.viktal-player.webp#gallery)

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.33: Mother's Sight](file://book/RHW/177-map-17-03.mothers-sight.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/178-map-17-03.mothers-sight-player.webp#gallery)

##### Encounters

This adventure begins the day of the Tithe, after [Friendly](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/friendly-attitude-xphb.md) villagers from Viktal ([Commoners](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/commoner-xmm.md)) lead the characters to Mother's Sight. It uses map 2.33 and consists of these encounters.

###### Tithe Competitions

Wyan directs the assemblage in a prayer to Mother, and the day of games begins. Characters each can play three games, participating in each selected game once. During each game, a character makes the ability check listed on the table below three times. Those who succeed on the check two or more times win the game; if they fail, a villager wins.

| Tithe Game | Check |
|------------|-------|
| Crooked Joust. Participants use stilts strapped to their arms and legs to topple one another. | Strength ([Athletics](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Athletics)) |
| Powrie Chase. Pursuers play tag in while wearing tattered red cloaks. | Dexterity ([Stealth](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Stealth)) |
| Lost Siblings. Blindfolded participants identify other players by touching their hair. | Intelligence ([Investigation](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Investigation)) |
| Gossamer Glutton. Whoever eats the most live moths wins. | Constitution |
| Never Naughty. Participants flatter elderly villagers, who decide who wins and who gets paddled. | Charisma ([Persuasion](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/skills.md#Persuasion)) |
^tithe-game-check

Characters who don't play a game might socialize and see some benign oddity extrapolated from the details presented earlier in this section.

###### Competition Winners

The day's games draw to a close at dusk. Wyan names a character who won two or more games as Mother's Favorite and crowns them with a garland of white camellias. If no character won this many games, a human villager named Lorelei (Medium [Commoner](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/humanoid/commoner-xmm.md)) wins the crown and invites them to sit with her at the head table during the feast.

###### Feast

Wyan begins the feast with another prayer as the Mother's Minders light a grand bonfire within a tall scaffold. During the feast, villagers encourage the characters eat and drink to excess. A character who does so must succeed on a DC 10 Constitution saving throw or gain the [Poisoned](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/conditions.md#Poisoned) condition for the next 6 hours.

###### The Sacrifice

At midnight, standing before the scaffold (see "map 2.33"), Wyan announces, "Now we prove our undying love for Mother and beg her for another season of bounty. Bring forth our sacrifice!" Mother's Favorite receives a bowl of food and tiny crafts and is instructed to take it to the bonfire.

If Lorelei is Mother's Favorite, she obeys and approaches the bonfire. If a character is Mother's Favorite, they choose whether to approach. Regardless, 2 rounds later, a biped with wolflike features and stag's horns (use the [Minotaur of Baphomet](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/minotaur-of-baphomet-xmm.md) stat block) emerges from the field nearest Mother's Favorite. This is one of Lorinda's monstrous children. It fights Mother's Favorite (and anyone else who damages it) to the death. During combat, the villagers raise their voices in a hymn but stay out of the conflict. Lorelei smiles and doesn't defend herself if attacked.

###### Conclusion

If the monster dies, Wyan and the villagers are horrified that the Tithe went wrong. They turn [Hostile](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/hostile-attitude-xphb.md), blaming the characters and demanding they leave. Mother Lorinda learns of this and seeks revenge.

If the monster wasn't killed, the villagers remain [Friendly](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/friendly-attitude-xphb.md), but their true nature becomes clear. Mother Lorinda also takes an interest in the characters, potentially seeking to adopt them as her new children.

Regardless of how the Tithe concludes, the characters gain 200 XP.

## Valachan

*Domain of the Hunter*

> [!note] 
> 
> - **Darklord.** Chakuna  
> - **Genres.** Gothic horror and slasher horror  
> - **Hallmarks.** Deadly predators, death traps, hostile wilderness, survival games  
> - **Mist Talismans.** Displacer beast skin, poisonous flower blossom, rusty foot trap  
> - **Aligned Tarokka Card.** Shepherd  
> - **Opposed Tarokka Card.** Darklord  
^282

> [!gallery]
> ![](file://book/RHW/179-18-001.shepherd-tarokka.webp#gallery)
> ![](file://book/RHW/180-18-002.darklord-tarokka.webp#gallery)

In the wild domain of Valachan, only the deadliest predators survive. Bestial hunters, carnivorous plants, and ravenous monsters stalk the dense rainforests, but the land's greatest threat is its Darklord: the devious, undying hunter [Chakuna](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/chakuna-rhw.md).

Chakuna stalks the jungle, testing herself against the domain's deadliest beasts. Yet little delights her more than discovering strangers to her realm—visitors who soon realize they've become the Darklord's newest quarry. Chakuna forces her victims to participate in the Trial of Hearts, a race through the wilderness to remote sanctuaries. Participants face deadly traps and all the dangers of the wilds, including Chakuna herself. Those who reach the goal at the end of the trial are permitted to leave Valachan. Those who don't reach it die, either due to the deadly wilderness or at the hands of Chakuna herself.

### Domain Features

Valachan is known for the following features:

- **Displacer Beast Packs.** Packs of [Displacer Beasts](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/displacer-beast-xmm.md) roam the jungle, led by Yana, a preternaturally large and cunning displacer beast that serves Chakuna.  
- **Natural Hunters.** Wild plants and creatures in Valachan usually seem hostile toward strangers. Most creatures here are carnivorous even if elsewhere they aren't.  
- **Trial of Hearts.** The deadly Trial of Hearts is a battle royale that starts on the night of the full moon. Chakuna chooses participants.  
- **Wilderness Domain.** Valachan is covered by a fantastically dangerous rainforest. Visitors face constant perils, but the domain's residents flourish.  

### Locations in Valachan

Valachan is lush and wild. Rare creatures and plants reign here, as do villages of people who understand and thrive in the rainforest. No roads pass through the land, but ships from other domains sometimes wreck on these shores. The settlement of Oselo and the Pantara Lodge are described below, and other notable locations are summarized on the "Valachan Locations table".

#### Oselo

The former home of Darklord Chakuna, Oselo is a prosperous village that welcomes visitors. When night falls, the residents change, shifting from people into panthers, ocelots, tigers, and other hunting cats. These shape-shifters hunt animals for food and do battle with other peoples only to defend their home. Most fear Chakuna and want no involvement with the Trial of Hearts, fearing the Darklord's wrath. However, in rare instances, Oselo's shape-shifters might be convinced to guide, hide, or otherwise aid participants in the Trial. This displeases Chakuna, but she respects the decisions of her people's elders. The villagers might adopt strangers deemed worthy, but outsiders first must prove themselves in an initiation ceremony focused on surviving unarmed in the forest for a week.

#### Pantara Lodge

The Pantara Lodge is a series of thatched structures strung together high in the forest canopy, suspended above the overgrown ruins of a burned castle. This is Chakuna's home. Its interconnected treehouses include a great hall, the Darklord's personal quarters, an armory, an infirmary, and several guest lodges. The Darklord's [Displacer Beast](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/monstrosity/displacer-beast-xmm.md) and [Panther](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/beast/panther-xmm.md) allies prowl the trees amid the lodge's structures and can enter them freely.

> [!gallery]
> ![Map 2.34: Valachan](file://book/RHW/181-map-18-01.valachan.webp#gallery)
> ![Player Version](file://book/RHW/182-map-18-01.valachan-player.webp#gallery)

![Valachan Locations](3-Mechanics/CLI/tables/valachan-locations-rhw.md)

### Chakuna

*Darklord Who Hunts to Survive*

![](file://book/RHW/183-18-003.chakuna.webp#center)

> [!quote] A quote from Chakuna  
> 
> You seem capable, but do you have the heart of a hunter?

Chakuna is Valachan's deadliest hunter, a youthful werepanther with the intensity and calm of a veteran executioner. Few can elude her cold cunning, deadly traps, and packs of feline allies.

Chakuna is no mere murderer. She hunts because she must to protect the people of Oselo from a more terrible fate. To that end, she prefers to target strangers in her land, forcing them to participate in the Trial of Hearts. She relishes the chance to hunt the proud and disrespectful, as well as the skilled and unpredictable. Chakuna knows no mercy, though, and even those she comes to respect eventually face her blade. She spares the people of Oselo alone, even as her peoples' fear of her grows.

> [!embed-monster]- Chakuna
> ![Chakuna](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/chakuna-rhw.md#^statblock)

#### Chakuna's Tale

For untold generations, Darklord Urik von Kharkov ruled Valachan from Castle Pantara and hunted the people of Valachan for sport. Yearly, the Darklord's hunts grew in carnage, with his favorite prey being the shape-shifters of Oselo. Von Kharkov viewed himself as the domain's greatest hunter, a title he confirmed every time he slaughtered one of Oselo's supernatural warriors.

Chakuna was a werepanther warrior of Oselo and, like most of her people, was a skillful hunter. Seeing that von Kharkov eventually would slay her entire village, she swore to save Oselo. Realizing it would take a monster to slay a monster, she left her people and sought the deepest secrets of her deadly homeland. When she returned, she volunteered to let von Kharkov hunt her. During the murderous game that followed, Chakuna burned Castle Pantara and took the former Darklord's head.

Valachan is no mundane land, though. A Domain of Dread demands a Darklord, and Valachan will be ruled only by its greatest hunter. Refusing to let von Kharkov return, Chakuna made a pact with the domain itself. Within the depths of the mazelike Yaguara Mountains, Chakuna ripped her own heart from her chest and consumed the heart of Urik von Kharkov. Doing so, she stole von Kharkov's powers. Yet to retain them, she must feed the land constantly with the blood of the hunted. If she doesn't, the plants and animals of Valachan grow murderous and howl for von Kharkov's return. So Chakuna continues a cycle of bloodshed, embracing the violence of her peoples' onetime oppressor to ensure her bitter domination of her vicious realm.

#### Chakuna's Domain

Valachan is altered by Chakuna's presence, creating the following effects.

- **Closing the Borders.** While in her domain, Chakuna can close or open the borders to Valachan at will. While the borders are closed, shadowy beasts skulk or soar amid the Mists surrounding Valachan. A creature that enters the Mists for the first time on a turn or starts its turn there takes `dice:1d10|noform|noparens|avg` (`1d10`) Piercing damage.  
- **Heightened Senses.** Beasts and Monstrosities have [Advantage](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/variant-rules/advantage-xphb.md) on Wisdom checks.  
- **Whispering Shadows.** Humanoids subtract `dice:1d8|noform|noparens|avg` (`1d8`) from any ability checks they make when they take the [Hide](3-Mechanics/CLI/rules/actions.md#Hide) action.  

If Chakuna dies, these effects end immediately.

#### Chakuna's Lair

Built above the overgrown ruins of von Kharkov's Castle Pantara, the Pantara Lodge is a maze of rope bridges, mighty boughs, and structures built among the branches of gigantic trees. Chakuna leaves those who die in the Trial of Hearts without demonstrating skill or honor dangling from the branches of her home.

##### Pantara Lodge

The Pantara Lodge rises 80 feet above the rainforest floor. The site is depicted on "map 2.35" and has the following features:

- **Chakuna's Chambers.** In her quarters, Chakuna studies lore from other realms, fruitlessly seeking ways to placate her domain without further bloodshed. Secret doors hidden here lead to her meditation chamber and a room where the undying head of Urik von Kharkov spits curses and plots his return.  
- **Great Hall and Banquet Room.** Chakuna welcomes guests in the lodge's great hall. Prior to the Trial of Hearts every moon, she hosts a lavish meal for her prey.  
- **Trophy Gallery.** The trophy gallery holds the skulls of deadly beasts, the weapons of those who failed to murder Chakuna, and the stuffed corpses of the Darklord's rivals—animals and people alike.  

### Adventures in Valachan

Adventures set in Valachan involve merciless wilderness, predatory animals, and deadly hunts. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

![Lethal traps and hidden snares threaten participants in the Trial of Hearts](file://book/RHW/184-18-005.pantara-lodge.webp#center)

#### Horror in Valachan

Adventures in Valachan often include the following elements.

##### Trial of Hearts Rules

Visitors to Valachan likely are forced to participate in the Trial of Hearts, a dangerous game where the domain's Darklord hunts them. On the night of the full moon, [Chakuna](3-Mechanics/CLI/bestiary/npc/chakuna-rhw.md) selects those she considers worthy to participate. At the Pantara Lodge, she shows her guests every courtesy, provides them with a map of the domain, and sets out these rules for the trial:

- Participants can divide into small groups or go it alone.  
- Once groups are established at the trial's start, alliances between contenders aren't permitted.  
- Participants must reach one of two shrines: either on Kiru Island or between the lakes called the Scars atop Anquara Plateau.  
- Participants can leave the Pantara Lodge at dawn. The following dusk, Chakuna pursues the contenders with hunting partners of her choice, attempting to slay any participants she encounters outside a shrine.  
- Only one person or group can occupy a shrine.  
- Participants can kill one another for any reason—particularly to take a shrine.
